style="padding-right:0.3em;">Area</th><td class="category">\n765.5&#160;ha (1,892 acres)</td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Istanbul</b> (<span class="nowrap"><small><a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">UK</a>: </small><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x8c/: secondary stress follows">\xcb\x8c</span><span title="/\xc9\xaa/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">\xc9\xaa</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span><span title="/\xc3\xa6/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">\xc3\xa6</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="/\xca\x8a/: &#39;u&#39; in &#39;push&#39;">\xca\x8a</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span></span>/</a></span></span>, <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/-<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="/u\xcb\x90/: &#39;oo&#39; in &#39;goose&#39;">u\xcb\x90</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span></span>/</a></span></span> or <span class="nowrap"><small><a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">US</a>: </small><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/-<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span><span title="/\xc9\x91\xcb\x90/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;father&#39;">\xc9\x91\xcb\x90</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span></span>-/</a></span></span> or <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="/\xc9\xaa/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">\xc9\xaa</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span><span title="/\xc9\x99n/: &#39;on&#39; in &#39;button&#39;">\xc9\x99n</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="/\xca\x8a/: &#39;u&#39; in &#39;push&#39;">\xca\x8a</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span></span>/</a></span></span>;<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>: <i lang="tr">\xc4\xb0stanbul</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Oghuz_languages" title="Help:IPA/Oghuz languages">[is\xcb\x88tanbu\xc9\xab]</a></span><small class="nowrap">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Istanbul_pronunciation.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fa/Istanbul_pronunciation.ogg" class="internal" title="Istanbul pronunciation.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small>), historically known as <b><a href="/wiki/Byzantium" title="Byzantium">Byzantium</a></b> and <b><a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a></b>, is the most populous city in <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> and the country\'s economic, cultural, and historic center. Istanbul is a transcontinental city in <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasia</a>, straddling the <a href="/wiki/Bosporus" title="Bosporus">Bosporus</a> <a href="/wiki/Strait" title="Strait">strait</a> (which separates <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>) between the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Marmara" title="Sea of Marmara">Sea of Marmara</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>. Its commercial and historical center lies on the <a href="/wiki/Continental_Europe" title="Continental Europe">European side</a> and about a third of its population lives on the <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Asian side</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-wctr281_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wctr281-11">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\nThe city is the administrative center of the Istanbul Metropolitan Municipality (<a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/conterminous" class="extiw" title="wikt:conterminous">coterminous</a> with <a href="/wiki/Istanbul_Province" title="Istanbul Province">Istanbul Province</a>), both hosting a population of around 15 million residents. <sup id="cite_ref-Population_of_Turkey_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Population_of_Turkey-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Istanbul is one of the <a href="/wiki/World%27s_largest_cities" class="mw-redirect" title="World&#39;s largest cities">world\'s most populous cities</a> and ranks as the world\'s 4th-<a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_proper_by_population" title="List of cities proper by population">largest city proper</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_European_cities_by_population" class="mw-redirect" title="List of European cities by population">largest European city</a>. Istanbul is viewed as a bridge between the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_world" title="Eastern world">East</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">West</a>.\n</p><p>Founded under the name of <i>Byzantion</i> (\xce\x92\xcf\x85\xce\xb6\xce\xac\xce\xbd\xcf\x84\xce\xb9\xce\xbf\xce\xbd) on the <a href="/wiki/Sarayburnu" title="Sarayburnu">Sarayburnu</a> promontory around 660 BCE, the city grew in size and influence, having become one of the most important cities in history. After its reestablishment as <i>Constantinople</i> in 330 CE, it served as an imperial capital for almost 16 centuries, during the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman</a>/<a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine</a> (330\xe2\x80\x931204 and 1261\xe2\x80\x931453), the <a href="/wiki/Latin_Empire" title="Latin Empire">Latin</a> (1204\xe2\x80\x931261), and the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> (1453\xe2\x80\x931922) <a href="/wiki/Empire" title="Empire">empires</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> It was instrumental in the advancement of <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> during Roman and Byzantine times, before the Ottomans <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Constantinople" title="Fall of Constantinople">conquered the city</a> in 1453 CE and transformed it into an Islamic stronghold and the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Caliphate" title="Ottoman Caliphate">Ottoman Caliphate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-maag1145_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-maag1145-13">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Istanbul\'s strategic position on the historic <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> rail networks to Europe and the Middle East, and the only sea route between the Black Sea and the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean</a> have produced a cosmopolitan populace. While <a href="/wiki/Ankara" title="Ankara">Ankara</a> was chosen instead as the new Turkish capital after the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_War_of_Independence" title="Turkish War of Independence">Turkish War of Independence</a>, the city has maintained its prominence in geopolitical and cultural affairs. The population of the city has increased tenfold since the 1950s, as migrants from across <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a> have moved in and city limits have expanded to accommodate them.<sup id="cite_ref-tu224_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tu224-15">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ecoc-popdem_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ecoc-popdem-16">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Arts, music, film, and cultural festivals were established towards the end of the 20th century and continue to be hosted by the city today. Infrastructure improvements have produced a complex transportation network in the city.\n</p><p>Approximately <span class="nowrap">12.56 million</span> foreign visitors arrived in Istanbul in 2015, five years after it was named a <a href="/wiki/European_Capital_of_Culture" title="European Capital of Culture">European Capital of Culture</a>, making the city the world\'s fifth most popular tourist destination.<sup id="cite_ref-Mastercard_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mastercard-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The city\'s biggest attraction is its historic center, partially listed as a UNESCO <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>, and its cultural and entertainment hub can be found across the city\'s natural harbor, the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horn" title="Golden Horn">Golden Horn</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Beyo%C4%9Flu" title="Beyo\xc4\x9flu">Beyo\xc4\x9flu</a> district. Considered a <a href="/wiki/Global_city" title="Global city">global city</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Istanbul has one of the fastest-growing metropolitan economies in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Berube_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Berube-19">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> It hosts the headquarters of many Turkish companies and media outlets and accounts for more than a quarter of the country\'s <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-oecd_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oecd-20">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Hoping to capitalize on its revitalization and rapid expansion, Istanbul has bid for the <a href="/wiki/Summer_Olympic_Games" title="Summer Olympic Games">Summer Olympics</a> five times in twenty years.<sup id="cite_ref-olympic.org_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-olympic.org-21">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#Media"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Media</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#Education"><span links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Toponymy">Toponymy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Istanbul&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Toponymy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Names_of_Istanbul" title="Names of Istanbul">Names of Istanbul</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rome-Capitole-StatueConstantin.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Rome-Capitole-StatueConstantin.jpg/170px-Rome-Capitole-StatueConstantin.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Rome-Capitole-StatueConstantin.jpg/255px-Rome-Capitole-StatueConstantin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Rome-Capitole-StatueConstantin.jpg/340px-Rome-Capitole-StatueConstantin.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rome-Capitole-StatueConstantin.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Constantine_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Constantine I">Constantine I</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The first known name of the city is <i><a href="/wiki/Byzantium" title="Byzantium">Byzantium</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>: <span lang="el">\xce\x92\xcf\x85\xce\xb6\xce\xac\xce\xbd\xcf\x84\xce\xb9\xce\xbf\xce\xbd</span>, <i>Byz\xc3\xa1ntion</i>), the name given to it at its foundation by <a href="/wiki/Megara" title="Megara">Megarean</a> colonists around 660 BCE.<sup id="cite_ref-roo177_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-roo177-22">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The name is thought to be derived from a personal name, <a href="/wiki/Byzas" title="Byzas">Byzas</a>. Ancient Greek tradition refers to a legendary king of that name as the leader of the Greek colonists. Modern scholars have also hypothesized that the name of Byzas was of local <a href="/wiki/Thracian" class="mw-redirect" title="Thracian">Thracian</a> or <a href="/wiki/Illyria" title="Illyria">Illyrian</a> origin and hence predated the Megarean settlement.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After <a href="/wiki/Constantine_the_Great" title="Constantine the Great">Constantine the Great</a> made it the new eastern capital of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> in 330 CE, the city became widely known as <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a>, which, as the Latinized form of "<span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">\xce\x9a\xcf\x89\xce\xbd\xcf\x83\xcf\x84\xce\xb1\xce\xbd\xcf\x84\xce\xb9\xce\xbd\xce\xbf\xcf\x8d\xcf\x80\xce\xbf\xce\xbb\xce\xb9\xcf\x82</span>" (<i>Konstantino\xc3\xbapolis</i>), means the "City of Constantine".<sup id="cite_ref-roo177_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-roo177-22">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> He also attempted to promote the name "Nova Roma" and its Greek version "<span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">\xce\x9d\xce\xad\xce\xb1 \xe1\xbf\xac\xcf\x8e\xce\xbc\xce\xb7</span>" <i>Nea Rom\xc4\x93</i> (<a href="/wiki/New_Rome" title="New Rome">New Rome</a>), but this did not enter widespread usage.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> <i>Constantinople</i> remained the most common name for the city in the West until the establishment of the Turkish Republic, and <i>Kostantiniyye</i> (<a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turkish_language" title="Ottoman Turkish language">Ottoman Turkish</a>: <span lang="ota" dir="rtl">\xd9\x82\xd8\xb3\xd8\xb7\xd9\x86\xd8\xb7\xd9\x8a\xd9\x86\xd9\x8a\xd9\x87</span>&#8206;) and <i>Be Makam-e Qonstantiniyyah al-Mahmiyyah</i> (meaning "the Protected Location of Constantinople") and <i>\xc4\xb0stanbul</i> were the names used alternatively by the Ottomans during their rule.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The use of <i>Constantinople</i> to refer to the city during the Ottoman period (from the mid-15th century) is now considered politically incorrect, even if not historically inaccurate, by Turks.<sup id="cite_ref-maag286_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-maag286-26">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By the 19th century, the city had acquired other names used by either foreigners or Turks. Europeans used <i>Constantinople</i> to refer to the whole of the city, but used the name <i><a href="/wiki/Stamboul" class="mw-redirect" title="Stamboul">Stamboul</a></i>\xe2\x80\x94as the Turks also did\xe2\x80\x94to describe the walled peninsula between the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horn" title="Golden Horn">Golden Horn</a> and the Sea of Marmara.<sup id="cite_ref-maag286_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-maag286-26">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> <i>Pera</i> (from the Greek word for "across") was used to describe the area between the Golden Horn and the Bosphorus, but Turks also used the name <i><a href="/wiki/Beyo%C4%9Flu" title="Beyo\xc4\x9flu">Beyo\xc4\x9flu</a></i> (today the official name for one of the city\'s <a href="/wiki/List_of_districts_of_Istanbul" title="List of districts of Istanbul">constituent districts</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> <i>Islambol</i> (meaning either "City of Islam" or "Full of Islam") was sometimes colloquially used to refer to the city, and was even engraved on some Ottoman coins,<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> but the belief that it was the precursor to the present name, <i>\xc4\xb0stanbul</i>, is belied by the fact that the latter existed well before the former and even predates the <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Constantinople" title="Fall of Constantinople">Ottoman conquest of the city</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-roo177_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-roo177-22">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The name <i>\xc4\xb0stanbul</i> (<small>Turkish pronunciation:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Oghuz_languages" title="Help:IPA/Oghuz languages">[is\xcb\x88tanbu\xc9\xab]</a></span><small class="nowrap">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Istanbul_pronunciation.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fa/Istanbul_pronunciation.ogg" class="internal" title="Istanbul pronunciation.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small>, colloquially <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Oghuz_languages" title="Help:IPA/Oghuz languages">[\xc9\xafs\xcb\x88tambu\xc9\xab]</a></span>) is commonly held to derive from the <a href="/wiki/Medieval_Greek" title="Medieval Greek">Medieval Greek</a> phrase <span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">"\xce\xb5\xe1\xbc\xb0\xcf\x82 \xcf\x84\xe1\xbd\xb4\xce\xbd <a href="/wiki/Polis" title="Polis">\xce\xa0\xcf\x8c\xce\xbb\xce\xb9\xce\xbd</a>"</span> (pronounced <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Greek" title="Help:IPA/Greek">[is tim \xcb\x88bolin]</a></span>), which means "to the city"<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> and is how Constantinople was referred to by the local Greeks. This reflected its status as the only major city in the vicinity. The importance of Constantinople in the Ottoman world was also reflected by its Ottoman name \'Der Saadet\' meaning the \'gate to Prosperity\' in Ottoman. An alternative view is that the name evolved directly from the name <i>Constantinople</i>, with the first and third syllables dropped.<sup id="cite_ref-roo177_22-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-roo177-22">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> A Turkish folk etymology traces the name to Islam bol "plenty of Islam"<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> because the city was called <i>Islambol</i> ("plenty of Islam") or <i>Islambul</i> ("find Islam") as the capital of the Islamic Ottoman Empire. It is first attested shortly after the conquest, and its invention was ascribed by some contemporary writers to Sultan <a href="/wiki/Mehmed_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Mehmed II">Mehmed II</a> himself.<sup id="cite_ref-IA_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IA-31">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Some Ottoman sources of the 17th century, such as <a href="/wiki/Evliya_%C3%87elebi" title="Evliya \xc3\x87elebi">Evliya \xc3\x87elebi</a>, describe it as the common Turkish name of the time; between the late 17th and late 18th centuries, it was also in official use. The first use of the word "Islambol" on coinage was in 1703 (1115 AH) during the reign of Sultan <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_III" title="Ahmed III">Ahmed III</a>. Nevertheless, the use of the name <i>Constantinople</i> remained common in English into the 20th century, <i>Istanbul</i> became common after Turkey adopted the Latin alphabet in 1928 and urged other countries to use the city\'s Turkish name.<sup id="cite_ref-Room_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Room-32">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gokturk_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gokturk-33">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In modern <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>, the name is written as <i>\xc4\xb0stanbul</i>, with a dotted \xc4\xb0, as the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_alphabet" title="Turkish alphabet">Turkish alphabet</a> distinguishes between a <a href="/wiki/Dotted_and_dotless_I" title="Dotted and dotless I">dotted and dotless I</a>. In English the stress is on the first or last syllable, but in Turkish it is on the second syllable (<i>tan</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>  A person from the city is an <i>\xc4\xb0stanbullu</i> (plural: <i>\xc4\xb0stanbullular</i>), although <i>Istanbulite</i> is used in English.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> \n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Istanbul&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Istanbul" title="History of Istanbul">History of Istanbul</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Istanbul_history" class="mw-redirect" title="Timeline of Istanbul history">Timeline of Istanbul history</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Second_Court_Topkapi_2007_80.JPG" class="image"><img alt="A stout cylindrical column in a courtyard in front of palatial arches of Islamic style" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Second_Court_Topkapi_2007_80.JPG/220px-Second_Court_Topkapi_2007_80.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Second_Court_Topkapi_2007_80.JPG/330px-Second_Court_Topkapi_2007_80.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Second_Court_Topkapi_2007_80.JPG/440px-Second_Court_Topkapi_2007_80.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Second_Court_Topkapi_2007_80.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Remains of a Byzantine column found at <a href="/wiki/Byzantium" title="Byzantium">Byzantium</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Acropolis" title="Acropolis">acropolis</a>, located today within the <a href="/wiki/Topkap%C4%B1_Palace" title="Topkap\xc4\xb1 Palace">Topkap\xc4\xb1 Palace</a> complex.</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> artifacts, uncovered by archeologists at the beginning of the 21st century, indicate that Istanbul\'s historic peninsula was settled as far back as the 6th millennium BCE.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> That early settlement, important in the spread of the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic_Revolution" title="Neolithic Revolution">Neolithic Revolution</a> from the Near East to Europe, lasted for almost a millennium before being inundated by rising water levels.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> The first human settlement on the Asian side, the Fikirtepe mound, is from the <a href="/wiki/Copper_Age" class="mw-redirect" title="Copper Age">Copper Age</a> period, with artifacts dating from 5500 to 3500 BCE,<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> On the European side, near the point of the peninsula (<a href="/wiki/Sarayburnu" title="Sarayburnu">Sarayburnu</a>), there was a Thracian settlement during the early 1st millennium BCE. Modern authors have linked it to the Thracian toponym <i>Lygos</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-janin_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-janin-42">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> mentioned by <a href="/wiki/Pliny_the_Elder" title="Pliny the Elder">Pliny the Elder</a> as an earlier name for the site of Byzantium.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The history of the city proper begins around 660 BCE,<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-byz-date_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-byz-date-50">&#91;c&#93;</a></sup> when Greek settlers from <a href="/wiki/Megara" title="Megara">Megara</a> established <a href="/wiki/Byzantium" title="Byzantium">Byzantium</a> on the European side of the Bosphorus. The settlers built an <a href="/wiki/Acropolis" title="Acropolis">acropolis</a> adjacent to the Golden Horn on the site of the early Thracian settlements, fueling the nascent city\'s economy.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The city experienced a brief period of <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Persian</a> rule at the turn of the 5th century BCE, but the Greeks recaptured it during the <a href="/wiki/Greco-Persian_Wars" title="Greco-Persian Wars">Greco-Persian Wars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Byzantium then continued as part of the <a href="/wiki/Delian_League" title="Delian League">Athenian League</a> and its successor, the <a href="/wiki/Second_Athenian_League" title="Second Athenian League">Second Athenian League</a>, before gaining independence in 355 BCE.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Long allied with the Romans, Byzantium officially became a part of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> in 73 CE.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Byzantium\'s decision to side with the <a href="/wiki/Roman_usurper" title="Roman usurper">Roman usurper</a> <a href="/wiki/Pescennius_Niger" title="Pescennius Niger">Pescennius Niger</a> against Emperor <a href="/wiki/Septimius_Severus" title="Septimius Severus">Septimius Severus</a> cost it dearly; by the time it surrendered at the end of 195 CE, two years of siege had left the city devastated.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Five years later, Severus began to rebuild Byzantium, and the city regained\xe2\x80\x94and, by some accounts, surpassed\xe2\x80\x94its previous prosperity.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rise_and_fall_of_Constantinople_and_the_Byzantine_Empire">Rise and fall of Constantinople and the Byzantine Empire</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Istanbul&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Rise and fall of Constantinople and the Byzantine Empire">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Constantinople_(1422)_by_Florentine_cartographer_Cristoforo_Buondelmonte.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A crudely drawn map depicting a walled city on a peninsula with a park, a network of roads, and a scattering of buildings" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Map_of_Constantinople_%281422%29_by_Florentine_cartographer_Cristoforo_Buondelmonte.jpg/170px-Map_of_Constantinople_%281422%29_by_Florentine_cartographer_Cristoforo_Buondelmonte.jpg" width="170" height="214" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Map_of_Constantinople_%281422%29_by_Florentine_cartographer_Cristoforo_Buondelmonte.jpg/255px-Map_of_Constantinople_%281422%29_by_Florentine_cartographer_Cristoforo_Buondelmonte.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Map_of_Constantinople_%281422%29_by_Florentine_cartographer_Cristoforo_Buondelmonte.jpg/340px-Map_of_Constantinople_%281422%29_by_Florentine_cartographer_Cristoforo_Buondelmonte.jpg 2x" data-file-width="592" data-file-height="746" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Constantinople_(1422)_by_Florentine_cartographer_Cristoforo_Buondelmonte.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Created in 1422 by <a href="/wiki/Cristoforo_Buondelmonti" title="Cristoforo Buondelmonti">Cristoforo Buondelmonti</a>, this is the oldest surviving map of Constantinople.</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Constantine_the_Great" title="Constantine the Great">Constantine the Great</a> effectively became the emperor of the whole of the Roman Empire in September 324.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Two months later, he laid out the plans for a new, Christian city to replace Byzantium. As the eastern capital of the empire, the city was named <i><a href="/wiki/New_Rome" title="New Rome">Nova Roma</a></i>; most called it Constantinople, a name that persisted into the 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> On 11 May 330, Constantinople was proclaimed the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a>, which was later permanently divided between the two sons of <a href="/wiki/Theodosius_I" title="Theodosius I">Theodosius I</a> upon his death on 17 January 395, when the city became the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Eastern Roman (Byzantine) Empire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ba222_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ba222-59">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The establishment of Constantinople served as one of Constantine\'s most lasting accomplishments, shifting Roman power eastward as the city became a center of Greek culture and Christianity.<sup id="cite_ref-ba222_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ba222-59">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gr63_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gr63-60">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Numerous churches were built across the city, including the <a href="/wiki/Hagia_Sophia" title="Hagia Sophia">Hagia Sophia</a> which was built during the reign of <a href="/wiki/Justinian_I" title="Justinian I">Justinian the Great</a> and remained the world\'s largest cathedral for a thousand years.<sup id="cite_ref-klwa171_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-klwa171-61">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Constantine also undertook a major renovation and expansion of the <a href="/wiki/Hippodrome_of_Constantinople" title="Hippodrome of Constantinople">Hippodrome of Constantinople</a>; accommodating tens of thousands of spectators, the hippodrome became central to civic life and, in the 5th and 6th centuries, the epicenter of episodes of unrest, including the <a href="/wiki/Nika_riots" title="Nika riots">Nika riots</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Constantinople\'s location also ensured its existence would stand the test of time; for many centuries, its walls and seafront protected Europe against invaders from the east and the advance of Islam.<sup id="cite_ref-gr63_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gr63-60">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> During most of the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, the latter part of the Byzantine era, Constantinople was the largest and wealthiest city on the European continent and at times the largest in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Constantinople began to decline continuously after the end of the reign of Basil II in 1025. The final blow was given by the conquest of Villardouin and Enrico Dandolo in 1204 during the <a href="/wiki/Fourth_Crusade" title="Fourth Crusade">Fourth Crusade</a>, where the City was sacked and pillaged.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> The city subsequently became the center of the <a href="/wiki/Latin_Empire" title="Latin Empire">Latin Empire</a>, created by Catholic crusaders to replace the Orthodox Byzantine Empire.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Hagia Sophia was converted to a Catholic church in 1204. The Byzantine Empire was restored, albeit weakened, in 1261.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Constantinople\'s churches, defenses, and basic services were in disrepair,<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> and its population had dwindled to a hundred thousand from half a million during the 8th century.<sup id="cite_ref-pop-figures_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pop-figures-70">&#91;d&#93;</a></sup> After the reconquest of 1261, however some of the city\'s monuments were restored, and some, like the two Deisis mosaics in Hagia Sofia and Kariye, were created.\n</p><p>Various economic and military policies instituted by <a href="/wiki/Andronikos_II_Palaiologos" title="Andronikos II Palaiologos">Andronikos II</a>, such as the reduction of military forces, weakened the empire and left it vulnerable to attack.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> In the mid-14th-century, the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turks" title="Ottoman Turks">Ottoman Turks</a> began a strategy of gradually taking smaller towns and cities, cutting off Constantinople\'s supply routes and strangling it slowly.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> On 29 May 1453, after an eight-week siege (during which the last Roman emperor, <a href="/wiki/Constantine_XI_Palaiologos" title="Constantine XI Palaiologos">Constantine XI</a>, was killed), <a href="/wiki/Sultan" title="Sultan">Sultan</a> <a href="/wiki/Mehmed_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Mehmed II">Mehmed II</a> "the Conqueror" <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Constantinople" title="Fall of Constantinople">captured Constantinople</a> and declared it the new capital of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>. Hours later, the sultan rode to the Hagia Sophia and summoned an imam to proclaim the <a href="/wiki/Shahada" title="Shahada">Islamic creed</a>, converting the grand cathedral into an imperial mosque due to the city\'s refusal to surrender peacefully.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Mehmed declared himself as the new "Kaysar-i R\xc3\xbbm" (the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turkish_language" title="Ottoman Turkish language">Ottoman Turkish</a> equivalent of <a href="/wiki/Caesar_(title)" title="Caesar (title)">Caesar</a> of Rome) and the Ottoman state was reorganized into an empire.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ottoman_Empire_and_Turkish_Republic_eras">Ottoman Empire and Turkish Republic eras</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Istanbul&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Ottoman Empire and Turkish Republic eras">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px"><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Aivazovsky_-_View_of_Constantinople_and_the_Bosphorus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Aivazovsky_-_View_of_Constantinople_and_the_Bosphorus.jpg/200px-Aivazovsky_-_View_of_Constantinople_and_the_Bosphorus.jpg" width="200" height="125" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Aivazovsky_-_View_of_Constantinople_and_the_Bosphorus.jpg/300px-Aivazovsky_-_View_of_Constantinople_and_the_Bosphorus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Aivazovsky_-_View_of_Constantinople_and_the_Bosphorus.jpg/400px-Aivazovsky_-_View_of_Constantinople_and_the_Bosphorus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="2509" /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Ivan_Constantinovich_Aivazovsky_-_Dusk_on_the_Golden_Horn.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Ivan_Constantinovich_Aivazovsky_-_Dusk_on_the_Golden_Horn.JPG/200px-Ivan_Constantinovich_Aivazovsky_-_Dusk_on_the_Golden_Horn.JPG" width="200" height="144" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Ivan_Constantinovich_Aivazovsky_-_Dusk_on_the_Golden_Horn.JPG/300px-Ivan_Constantinovich_Aivazovsky_-_Dusk_on_the_Golden_Horn.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Ivan_Constantinovich_Aivazovsky_-_Dusk_on_the_Golden_Horn.JPG/400px-Ivan_Constantinovich_Aivazovsky_-_Dusk_on_the_Golden_Horn.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1720" data-file-height="1238" /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:View_of_constantinople_by_evening_light.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/View_of_constantinople_by_evening_light.jpg/200px-View_of_constantinople_by_evening_light.jpg" width="200" height="129" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/View_of_constantinople_by_evening_light.jpg/300px-View_of_constantinople_by_evening_light.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/View_of_constantinople_by_evening_light.jpg/400px-View_of_constantinople_by_evening_light.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1858" data-file-height="1200" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Three paintings of Ottoman era Istanbul by <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Aivazovsky" title="Ivan Aivazovsky">Ivan Aivazovsky</a></div></div></div></div>\n<p>Following the conquest of Constantinople, Mehmed II immediately set out to revitalize the city, by then also known as Istanbul. He urged the return of those who had fled the city during the siege, and resettled Muslims, Jews, and Christians from other parts of Anatolia. He demanded that five thousand households needed to be transferred to Constantinople by September.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> From all over the Islamic empire, prisoners of war and deported people were sent to the city: these people were called "S\xc3\xbcrg\xc3\xbcn" in Turkish (<a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>: <span lang="el">\xcf\x83\xce\xbf\xcf\x85\xcf\x81\xce\xb3\xce\xbf\xcf\x8d\xce\xbd\xce\xb9\xce\xb4\xce\xb5\xcf\x82</span>).<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> However, many people escaped again from the city, and there were several outbreaks of plague, so that in 1459 Mehmet allowed the deported Greeks to come back to the city.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> He also invited people from all over Europe to his capital, creating a cosmopolitan society that persisted through much of the Ottoman period.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Plague continued, however, to be essentially endemic in Istanbul for the rest of the century, as it had been from 1520, with a few years of respite between 1529 and 1533, 1549 and 1552, and from 1567 to 1570; epidemics originating in the West and in the Hejaz and southern Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> Population growth in Anatolia, however, allowed Istanbul to replace its losses and maintain its population of around 500,000 inhabitants down to 1800. Mehmed II also repaired the city\'s damaged infrastructure, including the whole <a href="/wiki/Valens_Aqueduct#Ottoman_period" title="Valens Aqueduct">water system</a>, began to build the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Bazaar,_Istanbul" title="Grand Bazaar, Istanbul">Grand Bazaar</a>, and constructed <a href="/wiki/Topkap%C4%B1_Palace" title="Topkap\xc4\xb1 Palace">Topkap\xc4\xb1 Palace</a>, the sultan\'s official residence.<sup id="cite_ref-holale307_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-holale307-80">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> With the transfer of the capital from <a href="/wiki/Edirne" title="Edirne">Edirne</a> (formerly Adrianople) to Constantinople, the new state was declared as the successor and continuation of the Roman Empire.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_%E2%80%A6trialsanderrors_-_Kara-Kevi_(Galata)_and_view_of_Pera,_Constantinople,_Turkey,_ca._1895.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Flickr_-_%E2%80%A6trialsanderrors_-_Kara-Kevi_%28Galata%29_and_view_of_Pera%2C_Constantinople%2C_Turkey%2C_ca._1895.jpg/220px-Flickr_-_%E2%80%A6trialsanderrors_-_Kara-Kevi_%28Galata%29_and_view_of_Pera%2C_Constantinople%2C_Turkey%2C_ca._1895.jpg" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Flickr_-_%E2%80%A6trialsanderrors_-_Kara-Kevi_%28Galata%29_and_view_of_Pera%2C_Constantinople%2C_Turkey%2C_ca._1895.jpg/330px-Flickr_-_%E2%80%A6trialsanderrors_-_Kara-Kevi_%28Galata%29_and_view_of_Pera%2C_Constantinople%2C_Turkey%2C_ca._1895.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Flickr_-_%E2%80%A6trialsanderrors_-_Kara-Kevi_%28Galata%29_and_view_of_Pera%2C_Constantinople%2C_Turkey%2C_ca._1895.jpg/440px-Flickr_-_%E2%80%A6trialsanderrors_-_Kara-Kevi_%28Galata%29_and_view_of_Pera%2C_Constantinople%2C_Turkey%2C_ca._1895.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3289" data-file-height="2392" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_%E2%80%A6trialsanderrors_-_Kara-Kevi_(Galata)_and_view_of_Pera,_Constantinople,_Turkey,_ca._1895.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Galata_Bridge" title="Galata Bridge">Galata Bridge</a> in the 19th century</div></div></div>\n<p>The Ottomans quickly transformed the city from a bastion of Christianity to a symbol of <a href="/wiki/Islamic_culture" title="Islamic culture">Islamic culture</a>. <a href="/wiki/Waqf" title="Waqf">Religious foundations</a> were established to fund the construction of ornate <a href="/wiki/Mosques_commissioned_by_the_Ottoman_dynasty" title="Mosques commissioned by the Ottoman dynasty">imperial mosques</a>, often adjoined by schools, hospitals, and public baths.<sup id="cite_ref-holale307_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-holale307-80">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman Dynasty">Ottoman Dynasty</a> claimed the status of <a href="/wiki/Caliphate" title="Caliphate">caliphate</a> in 1517, with Istanbul remaining the capital of this <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Caliphate" title="Ottoman Caliphate">last caliphate</a> for four centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-maag1145_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-maag1145-13">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Suleiman_the_Magnificent" title="Suleiman the Magnificent">Suleiman the Magnificent</a>\'s reign from 1520 to 1566 was a period of especially great artistic and architectural achievement; chief architect <a href="/wiki/Mimar_Sinan" title="Mimar Sinan">Mimar Sinan</a> designed several iconic buildings in the city, while Ottoman arts of <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0znik_pottery" class="mw-redirect" title="\xc4\xb0znik pottery">ceramics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stained_glass" title="Stained glass">stained glass</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islamic_calligraphy" title="Islamic calligraphy">calligraphy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_miniature" title="Ottoman miniature">miniature</a> flourished.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> The population of Istanbul was 570,000 by the end of the 18th century.<sup id="cite_ref-chfo_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chfo-83">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A period of rebellion at the start of the 19th century led to the rise of the progressive Sultan <a href="/wiki/Mahmud_II" title="Mahmud II">Mahmud II</a> and eventually to the <i><a href="/wiki/Tanzimat" title="Tanzimat">Tanzimat</a></i> period, which produced political reforms and allowed new technology to be introduced to the city.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Bridges across the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horn" title="Golden Horn">Golden Horn</a> were constructed during this period,<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> and Istanbul was connected to the rest of the European railway network in the 1880s.<sup id="cite_ref-ha251_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ha251-86">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> Modern facilities, such as a water supply network, electricity, telephones, and trams, were gradually introduced to Istanbul over the following decades, although later than to other European cities.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> The modernization efforts were not enough to forestall the <a href="/wiki/Decline_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Decline of the Ottoman Empire">decline of the Ottoman Empire</a>.\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:358px;max-width:358px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:177px;max-width:177px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Aerial_view_of_Istanbul_19_March_1918.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Aerial_view_of_Istanbul_19_March_1918.jpg/175px-Aerial_view_of_Istanbul_19_March_1918.jpg" width="175" height="119" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Aerial_view_of_Istanbul_19_March_1918.jpg/263px-Aerial_view_of_Istanbul_19_March_1918.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Aerial_view_of_Istanbul_19_March_1918.jpg/350px-Aerial_view_of_Istanbul_19_March_1918.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1271" data-file-height="865" /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:177px;max-width:177px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Aerial_view_of_Istanbul_on_19_March_1918.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Aerial_view_of_Istanbul_on_19_March_1918.jpg/175px-Aerial_view_of_Istanbul_on_19_March_1918.jpg" width="175" height="119" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Aerial_view_of_Istanbul_on_19_March_1918.jpg/263px-Aerial_view_of_Istanbul_on_19_March_1918.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Aerial_view_of_Istanbul_on_19_March_1918.jpg/350px-Aerial_view_of_Istanbul_on_19_March_1918.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1273" data-file-height="869" /></a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">Two aerial photos of Istanbul, the Golden Horn and the Bosphorus, taken from a German zeppelin on 19 March 1918.</div></div></div>\n<p>Sultan <a href="/wiki/Abdul_Hamid_II" title="Abdul Hamid II">Abdul Hamid II</a> was deposed with the <a href="/wiki/Young_Turk_Revolution" title="Young Turk Revolution">Young Turk Revolution</a> in 1908 and the <a href="/wiki/General_Assembly_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="General Assembly of the Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Parliament</a>, closed since <a href="/wiki/First_Constitutional_Era" title="First Constitutional Era">14 February 1878</a>, was reopened 30 years later on 23 July 1908, which marked the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Second_Constitutional_Era" title="Second Constitutional Era">Second Constitutional Era</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-tarihiolaylar_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tarihiolaylar-88">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> A series of wars in the early 20th century, such as the <a href="/wiki/Italo-Turkish_War" title="Italo-Turkish War">Italo-Turkish War</a> (1911\xe2\x80\x931912) and the <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Wars" title="Balkan Wars">Balkan Wars</a> (1912\xe2\x80\x931913), plagued the ailing empire\'s capital and resulted in the <a href="/wiki/1913_Ottoman_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1913 Ottoman coup d&#39;\xc3\xa9tat">1913 Ottoman coup d\'\xc3\xa9tat</a>, which brought the regime of the <a href="/wiki/Three_Pashas" title="Three Pashas">Three Pashas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> \n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bankalar_Caddesi_in_the_1920%27s.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Bankalar_Caddesi_in_the_1920%27s.jpg/200px-Bankalar_Caddesi_in_the_1920%27s.jpg" width="200" height="244" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Bankalar_Caddesi_in_the_1920%27s.jpg/300px-Bankalar_Caddesi_in_the_1920%27s.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Bankalar_Caddesi_in_the_1920%27s.jpg/400px-Bankalar_Caddesi_in_the_1920%27s.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="977" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bankalar_Caddesi_in_the_1920%27s.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A view of <a href="/wiki/Bankalar_Caddesi" title="Bankalar Caddesi">Bankalar Caddesi</a> (<i>Banks Street</i>) in the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Republic_of_Turkey" title="History of the Republic of Turkey">late 1920s</a>. Completed in 1892, the Ottoman Central Bank headquarters is seen at left. In 1995 the <a href="/wiki/Borsa_Istanbul" title="Borsa Istanbul">Istanbul Stock Exchange</a> moved to <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0stinye" title="\xc4\xb0stinye">\xc4\xb0stinye</a>, while numerous Turkish banks have moved to <a href="/wiki/Levent" title="Levent">Levent</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maslak" title="Maslak">Maslak</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Ottoman Empire joined <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> (1914\xe2\x80\x931918) on the side of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers">Central Powers</a> and was ultimately defeated. The <a href="/wiki/Deportation_of_Armenian_intellectuals_on_24_April_1915" title="Deportation of Armenian intellectuals on 24 April 1915">deportation of Armenian intellectuals on 24 April 1915</a> was among the major events which marked the start of the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Genocide" title="Armenian Genocide">Armenian Genocide</a> during WWI.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> As a result of the war and the events in its aftermath, the city\'s <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Christianity in the Ottoman Empire">Christian</a> population declined from 450,000 to 240,000 between 1914 and 1927.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Armistice_of_Mudros" title="Armistice of Mudros">Armistice of Mudros</a> was signed on 30 October 1918 and the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I" title="Allies of World War I">Allies</a> <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_Constantinople" title="Occupation of Constantinople">occupied Constantinople</a> on 13 November 1918. The <a href="/wiki/General_Assembly_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="General Assembly of the Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Parliament</a> was dissolved by the Allies on 11 April 1920 and the Ottoman delegation led by <a href="/wiki/Damat_Ferid_Pasha" title="Damat Ferid Pasha">Damat Ferid Pasha</a> was forced to sign the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_S%C3%A8vres" title="Treaty of S\xc3\xa8vres">Treaty of S\xc3\xa8vres</a> on 10 August 1920.\n</p><p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_War_of_Independence" title="Turkish War of Independence">Turkish War of Independence</a> (1919\xe2\x80\x931922), the <a href="/wiki/Grand_National_Assembly_of_Turkey" title="Grand National Assembly of Turkey">Grand National Assembly of Turkey</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ankara" title="Ankara">Ankara</a> abolished the <a href="/wiki/Sultanate" class="mw-redirect" title="Sultanate">Sultanate</a> on 1 November 1922, and the last <a href="/wiki/List_of_sultans_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="List of sultans of the Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Sultan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mehmed_VI" title="Mehmed VI">Mehmed VI</a>, was declared <i><a href="/wiki/150_personae_non_gratae_of_Turkey" title="150 personae non gratae of Turkey">persona non grata</a></i>. Leaving aboard the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">British</a> <a href="/wiki/Warship" title="Warship">warship</a> <a href="/wiki/HMS_Malaya" title="HMS Malaya">HMS <i>Malaya</i></a> on 17 November 1922, he went into exile and died in <a href="/wiki/Sanremo" title="Sanremo">Sanremo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, on 16 May 1926. The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lausanne" title="Treaty of Lausanne">Treaty of Lausanne</a> was signed on 24 July 1923, and the <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_Constantinople" title="Occupation of Constantinople">occupation of Constantinople</a> ended with the departure of the last forces of the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I" title="Allies of World War I">Allies</a> from the city on 4 October 1923.<sup id="cite_ref-liberation-of-istanbul_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-liberation-of-istanbul-92">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> Turkish forces of the Ankara government, commanded by <a href="/wiki/%C5%9E%C3%BCkr%C3%BC_Naili_G%C3%B6kberk" title="\xc5\x9e\xc3\xbckr\xc3\xbc Naili G\xc3\xb6kberk">\xc5\x9e\xc3\xbckr\xc3\xbc Naili Pasha</a> (3rd Corps), entered the city with a ceremony on 6 October 1923, which has been marked as the <i>Liberation Day</i> of Istanbul (<a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>: <i>\xc4\xb0stanbul\'un Kurtulu\xc5\x9fu</i>) and is commemorated every year on its anniversary.<sup id="cite_ref-liberation-of-istanbul_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-liberation-of-istanbul-92">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> On 29 October 1923 the Grand National Assembly of Turkey declared the establishment of the Turkish Republic, with Ankara as its capital. <a href="/wiki/Mustafa_Kemal_Atat%C3%BCrk" title="Mustafa Kemal Atat\xc3\xbcrk">Mustafa Kemal Atat\xc3\xbcrk</a> became the Republic\'s first <a href="/wiki/President_of_Turkey" title="President of Turkey">President</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Ankara" title="Ankara">Ankara</a> was selected as Turkey\'s capital in 1923 to distance the new, secular republic from its Ottoman history.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> From the late 1940s and early 1950s, Istanbul underwent great structural change, as new public squares, boulevards, and avenues were constructed throughout the city, sometimes at the expense of historical buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> The population of Istanbul began to rapidly increase in the 1970s, as people from Anatolia migrated to the city to find employment in the many new factories that were built on the outskirts of the sprawling metropolis. This sudden, sharp rise in the city\'s population caused a large demand for housing, and many previously outlying villages and forests became engulfed into the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_area" title="Metropolitan area">metropolitan area</a> of Istanbul.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:1558px;">\n<div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Galata_Kulesi_%27nden_panorama.jpg" class="image" title="A panoramic view of Ottoman era Istanbul from Galata Tower in the 19th century (image with notes)"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Galata_Kulesi_%27nden_panorama.jpg/1550px-Galata_Kulesi_%27nden_panorama.jpg" width="1550" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Galata_Kulesi_%27nden_panorama.jpg/2325px-Galata_Kulesi_%27nden_panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Galata_Kulesi_%27nden_panorama.jpg/3100px-Galata_Kulesi_%27nden_panorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4350" data-file-height="420" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Galata_Kulesi_%27nden_panorama.jpg" title="File:Galata Kulesi &#39;nden panorama.jpg"> </a></div><center>A panoramic view of Ottoman era Istanbul from <a href="/wiki/Galata_Tower" title="Galata Tower">Galata Tower</a> in the 19th century (<a href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/File:Galata_Kulesi_%27nden_panorama.jpg" class="extiw" title="commons:File:Galata Kulesi &#39;nden panorama.jpg">image with notes</a>)</center></div>\n</div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Istanbul&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Turkey" title="Geography of Turkey">Geography of Turkey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_Turkey" title="Geology of Turkey">Geology of Turkey</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:West-turkey-plates-cropped.gif" class="image"><img alt="A high concentration of fault lines in northwestern Turkey, where the Eurasian and African plates meet; a few faults and ridges also appear under the Mediterranean" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/West-turkey-plates-cropped.gif/220px-West-turkey-plates-cropped.gif" width="220" height="203" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/West-turkey-plates-cropped.gif/330px-West-turkey-plates-cropped.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/West-turkey-plates-cropped.gif/440px-West-turkey-plates-cropped.gif 2x" data-file-width="597" data-file-height="550" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:West-turkey-plates-cropped.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Fault_(geology)" title="Fault (geology)">Faults</a> in western Turkey are concentrated just southwest of Istanbul, passing under the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Marmara" title="Sea of Marmara">Sea of Marmara</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">Aegean Sea</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Istanbul_and_Bosporus_big.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Satellite image showing a thin piece of land, densely populated on the south, bisected by a waterway" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Istanbul_and_Bosporus_big.jpg/220px-Istanbul_and_Bosporus_big.jpg" width="220" height="256" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Istanbul_and_Bosporus_big.jpg/330px-Istanbul_and_Bosporus_big.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Istanbul_and_Bosporus_big.jpg/440px-Istanbul_and_Bosporus_big.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="1163" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Istanbul_and_Bosporus_big.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Satellite view of Istanbul and the <a href="/wiki/Bosphorus" class="mw-redirect" title="Bosphorus">Bosphorus</a> <a href="/wiki/Strait" title="Strait">strait</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Istanbul_topographic_map.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Istanbul_topographic_map.jpg/220px-Istanbul_topographic_map.jpg" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Istanbul_topographic_map.jpg/330px-Istanbul_topographic_map.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Istanbul_topographic_map.jpg/440px-Istanbul_topographic_map.jpg 2x" data-file-width="849" data-file-height="602" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Istanbul_topographic_map.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Topography of Istanbul</div></div></div>\n<p>Istanbul is located in north-western <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Marmara_Region" title="Marmara Region">Marmara Region</a> on a total area of 5,343 square kilometers (2,063&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-city-area_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-city-area-4">&#91;b&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bosphorus" class="mw-redirect" title="Bosphorus">Bosphorus</a>, which connects the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Marmara" title="Sea of Marmara">Sea of Marmara</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>, divides the city into a European, <a href="/wiki/Thrace" title="Thrace">Thracian</a> side\xe2\x80\x94comprising the historic and economic centers\xe2\x80\x94and an Asian, <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolian</a> side. The city is further divided by the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horn" title="Golden Horn">Golden Horn</a>, a natural harbor bounding the peninsula where the former Byzantium and Constantinople were founded. The confluence of the Sea of Marmara, the Bosphorus, and the Golden Horn at the heart of present-day Istanbul has deterred attacking forces for thousands of years and remains a prominent feature of the city\'s landscape.<sup id="cite_ref-gr63_60-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gr63-60">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Following <a href="/wiki/Seven_hills_of_Rome" title="Seven hills of Rome">the model of Rome</a>, the historic peninsula is said to be characterized by <a href="/wiki/Seven_hills_of_Istanbul" title="Seven hills of Istanbul">seven hills</a>, each topped by imperial mosques. The easternmost of these hills is the site of Topkap\xc4\xb1 Palace on the <a href="/wiki/Sarayburnu" title="Sarayburnu">Sarayburnu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> Rising from the opposite side of the Golden Horn is another, conical hill, where the modern Beyo\xc4\x9flu district is situated. Because of the topography, buildings in Beyo\xc4\x9flu were once constructed with the help of terraced retaining walls, and roads were laid out in the form of steps.<sup id="cite_ref-topo_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-topo-102">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/%C3%9Csk%C3%BCdar" title="\xc3\x9csk\xc3\xbcdar">\xc3\x9csk\xc3\xbcdar</a> on the Asian side exhibits similarly hilly characteristics, with the terrain gradually extending down to the Bosphorus coast, but the landscape in \xc5\x9eemsipa\xc5\x9fa and Ayazma is more abrupt, akin to a <a href="/wiki/Promontory" title="Promontory">promontory</a>. The highest point in Istanbul is <a href="/wiki/Camlica_Hill" class="mw-redirect" title="Camlica Hill">\xc3\x87aml\xc4\xb1ca Hill</a>, with an altitude of 288 meters (945&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-topo_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-topo-102">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> The northern half of Istanbul has a higher mean elevation compared to the south coast, with locations surpassing 200 meters (660&#160;ft), and some coasts with steep cliffs resembling <a href="/wiki/Fjord" title="Fjord">fjords</a>, especially around the northern end of the Bosphorus, where it opens up to the Black Sea.\n</p><p>Istanbul is situated near the <a href="/wiki/North_Anatolian_Fault" title="North Anatolian Fault">North Anatolian Fault</a>, close to the boundary between the <a href="/wiki/African_Plate" title="African Plate">African</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_Plate" title="Eurasian Plate">Eurasian</a> Plates. This fault zone, which runs from northern Anatolia to the Sea of Marmara, has been responsible for several deadly earthquakes throughout the city\'s history. Among the most devastating of these seismic events was the <a href="/wiki/1509_Istanbul_earthquake" class="mw-redirect" title="1509 Istanbul earthquake">1509 earthquake</a>, which caused a tsunami that broke over the walls of the city and killed more than 10,000 people. More recently, in 1999, <a href="/wiki/1999_%C4%B0zmit_earthquake" title="1999 \xc4\xb0zmit earthquake">an earthquake</a> with its epicenter in nearby <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0zmit" title="\xc4\xb0zmit">\xc4\xb0zmit</a> left 18,000 people dead, including 1,000 people in Istanbul\'s suburbs. The people of Istanbul remain concerned that an even more catastrophic seismic event may be in the city\'s near future, as thousands of structures recently built to accommodate Istanbul\'s rapidly increasing population may not have been constructed properly.<sup id="cite_ref-dis-awaits_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dis-awaits-103">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> Seismologists say the risk of a 7.6-<a href="/wiki/Moment_magnitude_scale" title="Moment magnitude scale">magnitude</a> or greater earthquake striking Istanbul by 2030 is more than <span class="nowrap">60 percent</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Istanbul&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fog-over-istanbul-skyscrapers.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Skyscrapers, both near and far, soar above a dense layer of fog that keeps the ground hidden from view." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Fog-over-istanbul-skyscrapers.jpg/220px-Fog-over-istanbul-skyscrapers.jpg" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Fog-over-istanbul-skyscrapers.jpg/330px-Fog-over-istanbul-skyscrapers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Fog-over-istanbul-skyscrapers.jpg/440px-Fog-over-istanbul-skyscrapers.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="639" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fog-over-istanbul-skyscrapers.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Fog, seen here shrouding <a href="/wiki/Levent" title="Levent">Levent</a>, frequently forms in the morning.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Istanbul-precipitation.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Istanbul-precipitation.png/220px-Istanbul-precipitation.png" width="220" height="80" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Istanbul-precipitation.png/330px-Istanbul-precipitation.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Istanbul-precipitation.png/440px-Istanbul-precipitation.png 2x" data-file-width="572" data-file-height="208" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Istanbul-precipitation.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Contrasting annual <a href="/wiki/Precipitation" title="Precipitation">precipitation</a> differences in Istanbul, creating multiple microclimates.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Istanbul_K%C3%B6ppen_Map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Istanbul_K%C3%B6ppen_Map.png/220px-Istanbul_K%C3%B6ppen_Map.png" width="220" height="117" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Istanbul_K%C3%B6ppen_Map.png/330px-Istanbul_K%C3%B6ppen_Map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Istanbul_K%C3%B6ppen_Map.png/440px-Istanbul_K%C3%B6ppen_Map.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="424" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Istanbul_K%C3%B6ppen_Map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Microclimates of Istanbul according to <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">K\xc3\xb6ppen\xe2\x80\x93Geiger classification system</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">K\xc3\xb6ppen\xe2\x80\x93Geiger classification system</a>, Istanbul has a borderline <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean climate</a> (<i>Csa</i>), <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical climate</a> (<i>Cfa</i>) and <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a> (<i>Cfb</i>), due to its location in a transitional climatic zone. Since precipitation in summer months ranges from 20 to 65&#160;mm (1 to 3&#160;in), depending on location, the city cannot be classified as solely Mediterranean or humid subtropical.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Due to its size, diverse topography, maritime location and most importantly having a coastline to two different bodies of water to the north and south, Istanbul exhibits <a href="/wiki/Microclimate" title="Microclimate">microclimates</a>. The northern half of the city, as well as the Bosporus coastline, express characteristics of <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical climates</a>, because of humidity from the Black Sea and the relatively high concentration of vegetation. The climate in the populated areas of the city to the south, located on the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Marmara" title="Sea of Marmara">Sea of Marmara</a>, is warmer, drier and less affected by humidity.<sup id="cite_ref-efcu716_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-efcu716-109">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> The annual precipitation in the northern half can be twice as much (Bah\xc3\xa7ek\xc3\xb6y, 1166.6&#160;mm), than it is in the southern, Marmara coast (Florya 635.0&#160;mm).<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> There is a significant difference between annual mean temperatures on the north and south coasts as well, Bah\xc3\xa7ek\xc3\xb6y 12.8&#160;\xc2\xb0C (55.0&#160;\xc2\xb0F), Kartal 15.03&#160;\xc2\xb0C (59.05&#160;\xc2\xb0F).<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> Parts of the province that are away from both seas exhibit considerable continental influences, with much more pronounced night-day and summer-winter temperature differences. In winter some parts of the province average freezing or below at night.\n</p><p>Istanbul\'s persistently high <a href="/wiki/Humidity" title="Humidity">humidity</a> reaches <span class="nowrap">80 percent</span> most mornings.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc-weather_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-weather-112">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> Because of this, fog is very common, although more so in northern parts of the city and away from the city center.<sup id="cite_ref-efcu716_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-efcu716-109">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Dense fog disrupts transportation in the region, including on the Bosphorus, and is common during the autumn and winter months when the humidity remains high into the afternoon.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> The humid conditions and the fog tend to dissipate by midday during the summer months, but the lingering humidity exacerbates the moderately high summer temperatures.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc-weather_112-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-weather-112">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pelit_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pelit-116">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> During these summer months, high temperatures average around 29&#160;\xc2\xb0C (84&#160;\xc2\xb0F) and rainfall is uncommon; there are only about fifteen days with measurable precipitation between June and August.<sup id="cite_ref-tsms-main_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tsms-main-117">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> The summer months also have the highest concentration of thunderstorms.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Winter is colder in Istanbul than in most other cities around the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Basin" title="Mediterranean Basin">Mediterranean Basin</a>, with low temperatures averaging 1\xe2\x80\x934&#160;\xc2\xb0C (34\xe2\x80\x9339&#160;\xc2\xb0F).<sup id="cite_ref-tsms-main_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tsms-main-117">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lake-effect_snow" title="Lake-effect snow">Lake-effect snow</a> from the Black Sea is common, although difficult to forecast, with the potential to be heavy and\xe2\x80\x94as with the fog\xe2\x80\x94disruptive to the city\'s infrastructure.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> Spring and autumn are mild, but often wet and unpredictable; chilly winds from the northwest and warm gusts from the south\xe2\x80\x94sometimes in the same day\xe2\x80\x94tend to cause fluctuations in temperature.<sup id="cite_ref-pelit_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pelit-116">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Overall, Istanbul has an annual average of <span class="nowrap">130 days</span> with significant precipitation, which amounts to 810 millimeters (31.9&#160;in) per year.<sup id="cite_ref-tsms-main_117-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tsms-main-117">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tsms-rain_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tsms-rain-121">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> The highest and lowest temperatures ever recorded in the city center on the Marmara coast are 40.5&#160;\xc2\xb0C (105&#160;\xc2\xb0F) and \xe2\x88\x9216.1&#160;\xc2\xb0C (3&#160;\xc2\xb0F). The greatest rainfall recorded in a day is 227 millimeters (8.9&#160;in), and the highest recorded snow cover is 80 centimeters (31&#160;in).<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable collapsible" style="width:90%;
