style="background:#FFFF66;color:#000000;">15.0\n</td>\n<td style="background:#FFFF55;color:#000000;">14.0\n</td>\n<td style="background:#FFFF33;color:#000000;">12.0\n</td>\n<td style="background:#F7F722;color:#000000;">11.0\n</td>\n<td style="background:#F0F011;color:#000000;">10.0\n</td>\n<td style="background:#E9E900;color:#000000;">9.0\n</td>\n<td style="background:#FFFF35;color:#000000;border-left-width:medium">12.2\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Average <a href="/wiki/Ultraviolet_index" title="Ultraviolet index">Ultraviolet index</a>\n</th>\n<td style="background:#289500;color:#000000;">2\n</td>\n<td style="background:#289500;color:#000000;">2\n</td>\n<td style="background:#f7e400;color:#000000;">4\n</td>\n<td style="background:#f7e400;color:#000000;">5\n</td>\n<td style="background:#f85900;color:#000000;">7\n</td>\n<td style="background:#d8001d;color:#000000;">8\n</td>\n<td style="background:#d8001d;color:#000000;">9\n</td>\n<td style="background:#d8001d;color:#000000;">8\n</td>\n<td style="background:#f85900;color:#000000;">6\n</td>\n<td style="background:#f7e400;color:#000000;">4\n</td>\n<td style="background:#289500;color:#000000;">2\n</td>\n<td style="background:#289500;color:#000000;">1\n</td>\n<td style="background:#f7e400;color:#000000;border-left-width:medium">4.8\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th colspan="14" style="background:#f8f9fa;font-weight:normal;font-size:95%;">Source: Weather Atlas <sup id="cite_ref-Weather_Atlas_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Weather_Atlas-127">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>\n</th></tr></tbody></table>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate_change">Climate change</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Istanbul&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Climate change">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Global_warming_in_Turkey" class="mw-redirect" title="Global warming in Turkey">Global warming in Turkey</a> may cause more urban heatwaves,<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> droughts,<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> storms,<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> and flooding.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CCTur_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CCTur-132">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> Sea level rise is forecast to affect city infrastructure, for example <a href="/wiki/Kad%C4%B1k%C3%B6y_(Istanbul_Metro)" title="Kad\xc4\xb1k\xc3\xb6y (Istanbul Metro)">Kad\xc4\xb1koy metro  station</a> is threatened with flooding.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> \n<a href="/wiki/Xeriscaping" title="Xeriscaping">Xeriscaping</a> of green spaces has been suggested,<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> however Istanbul does not have a climate change action plan merely an inactive website.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cityscape">Cityscape</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Istanbul&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Cityscape">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_urban_centers_in_Istanbul" title="List of urban centers in Istanbul">List of urban centers in Istanbul</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Topkap%C4%B1_-_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Topkap%C4%B1_-_01.jpg/220px-Topkap%C4%B1_-_01.jpg" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Topkap%C4%B1_-_01.jpg/330px-Topkap%C4%B1_-_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Topkap%C4%B1_-_01.jpg/440px-Topkap%C4%B1_-_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3635" data-file-height="1817" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Topkap%C4%B1_-_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A view of <a href="/wiki/Topkap%C4%B1_Palace" title="Topkap\xc4\xb1 Palace">Topkap\xc4\xb1 Palace</a> from across the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horn" title="Golden Horn">Golden Horn</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/Prince_Islands" title="Prince Islands">Prince Islands</a> in the background.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Fatih" title="Fatih">Fatih</a> district, which was named after Sultan <a href="/wiki/Mehmed_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Mehmed II">Mehmed the Conqueror</a> (<a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>: <i>Fatih Sultan Mehmed</i>), corresponds to what was, until the Ottoman conquest in 1453, the whole of the city of <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a> (today is the capital district and called the <i>historic peninsula</i> of Istanbul) on the southern shore of the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horn" title="Golden Horn">Golden Horn</a>, across the medieval <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Genoa" title="Republic of Genoa">Genoese</a> citadel of <a href="/wiki/Galata" title="Galata">Galata</a> on the northern shore. The Genoese fortifications in Galata were largely demolished in the 19th century, leaving only the <a href="/wiki/Galata_Tower" title="Galata Tower">Galata Tower</a>, to make way for the northward expansion of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> Galata (<a href="/wiki/Karak%C3%B6y" title="Karak\xc3\xb6y">Karak\xc3\xb6y</a>) is today a quarter within the <a href="/wiki/Beyo%C4%9Flu" title="Beyo\xc4\x9flu">Beyo\xc4\x9flu</a> (Pera) district, which forms Istanbul\'s commercial and entertainment center and includes <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0stiklal_Avenue" title="\xc4\xb0stiklal Avenue">\xc4\xb0stiklal Avenue</a> and <a href="/wiki/Taksim_Square" title="Taksim Square">Taksim Square</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Dolmabah%C3%A7e_Palace" title="Dolmabah\xc3\xa7e Palace">Dolmabah\xc3\xa7e Palace</a>, the seat of government during the late Ottoman period, is located in the <a href="/wiki/Be%C5%9Fikta%C5%9F" title="Be\xc5\x9fikta\xc5\x9f">Be\xc5\x9fikta\xc5\x9f</a> district on the European shore of the <a href="/wiki/Bosphorus" class="mw-redirect" title="Bosphorus">Bosphorus</a> strait, to the north of Beyo\xc4\x9flu. The <a href="/wiki/Sublime_Porte" title="Sublime Porte">Sublime Porte</a> (<i>B\xc3\xa2b-\xc4\xb1 \xc3\x82li</i>), which became a <a href="/wiki/Metonym" class="mw-redirect" title="Metonym">metonym</a> for the Ottoman government, was originally used to describe the Imperial Gate (<i>B\xc3\xa2b-\xc4\xb1 H\xc3\xbcm\xc3\xa2y\xc3\xbbn</i>) at the outermost courtyard of the <a href="/wiki/Topkap%C4%B1_Palace" title="Topkap\xc4\xb1 Palace">Topkap\xc4\xb1 Palace</a>; but after the 18th century, the <i>Sublime Porte</i> (or simply <i>Porte</i>) began to refer to the gate of the <i>Sadrazaml\xc4\xb1k</i> (Prime Ministry) compound in the <a href="/wiki/Ca%C4%9Falo%C4%9Flu" title="Ca\xc4\x9falo\xc4\x9flu">Ca\xc4\x9falo\xc4\x9flu</a> quarter near Topkap\xc4\xb1 Palace, where the offices of the <a href="/wiki/Sadrazam" class="mw-redirect" title="Sadrazam">Sadrazam</a> (<a href="/wiki/Grand_Vizier" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand Vizier">Grand Vizier</a>) and other <a href="/wiki/Vizier" title="Vizier">Viziers</a> were located, and where foreign diplomats were received. The former village of <a href="/wiki/Ortak%C3%B6y" title="Ortak\xc3\xb6y">Ortak\xc3\xb6y</a> is situated within Be\xc5\x9fikta\xc5\x9f and gives its name to the <a href="/wiki/Ortak%C3%B6y_Mosque" title="Ortak\xc3\xb6y Mosque">Ortak\xc3\xb6y Mosque</a> on the Bosphorus, near the <a href="/wiki/Bosphorus_Bridge" title="Bosphorus Bridge">Bosphorus Bridge</a>. Lining both the European and Asian shores of the Bosphorus are the historic <i><a href="/wiki/Yal%C4%B1" title="Yal\xc4\xb1">yal\xc4\xb1s</a></i>, luxurious chalet mansions built by Ottoman aristocrats and elites as summer homes.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> Farther inland, outside the city\'s inner ring road, are <a href="/wiki/Levent" title="Levent">Levent</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maslak" title="Maslak">Maslak</a>, Istanbul\'s main business districts.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ya%C4%9Fl%C4%B1k%C3%A7%C4%B1_Hac%C4%B1_Re%C5%9Fit_Bey_and_Prenses_Rukiye_Yal%C4%B1s%C4%B1_on_the_Bosphorus,_Istanbul,_Turkey_001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Two- and three-story colored houses with docks and balconies, built directly on the edge of the water" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Ya%C4%9Fl%C4%B1k%C3%A7%C4%B1_Hac%C4%B1_Re%C5%9Fit_Bey_and_Prenses_Rukiye_Yal%C4%B1s%C4%B1_on_the_Bosphorus%2C_Istanbul%2C_Turkey_001.jpg/220px-Ya%C4%9Fl%C4%B1k%C3%A7%C4%B1_Hac%C4%B1_Re%C5%9Fit_Bey_and_Prenses_Rukiye_Yal%C4%B1s%C4%B1_on_the_Bosphorus%2C_Istanbul%2C_Turkey_001.jpg" width="220" height="123" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Ya%C4%9Fl%C4%B1k%C3%A7%C4%B1_Hac%C4%B1_Re%C5%9Fit_Bey_and_Prenses_Rukiye_Yal%C4%B1s%C4%B1_on_the_Bosphorus%2C_Istanbul%2C_Turkey_001.jpg/330px-Ya%C4%9Fl%C4%B1k%C3%A7%C4%B1_Hac%C4%B1_Re%C5%9Fit_Bey_and_Prenses_Rukiye_Yal%C4%B1s%C4%B1_on_the_Bosphorus%2C_Istanbul%2C_Turkey_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Ya%C4%9Fl%C4%B1k%C3%A7%C4%B1_Hac%C4%B1_Re%C5%9Fit_Bey_and_Prenses_Rukiye_Yal%C4%B1s%C4%B1_on_the_Bosphorus%2C_Istanbul%2C_Turkey_001.jpg/440px-Ya%C4%9Fl%C4%B1k%C3%A7%C4%B1_Hac%C4%B1_Re%C5%9Fit_Bey_and_Prenses_Rukiye_Yal%C4%B1s%C4%B1_on_the_Bosphorus%2C_Istanbul%2C_Turkey_001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2403" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ya%C4%9Fl%C4%B1k%C3%A7%C4%B1_Hac%C4%B1_Re%C5%9Fit_Bey_and_Prenses_Rukiye_Yal%C4%B1s%C4%B1_on_the_Bosphorus,_Istanbul,_Turkey_001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Originally outside the city, <i><a href="/wiki/Yal%C4%B1" title="Yal\xc4\xb1">yal\xc4\xb1</a></i> residences along the <a href="/wiki/Bosphorus" class="mw-redirect" title="Bosphorus">Bosphorus</a> are now homes in some of Istanbul\'s elite neighborhoods.</div></div></div>\n<p>During the Ottoman period, <a href="/wiki/%C3%9Csk%C3%BCdar" title="\xc3\x9csk\xc3\xbcdar">\xc3\x9csk\xc3\xbcdar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kad%C4%B1k%C3%B6y" title="Kad\xc4\xb1k\xc3\xb6y">Kad\xc4\xb1k\xc3\xb6y</a> were outside the scope of urban Istanbul, serving as tranquil outposts with seaside <i>yal\xc4\xb1s</i> and gardens. But in the second half of the 20th century, the Asian side experienced major urban growth; the late development of this part of the city led to better infrastructure and tidier urban planning when compared with most other residential areas in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-wctr281_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wctr281-11">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Much of the Asian side of the Bosphorus functions as a suburb of the economic and commercial centers in European Istanbul, accounting for a third of the city\'s population but only a quarter of its employment.<sup id="cite_ref-wctr281_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wctr281-11">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> As a result of Istanbul\'s exponential growth in the 20th century, a significant portion of the city is composed of <i><a href="/wiki/Gecekondu" title="Gecekondu">gecekondus</a></i> (literally "built overnight"), referring to illegally constructed squatter buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-kar7896_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kar7896-140">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> At present, some <i>gecekondu</i> areas are being gradually demolished and replaced by modern mass-housing compounds.<sup id="cite_ref-yavuz_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yavuz-141">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> Moreover, large scale <a href="/wiki/Gentrification" title="Gentrification">gentrification</a> and <a href="/wiki/Urban_renewal" title="Urban renewal">urban renewal</a> projects have been taking place,<sup id="cite_ref-AtkinsonBridge2005_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AtkinsonBridge2005-142">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> such as the one in <a href="/wiki/Tarlaba%C5%9F%C4%B1" title="Tarlaba\xc5\x9f\xc4\xb1">Tarlaba\xc5\x9f\xc4\xb1</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> some of these projects, like the one in <a href="/wiki/Sulukule" title="Sulukule">Sulukule</a>, have faced criticism.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> The Turkish government also has ambitious plans for an expansion of the city west and northwards on the European side in conjunction with plans for a <a href="/wiki/Istanbul_New_Airport" title="Istanbul New Airport">third airport</a>; the new parts of the city will include four different settlements with specified urban functions, housing 1.5 million people.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Istanbul does not have a primary urban park, but it has several green areas. <a href="/wiki/G%C3%BClhane_Park" title="G\xc3\xbclhane Park">G\xc3\xbclhane Park</a> and <a href="/wiki/Y%C4%B1ld%C4%B1z_Park" title="Y\xc4\xb1ld\xc4\xb1z Park">Y\xc4\xb1ld\xc4\xb1z Park</a> were originally included within the grounds of two of Istanbul\'s palaces\xe2\x80\x94<a href="/wiki/Topkap%C4%B1_Palace" title="Topkap\xc4\xb1 Palace">Topkap\xc4\xb1 Palace</a> and <a href="/wiki/Y%C4%B1ld%C4%B1z_Palace" title="Y\xc4\xb1ld\xc4\xb1z Palace">Y\xc4\xb1ld\xc4\xb1z Palace</a>\xe2\x80\x94but they were repurposed as public parks in the early decades of the Turkish Republic.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> Another park, <a href="/wiki/Fethi_Pa%C5%9Fa_Korusu" title="Fethi Pa\xc5\x9fa Korusu">Fethi Pa\xc5\x9fa Korusu</a>, is situated on a hillside adjacent to the <a href="/wiki/Bosphorus_Bridge" title="Bosphorus Bridge">Bosphorus Bridge</a> in Anatolia, opposite Y\xc4\xb1ld\xc4\xb1z Palace in Europe. Along the European side, and close to the <a href="/wiki/Fatih_Sultan_Mehmet_Bridge" title="Fatih Sultan Mehmet Bridge">Fatih Sultan Mehmet Bridge</a>, is <a href="/wiki/Emirgan_Park" title="Emirgan Park">Emirgan Park</a>, which was known as the <i>Kyparades</i> (<a href="/wiki/Cypress" title="Cypress">Cypress</a> Forest) during the Byzantine period. In the Ottoman period, it was first granted to <a href="/wiki/Lord_Chancellor" title="Lord Chancellor">Ni\xc5\x9fanc\xc4\xb1</a> Feridun Ahmed Pasha in the 16th century, before being granted by Sultan <a href="/wiki/Murad_IV" title="Murad IV">Murad IV</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Safavid_dynasty" title="Safavid dynasty">Safavid</a> <a href="/wiki/Emir" title="Emir">Emir</a> G\xc3\xbbne Han in the 17th century, hence the name <i>Emirgan</i>. The 47-hectare (120-acre) park was later owned by <a href="/wiki/Khedive" title="Khedive">Khedive</a> <a href="/wiki/Isma%27il_Pasha" title="Isma&#39;il Pasha">Ismail Pasha</a> of <a href="/wiki/Khedivate_of_Egypt" title="Khedivate of Egypt">Ottoman Egypt and Sudan</a> in the 19th century. Emirgan Park is known for its diversity of plants and an annual <a href="/wiki/Tulip" title="Tulip">tulip</a> festival is held there since 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Justice_and_Development_Party_(Turkey)" title="Justice and Development Party (Turkey)">AKP</a> government\'s decision to replace <a href="/wiki/Taksim_Gezi_Park" title="Taksim Gezi Park">Taksim Gezi Park</a> with a replica of the Ottoman era <a href="/wiki/Taksim_Military_Barracks" title="Taksim Military Barracks">Taksim Military Barracks</a> (which was transformed into the <a href="/wiki/Taksim_Stadium" title="Taksim Stadium">Taksim Stadium</a> in 1921, before being demolished in 1940 for building Gezi Park) sparked a series of <a href="/wiki/Gezi_Park_protests" title="Gezi Park protests">nationwide protests in 2013</a> covering a wide range of issues. Popular during the summer among Istanbulites is <a href="/wiki/Belgrad_Forest" title="Belgrad Forest">Belgrad Forest</a>, spreading across 5,500 hectares (14,000 acres) at the northern edge of the city. The forest originally supplied water to the city and remnants of reservoirs used during Byzantine and Ottoman times survive.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:808px;">\n<div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Istanbul_panorama_and_skyline.jpg" class="image" title="Panoramic view of Istanbul from the confluence of the Bosphorus and the Sea of Marmara. Several landmarks\xe2\x80\x94including Sultan Ahmed Mosque, the Hagia Sophia, Topkap\xc4\xb1 Palace, and Dolmabah\xc3\xa7e Palace\xe2\x80\x94can be seen along their shores."><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Istanbul_panorama_and_skyline.jpg/800px-Istanbul_panorama_and_skyline.jpg" width="800" height="173" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Istanbul_panorama_and_skyline.jpg/1200px-Istanbul_panorama_and_skyline.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Istanbul_panorama_and_skyline.jpg/1600px-Istanbul_panorama_and_skyline.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="1123" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:center"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Istanbul_panorama_and_skyline.jpg" title="File:Istanbul panorama and skyline.jpg"> </a></div>Panoramic view of Istanbul from the confluence of the <a href="/wiki/Bosphorus" class="mw-redirect" title="Bosphorus">Bosphorus</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Marmara" title="Sea of Marmara">Sea of Marmara</a>. Several landmarks\xe2\x80\x94including <a href="/wiki/Sultan_Ahmed_Mosque" title="Sultan Ahmed Mosque">Sultan Ahmed Mosque</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hagia_Sophia" title="Hagia Sophia">Hagia Sophia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Topkap%C4%B1_Palace" title="Topkap\xc4\xb1 Palace">Topkap\xc4\xb1 Palace</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dolmabah%C3%A7e_Palace" title="Dolmabah\xc3\xa7e Palace">Dolmabah\xc3\xa7e Palace</a>\xe2\x80\x94can be seen along their shores.</div>\n</div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Istanbul&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Istanbul" title="Architecture of Istanbul">Architecture of Istanbul</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Turkey-3019_-_Hagia_Sophia_(2216460729).jpg" class="image"><img alt="A reddish building topped by a large dome and surrounded by smaller domes and four towers" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Turkey-3019_-_Hagia_Sophia_%282216460729%29.jpg/220px-Turkey-3019_-_Hagia_Sophia_%282216460729%29.jpg" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Turkey-3019_-_Hagia_Sophia_%282216460729%29.jpg/330px-Turkey-3019_-_Hagia_Sophia_%282216460729%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Turkey-3019_-_Hagia_Sophia_%282216460729%29.jpg/440px-Turkey-3019_-_Hagia_Sophia_%282216460729%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3329" data-file-height="2534" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Turkey-3019_-_Hagia_Sophia_(2216460729).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Originally a church, later a mosque, and today (since 1935) a museum, the 6th-century <a href="/wiki/Hagia_Sophia" title="Hagia Sophia">Hagia Sophia</a> (532\xe2\x80\x93537) in Istanbul (Constantinople) built by the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine</a> emperor <a href="/wiki/Justinian_I" title="Justinian I">Justinian the Great</a> was the largest cathedral ever constructed in the world for nearly a thousand years, until the completion of the <a href="/wiki/Seville_Cathedral" title="Seville Cathedral">Seville Cathedral</a> (1507) in <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>.</div></div></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px"><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Dolmabah%C3%A7e_Palace_(cropped).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Dolmabah%C3%A7e_Palace_%28cropped%29.JPG/200px-Dolmabah%C3%A7e_Palace_%28cropped%29.JPG" width="200" height="83" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Dolmabah%C3%A7e_Palace_%28cropped%29.JPG/300px-Dolmabah%C3%A7e_Palace_%28cropped%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Dolmabah%C3%A7e_Palace_%28cropped%29.JPG/400px-Dolmabah%C3%A7e_Palace_%28cropped%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="427" /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Istanbul_-_Palau_de_%C3%87%C4%B1ra%C4%9Fan.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Istanbul_-_Palau_de_%C3%87%C4%B1ra%C4%9Fan.JPG/200px-Istanbul_-_Palau_de_%C3%87%C4%B1ra%C4%9Fan.JPG" width="200" height="128" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Istanbul_-_Palau_de_%C3%87%C4%B1ra%C4%9Fan.JPG/300px-Istanbul_-_Palau_de_%C3%87%C4%B1ra%C4%9Fan.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Istanbul_-_Palau_de_%C3%87%C4%B1ra%C4%9Fan.JPG/400px-Istanbul_-_Palau_de_%C3%87%C4%B1ra%C4%9Fan.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2931" data-file-height="1876" /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Bosfor_B17-34.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Bosfor_B17-34.jpg/200px-Bosfor_B17-34.jpg" width="200" height="140" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Bosfor_B17-34.jpg/300px-Bosfor_B17-34.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Bosfor_B17-34.jpg/400px-Bosfor_B17-34.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1050" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Built by sultans <a href="/wiki/Abd%C3%BClmecid_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Abd\xc3\xbclmecid I">Abd\xc3\xbclmecid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Abd%C3%BClaziz_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Abd\xc3\xbclaziz of the Ottoman Empire">Abd\xc3\xbclaziz</a>, the 19th-century <a href="/wiki/Dolmabah%C3%A7e_Palace" title="Dolmabah\xc3\xa7e Palace">Dolmabah\xc3\xa7e</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C3%87%C4%B1ra%C4%9Fan_Palace" title="\xc3\x87\xc4\xb1ra\xc4\x9fan Palace">\xc3\x87\xc4\xb1ra\xc4\x9fan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beylerbeyi_Palace" title="Beylerbeyi Palace">Beylerbeyi</a> palaces on the European and Asian shores of the <a href="/wiki/Bosphorus" class="mw-redirect" title="Bosphorus">Bosphorus</a> strait were designed by members of the Armenian <a href="/wiki/Balyan_family" title="Balyan family">Balyan family</a> of Ottoman court architects.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div></div>\n<p>Istanbul is primarily known for its Byzantine and Ottoman architecture, but its buildings reflect the various peoples and empires that have previously ruled the city. Examples of Genoese and Roman architecture remain visible in Istanbul alongside their Ottoman counterparts. Nothing of the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek_architecture" title="Ancient Greek architecture">architecture of the classical Greek period</a> has survived, but <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Roman_architecture" title="Ancient Roman architecture">Roman architecture</a> has proved to be more durable. <a href="/wiki/Obelisk_of_Theodosius" title="Obelisk of Theodosius">The obelisk</a> erected by <a href="/wiki/Theodosius_I" title="Theodosius I">Theodosius</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Hippodrome_of_Constantinople" title="Hippodrome of Constantinople">Hippodrome of Constantinople</a> is still visible in Sultanahmet Square, and a section of the <a href="/wiki/Valens_Aqueduct" title="Valens Aqueduct">Valens Aqueduct</a>, constructed in the late 4th century, stands relatively intact at the western edge of the Fatih district.<sup id="cite_ref-coaot_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coaot-151">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Column_of_Constantine" title="Column of Constantine">Column of Constantine</a>, erected in 330 CE to mark the new Roman capital, stands not far from the Hippodrome.<sup id="cite_ref-coaot_151-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coaot-151">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sultan_Ahmed_Mosque_Istanbul_Turkey_retouched.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Sultan_Ahmed_Mosque_Istanbul_Turkey_retouched.jpg/220px-Sultan_Ahmed_Mosque_Istanbul_Turkey_retouched.jpg" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Sultan_Ahmed_Mosque_Istanbul_Turkey_retouched.jpg/330px-Sultan_Ahmed_Mosque_Istanbul_Turkey_retouched.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Sultan_Ahmed_Mosque_Istanbul_Turkey_retouched.jpg/440px-Sultan_Ahmed_Mosque_Istanbul_Turkey_retouched.jpg 2x" data-file-width="930" data-file-height="659" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sultan_Ahmed_Mosque_Istanbul_Turkey_retouched.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Completed in 1616, the <a href="/wiki/Sultan_Ahmed_Mosque" title="Sultan Ahmed Mosque">Sultan Ahmed Mosque</a> is popularly known as the <i>Blue Mosque</i> due to the blue <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0znik_tiles" class="mw-redirect" title="\xc4\xb0znik tiles">\xc4\xb0znik tiles</a> which adorn its interior.<sup id="cite_ref-bluemosque_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bluemosque-152">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>Early <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_architecture" title="Byzantine architecture">Byzantine architecture</a> followed the classical Roman model of domes and arches, but improved upon these elements, as in the <a href="/wiki/Little_Hagia_Sophia" title="Little Hagia Sophia">Church of the Saints Sergius and Bacchus</a>. The oldest surviving Byzantine church in Istanbul\xe2\x80\x94albeit in ruins\xe2\x80\x94is the <a href="/wiki/Monastery_of_Stoudios" title="Monastery of Stoudios">Monastery of Stoudios</a> (later converted into the Imrahor Mosque), which was built in 454.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> After the recapture of Constantinople in 1261, the Byzantines enlarged two of the most important churches extant, <a href="/wiki/Chora_Church" title="Chora Church">Chora Church</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pammakaristos_Church" title="Pammakaristos Church">Pammakaristos Church</a>. The pinnacle of Byzantine architecture, and one of Istanbul\'s most iconic structures, is the <a href="/wiki/Hagia_Sophia" title="Hagia Sophia">Hagia Sophia</a>. Topped by a dome 31 meters (102&#160;ft) in diameter,<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> the Hagia Sophia stood as the world\'s largest cathedral for centuries, and was later converted into a mosque and, as it stands now, a museum.<sup id="cite_ref-klwa171_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-klwa171-61">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Among the oldest surviving examples of <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_architecture" title="Ottoman architecture">Ottoman architecture</a> in Istanbul are the <a href="/wiki/Anadoluhisar%C4%B1" title="Anadoluhisar\xc4\xb1">Anadoluhisar\xc4\xb1</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rumelihisar%C4%B1" title="Rumelihisar\xc4\xb1">Rumelihisar\xc4\xb1</a> fortresses, which assisted the Ottomans during their siege of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> Over the next four centuries, the Ottomans made an indelible impression on the skyline of Istanbul, building towering mosques and ornate palaces. The largest palace, <a href="/wiki/Topkap%C4%B1_Palace" title="Topkap\xc4\xb1 Palace">Topkap\xc4\xb1</a>, includes a diverse array of architectural styles, from <a href="/wiki/Baroque_architecture" title="Baroque architecture">Baroque</a> inside the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Harem" class="mw-redirect" title="Imperial Harem">Harem</a>, to its <a href="/wiki/Neoclassical_architecture" title="Neoclassical architecture">Neoclassical</a> style <a href="/wiki/Enderun_School" title="Enderun School">Ender\xc3\xbbn Library</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Mosques_commissioned_by_the_Ottoman_dynasty" title="Mosques commissioned by the Ottoman dynasty">imperial mosques</a> include <a href="/wiki/Fatih_Mosque" class="mw-redirect" title="Fatih Mosque">Fatih Mosque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bayezid_Mosque" class="mw-redirect" title="Bayezid Mosque">Bayezid Mosque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yavuz_Selim_Mosque" title="Yavuz Selim Mosque">Yavuz Selim Mosque</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%BCleymaniye_Mosque" title="S\xc3\xbcleymaniye Mosque">S\xc3\xbcleymaniye Mosque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sultan_Ahmed_Mosque" title="Sultan Ahmed Mosque">Sultan Ahmed Mosque</a> (the Blue Mosque), and <a href="/wiki/New_Mosque_(Istanbul)" title="New Mosque (Istanbul)">Yeni Mosque</a>, all of which were built at the peak of the Ottoman Empire, in the 16th and 17th centuries. In the following centuries, and especially after the <i><a href="/wiki/Tanzimat" title="Tanzimat">Tanzimat</a></i> reforms, Ottoman architecture was supplanted by European styles.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> An example of which is the imperial <a href="/wiki/Nuruosmaniye_Mosque" title="Nuruosmaniye Mosque">Nuruosmaniye Mosque</a>. Areas around <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0stiklal_Avenue" title="\xc4\xb0stiklal Avenue">\xc4\xb0stiklal Avenue</a> were filled with grand European embassies and rows of buildings in Neoclassical, <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_Revival_architecture" title="Renaissance Revival architecture">Renaissance Revival</a> and <a href="/wiki/Art_Nouveau" title="Art Nouveau">Art Nouveau</a> styles, which went on to influence the architecture of a variety of structures in Beyo\xc4\x9flu\xe2\x80\x94including churches, stores, and theaters\xe2\x80\x94and official buildings such as <a href="/wiki/Dolmabah%C3%A7e_Palace" title="Dolmabah\xc3\xa7e Palace">Dolmabah\xc3\xa7e Palace</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administration">Administration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Istanbul&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Administration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/List_of_districts_of_Istanbul" title="List of districts of Istanbul">List of districts of Istanbul</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_neighbourhoods_of_Istanbul" title="List of neighbourhoods of Istanbul">List of neighbourhoods of Istanbul</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:342px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Istanbul_location_districts.svg" class="image"><img alt="A map depicting districts, squeezed between two bodies of water; farther districts are very large compared to those clustered in the center." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Istanbul_location_districts.svg/340px-Istanbul_location_districts.svg.png" width="340" height="183" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Istanbul_location_districts.svg/510px-Istanbul_location_districts.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Istanbul_location_districts.svg/680px-Istanbul_location_districts.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="276" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Istanbul_location_districts.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Istanbul\'s districts extend far from the city center, along the full length of the Bosphorus (with the Black Sea at the top and the Sea of Marmara at the bottom of the map).</div></div></div>\n<p>Since 2004, the municipal boundaries of Istanbul have been coincident with the boundaries of its province.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> The city, considered capital of <a href="/wiki/Istanbul_Province" title="Istanbul Province">Istanbul Province</a>, is administered by the Istanbul Metropolitan Municipality (MMI), which oversees the <a href="/wiki/List_of_districts_of_Istanbul" title="List of districts of Istanbul">39 districts</a> of the city-province.<sup id="cite_ref-city-area_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-city-area-4">&#91;b&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The current city structure can be traced back to the <i>Tanzimat</i> period of reform in the 19th century, before which <a href="/wiki/Qadi" title="Qadi">Islamic judges</a> and imams led the city under the auspices of the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Vizier" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand Vizier">Grand Vizier</a>. Following the model of French cities, this religious system was replaced by a mayor and a citywide council composed of representatives of the confessional groups (<i><a href="/wiki/Millet_(Ottoman_Empire)" title="Millet (Ottoman Empire)">millet</a></i>) across Istanbul. Beyo\xc4\x9flu was the first area of the city to have its own director and council, with members instead being longtime residents of the neighborhood.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> Laws enacted after the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_constitution_of_1876" title="Ottoman constitution of 1876">Ottoman constitution of 1876</a> aimed to expand this structure across the city, imitating the twenty <a href="/wiki/Arrondissements_of_Paris" title="Arrondissements of Paris">arrondissements of Paris</a>, but they were not fully implemented until 1908, when Istanbul was declared a province with nine constituent districts.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> This system continued beyond the founding of the Turkish Republic, with the province renamed a <i>belediye</i> (municipality), but the municipality was disbanded in 1957.<sup id="cite_ref-mmi-history_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mmi-history-98">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Adalar_5536.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Adalar_5536.jpg/220px-Adalar_5536.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Adalar_5536.jpg/330px-Adalar_5536.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Adalar_5536.jpg/440px-Adalar_5536.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2576" data-file-height="1932" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Adalar_5536.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Statue of <a href="/wiki/Mustafa_Kemal_Atat%C3%BCrk" title="Mustafa Kemal Atat\xc3\xbcrk">Atat\xc3\xbcrk</a> in <a href="/wiki/B%C3%BCy%C3%BCkada" title="B\xc3\xbcy\xc3\xbckada">B\xc3\xbcy\xc3\xbckada</a>, the largest of the <a href="/wiki/Prince_Islands" title="Prince Islands">Prince Islands</a> to the southeast of Istanbul, which collectively form the <a href="/wiki/Adalar" class="mw-redirect" title="Adalar">Adalar (<i>Isles</i>)</a> district of <a href="/wiki/Istanbul_Province" title="Istanbul Province">Istanbul Province</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Small settlements adjacent to major population centers in Turkey, including Istanbul, were merged into their respective primary cities during the early 1980s, resulting in metropolitan municipalities.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> The main decision-making body of the Istanbul Metropolitan Municipality is the Municipal Council, with members drawn from district councils.\n</p><p>The Municipal Council is responsible for citywide issues, including managing the budget, maintaining civic infrastructure, and overseeing museums and major cultural centers.<sup id="cite_ref-kapa1535_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kapa1535-166">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> Since the government operates under a "powerful mayor, weak council" approach, the council\'s leader\xe2\x80\x94the metropolitan mayor\xe2\x80\x94has the authority to make swift decisions, often at the expense of transparency.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> The Municipal Council is advised by the Metropolitan Executive Committee, although the Committee also has limited power to make decisions of its own.<sup id="cite_ref-kapa156_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kapa156-168">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> All representatives on the Committee are appointed by the metropolitan mayor and the Council, with the mayor\xe2\x80\x94or someone of his or her choosing\xe2\x80\x94serving as head.<sup id="cite_ref-kapa156_168-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kapa156-168">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mmi-mec_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mmi-mec-169">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Taksim_Square_2012.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Taksim_Square_2012.jpg/220px-Taksim_Square_2012.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Taksim_Square_2012.jpg/330px-Taksim_Square_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Taksim_Square_2012.jpg/440px-Taksim_Square_2012.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1063" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Taksim_Square_2012.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A view of <a href="/wiki/Taksim_Square" title="Taksim Square">Taksim Square</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Republic_Monument" title="Republic Monument">Republic Monument</a> (1928) designed by Italian sculptor <a href="/wiki/Pietro_Canonica" title="Pietro Canonica">Pietro Canonica</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>District councils are chiefly responsible for waste management and construction projects within their respective districts. They each maintain their own budgets, although the metropolitan mayor reserves the right to review district decisions. One-fifth of all district council members, including the district mayors, also represent their districts in the Municipal Council.<sup id="cite_ref-kapa1535_166-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kapa1535-166">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> All members of the district councils and the Municipal Council, including the metropolitan mayor, are elected to five-year terms.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> Representing the <a href="/wiki/Justice_and_Development_Party_(Turkey)" title="Justice and Development Party (Turkey)">Justice and Development Party</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mevl%C3%BCt_Uysal" title="Mevl\xc3\xbct Uysal">Mevl\xc3\xbct Uysal</a> has been the <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_Istanbul" title="List of mayors of Istanbul">Mayor of Istanbul</a> since September 28, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>With the Istanbul Metropolitan Municipality and Istanbul Province having equivalent jurisdictions, few responsibilities remain for the provincial government. Similar to the MMI, the Istanbul Special Provincial Administration has a governor, a democratically elected decision-making body\xe2\x80\x94the Provincial Parliament\xe2\x80\x94and an appointed Executive Committee. Mirroring the executive committee at the municipal level, the Provincial Executive Committee includes a secretary-general and leaders of departments that advise the Provincial Parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-mmi-mec_169-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mmi-mec-169">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> The Provincial Administration\'s duties are largely limited to the building and maintenance of schools, residences, government buildings, and roads, and the promotion of arts, culture, and nature conservation.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Vasip_%C5%9Eahin" title="Vasip \xc5\x9eahin">Vasip \xc5\x9eahin</a> has been the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Governors_of_Istanbul_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Governors of Istanbul Province">Governor of Istanbul Province</a> since September 25, 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Istanbul&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Turkey" title="Demographics of Turkey">Demographics of Turkey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Istanbul_Province" title="Istanbul Province">Istanbul Province</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a id="cite_ref-pop-figures_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pop-figures-70">&#91;d&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:IstanbulGrowth1975and2011.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/IstanbulGrowth1975and2011.png/220px-IstanbulGrowth1975and2011.png" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/IstanbulGrowth1975and2011.png/330px-IstanbulGrowth1975and2011.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/IstanbulGrowth1975and2011.png/440px-IstanbulGrowth1975and2011.png 2x" data-file-width="722" data-file-height="961" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:IstanbulGrowth1975and2011.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Two maps comparing the size of urban areas in Istanbul (indicated as the grey zones) in 1975 and 2011.</div></div></div>\n<p>Throughout most of its history, Istanbul has ranked among the largest cities in the world. By 500 CE, Constantinople had somewhere between 400,000 and 500,000 people, edging out its predecessor, Rome, for <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_cities_throughout_history" title="List of largest cities throughout history">world\'s largest city</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> Constantinople jostled with other major historical cities, such as <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chang%27an" title="Chang&#39;an">Chang\'an</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kaifeng" title="Kaifeng">Kaifeng</a> and <a href="/wiki/Merv" title="Merv">Merv</a> for the position of <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_cities_throughout_history" title="List of largest cities throughout history">world\'s most populous city</a> until the 12th century. It never returned to being the world\'s largest, but remained <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_European_cities_in_history" title="List of largest European cities in history">Europe\'s largest city</a> from 1500 to 1750, when it was surpassed by <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cha463_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cha463-177">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Statistical_Institute" title="Turkish Statistical Institute">Turkish Statistical Institute</a> estimates that the population of <a href="/wiki/Istanbul_Province" title="Istanbul Province">Istanbul Metropolitan Municipality</a> was 14,377,019 at the end of 2014, hosting <span class="nowrap">19 percent</span> of the country\'s population.<sup id="cite_ref-Population_of_Turkey_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Population_of_Turkey-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Then about 97\xe2\x80\x9398% of the inhabitants of the metropolitan municipality were within city limits, up from 89% in 2007<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> and 61% in 1980.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> 64.9% of the residents live on the <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">European</a> side and 35.1% on the <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asian</a> side.<sup id="cite_ref-ist_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ist-180">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> While the city ranks as the world\'s <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_proper_by_population" title="List of cities proper by population">5th</a>-largest city proper, it drops to the <a href="/wiki/List_of_urban_areas_by_population" title="List of urban areas by population">24th</a> place as an urban area and to the <a href="/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_by_population" title="List of metropolitan areas by population">18th</a> place as a metro area because the city limits are roughly equivalent to the agglomeration. Today, it forms one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_in_Europe" title="List of metropolitan areas in Europe">largest urban agglomerations in Europe</a>, alongside <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-un-agg_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-un-agg-183">&#91;e&#93;</a></sup> The city\'s annual population growth of <span class="nowrap">3.45 percent</span> ranks as the highest among the seventy-eight largest metropolises in the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development</a>. The high population growth mirrors an urbanization trend across the country, as the second and third fastest-growing OECD metropolises are the Turkish cities of <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0zmir" title="\xc4\xb0zmir">\xc4\xb0zmir</a> and Ankara.<sup id="cite_ref-oecd_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oecd-20">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Istiklal_busy_afternoon.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Istiklal_busy_afternoon.JPG/220px-Istiklal_busy_afternoon.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Istiklal_busy_afternoon.JPG/330px-Istiklal_busy_afternoon.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Istiklal_busy_afternoon.JPG/440px-Istiklal_busy_afternoon.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4752" data-file-height="3168" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Istiklal_busy_afternoon.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/%C4%B0stiklal_Avenue" title="\xc4\xb0stiklal Avenue">\xc4\xb0stiklal Avenue</a> is visited by nearly 3 million people on weekend days.</div></div></div>\n<p>Istanbul experienced especially rapid growth during the second half of the 20th century, with its population increasing tenfold between 1950 and 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-tu224_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tu224-15">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> This growth in population comes, in part, from an expansion of city limits\xe2\x80\x94particularly between 1980 and 1985, when the number of Istanbulites nearly doubled.<sup id="cite_ref-mmi-history_98-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mmi-history-98">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> The remarkable growth was, and still is, largely fueled by migrants from eastern Turkey seeking employment and improved living conditions. The number of residents of Istanbul originating from seven northern and eastern provinces is greater than the populations of their entire respective provinces; <a href="/wiki/Sivas_Province" title="Sivas Province">Sivas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kastamonu_Province" title="Kastamonu Province">Kastamonu</a> each account for more than half a million residents of Istanbul.<sup id="cite_ref-ecoc-popdem_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ecoc-popdem-16">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Istanbul\'s foreign population, by comparison, is very small, 42,228 residents in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> Only <span class="nowrap">28 percent</span> of the city\'s residents are originally from Istanbul.<sup id="cite_ref-konda_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-konda-185">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> The most densely populated areas tend to lie to the northwest, west, and southwest of the city center, on the European side; the most densely populated district on the Asian side is <a href="/wiki/%C3%9Csk%C3%BCdar" title="\xc3\x9csk\xc3\xbcdar">\xc3\x9csk\xc3\xbcdar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ecoc-popdem_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ecoc-popdem-16">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_and_ethnic_groups">Religious and ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Istanbul&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Religious and ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Istanbul" title="Religion in Istanbul">Religion in Istanbul</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Assyrians_in_Turkey" class="mw-redirect" title="Assyrians in Turkey">Assyrians in Turkey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kurds_in_Turkey" title="Kurds in Turkey">Kurds in Turkey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bosniaks_in_Turkey" title="Bosniaks in Turkey">Bosniaks in Turkey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greeks_in_Turkey" title="Greeks in Turkey">Greeks in Turkey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armenians_in_Turkey" title="Armenians in Turkey">Armenians in Turkey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jews_in_Turkey" class="mw-redirect" title="Jews in Turkey">Jews in Turkey</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Albanians_in_Turkey" title="Albanians in Turkey">Albanians in Turkey</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Greeks_in_Istanbul_1844_1997.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Greeks_in_Istanbul_1844_1997.png/300px-Greeks_in_Istanbul_1844_1997.png" width="300" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Greeks_in_Istanbul_1844_1997.png/450px-Greeks_in_Istanbul_1844_1997.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Greeks_in_Istanbul_1844_1997.png/600px-Greeks_in_Istanbul_1844_1997.png 2x" data-file-width="878" data-file-height="416" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Greeks_in_Istanbul_1844_1997.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Greek population in Istanbul and percentages of the city population (1844\xe2\x80\x931997). The <a href="/wiki/Population_exchange_between_Greece_and_Turkey" title="Population exchange between Greece and Turkey">1923 population exchange between Greece and Turkey</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Varl%C4%B1k_Vergisi" title="Varl\xc4\xb1k Vergisi">1942 wealth tax</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Istanbul_pogrom" title="Istanbul pogrom">Istanbul pogrom</a> in 1955 contributed to the sharp decrease of the Greek community.</div></div></div>\n<p>Istanbul has been a cosmopolitan city throughout much of its history, but it has become more homogenized since the end of the Ottoman Empire. The vast majority of people across Turkey, and in Istanbul, are <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslim</a>, and more specifically members of the <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni</a> branch of <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>. Most Sunnis follow the <a href="/wiki/Hanafi" title="Hanafi">Hanafi</a> school of Islamic thought, although approximately <span class="nowrap">10 percent</span> of Sunnis follow the <a href="/wiki/Shafi%27i" class="mw-redirect" title="Shafi&#39;i">Shafi\'i</a> school. The largest non-Sunni Muslim sect, accounting for <span class="nowrap">4.5 million</span> Turks, is the <a href="/wiki/Alevi" class="mw-redirect" title="Alevi">Alevis</a>; a third of all Alevis in the country live in Istanbul.<sup id="cite_ref-konda_185-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-konda-185">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> Mystic movements, like <a href="/wiki/Sufism" title="Sufism">Sufism</a>, were officially banned after the establishment of the Turkish Republic, but they still boast numerous followers.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Ecumenical_Patriarch_of_Constantinople" title="Ecumenical Patriarch of Constantinople">Patriarch of Constantinople</a> has been designated Ecumenical Patriarch since the sixth century, and has subsequently come to be widely regarded as the leader of the world\'s <span class="nowrap">300 million</span> <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Orthodox Christians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> Since 1601, the Patriarchate has been based in Istanbul\'s <a href="/wiki/Church_of_St._George,_Istanbul" class="mw-redirect" title="Church of St. George, Istanbul">Church of St. George</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> Into the 19th century, the Christians of Istanbul tended to be either <a href="/wiki/Greek_Orthodox_Church" title="Greek Orthodox Church">Greek Orthodox</a> or members of the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Apostolic_Church" title="Armenian Apostolic Church">Armenian Apostolic Church</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> The headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Orthodox_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish Orthodox Church">Turkish Orthodox Church</a> are located in the city. Because of events during the 20th century\xe2\x80\x94including the <a href="/wiki/Population_exchange_between_Greece_and_Turkey" title="Population exchange between Greece and Turkey">1923 population exchange</a> between Greece and Turkey, a <a href="/wiki/Varl%C4%B1k_Vergisi" title="Varl\xc4\xb1k Vergisi">1942 wealth tax</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Istanbul_riots" class="mw-redirect" title="Istanbul riots">1955 Istanbul riots</a>\xe2\x80\x94the Greek population, originally centered in <a href="/wiki/Fener" title="Fener">Fener</a> and <a href="/wiki/Samatya" title="Samatya">Samatya</a>, has decreased substantially. At the start of the 21st century, Istanbul\'s Greek population numbered 3,000 (down from 130,000 in 1923 and 260,000 according to the Ottoman Census of 1910 of 850,000 total).<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> There are today between 50,000 and <span class="nowrap">90,000</span> <a href="/wiki/Armenians_in_Istanbul" title="Armenians in Istanbul">Armenians in Istanbul</a>, down from about 164,000 in 1913 (partly due to the Armenian Genocide) according to the Ottoman Census.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St._Anthony_of_Padua_Church_in_Istanbul_06.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/St._Anthony_of_Padua_Church_in_Istanbul_06.JPG/220px-St._Anthony_of_Padua_Church_in_Istanbul_06.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/St._Anthony_of_Padua_Church_in_Istanbul_06.JPG/330px-St._Anthony_of_Padua_Church_in_Istanbul_06.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/St._Anthony_of_Padua_Church_in_Istanbul_06.JPG/440px-St._Anthony_of_Padua_Church_in_Istanbul_06.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St._Anthony_of_Padua_Church_in_Istanbul_06.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Church_of_St._Anthony_of_Padua,_Istanbul" title="Church of St. Anthony of Padua, Istanbul">Church of St. Anthony of Padua</a> on <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0stiklal_Avenue" title="\xc4\xb0stiklal Avenue">\xc4\xb0stiklal Avenue</a> in <a href="/wiki/Beyo%C4%9Flu" title="Beyo\xc4\x9flu">Beyo\xc4\x9flu</a> (Pera) is the largest Catholic church in Turkey.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%C4%B0stanbul_-_Kamondo_Merdivenleri_-_Mart_2013.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/%C4%B0stanbul_-_Kamondo_Merdivenleri_-_Mart_2013.JPG/220px-%C4%B0stanbul_-_Kamondo_Merdivenleri_-_Mart_2013.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/%C4%B0stanbul_-_Kamondo_Merdivenleri_-_Mart_2013.JPG/330px-%C4%B0stanbul_-_Kamondo_Merdivenleri_-_Mart_2013.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/%C4%B0stanbul_-_Kamondo_Merdivenleri_-_Mart_2013.JPG/440px-%C4%B0stanbul_-_Kamondo_Merdivenleri_-_Mart_2013.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%C4%B0stanbul_-_Kamondo_Merdivenleri_-_Mart_2013.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/House_of_Camondo" title="House of Camondo">Camondo</a> Steps at <a href="/wiki/Bankalar_Caddesi" title="Bankalar Caddesi">Bankalar Caddesi</a> (<i>Banks Street</i>) in <a href="/wiki/Galata" title="Galata">Galata</a>, constructed by Ottoman-Venetian Jewish banker <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Salomon_Camondo" title="Abraham Salomon Camondo">Abraham Salomon Camondo</a>, c. 1870\xe2\x80\x931880.</div></div></div>\n<p>The largest ethnic minority in Istanbul is the <a href="/wiki/Kurdish_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Kurdish people">Kurdish</a> community, originating from eastern and southeastern Turkey. Although the Kurdish presence in the city dates back to the early Ottoman period,<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> the influx of Kurds into the city has accelerated since the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Kurdish%E2%80%93Turkish_conflict" class="mw-redirect" title="Kurdish\xe2\x80\x93Turkish conflict">Kurdish\xe2\x80\x93Turkish conflict</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Kurdistan_Workers%27_Party" title="Kurdistan Workers&#39; Party">PKK</a> (i.e. since the late 1970s).<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> About two to three million residents of Istanbul are Kurdish, meaning there are more Kurds in Istanbul than in any other city in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Nachmani2003_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nachmani2003-195">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-KONDA2006_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KONDA2006-196">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-KONDA2008_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KONDA2008-197">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Radikal2008_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Radikal2008-198">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bird2007_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bird2007-199">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> There are other significant ethnic minorities as well, the <a href="/wiki/Bosniaks" title="Bosniaks">Bosniaks</a> are the main people of an entire district \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Bayrampa%C5%9Fa" title="Bayrampa\xc5\x9fa">Bayrampa\xc5\x9fa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> The neighborhood of <a href="/wiki/Balat_(Istanbul)" class="mw-redirect" title="Balat (Istanbul)">Balat</a> used to be home to a sizable <a href="/wiki/Sephardi_Jews" title="Sephardi Jews">Sephardi Jewish</a> community, first formed after their expulsion from Spain in 1492.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Romaniotes" class="mw-redirect" title="Romaniotes">Romaniotes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ashkenazi_Jews" title="Ashkenazi Jews">Ashkenazi Jews</a> resided in Istanbul even before the Sephardim, but their proportion has since dwindled; today, <span class="nowrap">1 percent</span> of Istanbul\'s Jews are Ashkenazi.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> In large part due to emigration to <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>, the Jewish population nationwide dropped from 100,000 in 1950 to 18,000 in 2005, with the majority of them living in either Istanbul or \xc4\xb0zmir.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Levantines_(Latin_Christians)" class="mw-redirect" title="Levantines (Latin Christians)">Levantines</a>, Latin Christians who settled in Galata during the Ottoman period, played a seminal role in shaping the culture and architecture of Istanbul during the 19th and early 20th centuries; their population has dwindled, but they remain in the city in small numbers.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> From the increase in mutual cooperation between Turkey and several African States like Somalia and Djibouti, several young students and workers have been migrating to Istanbul in search of better education and employment opportunities. There is also a small Nigerian, Congolese and Cameroonian and North African community present.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Istanbul&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="infobox vcard" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;padding-top:0; padding-bottom:0;"><div style="padding-top:0.3em; padding-bottom:0.3em; border-top:2px solid #000099; border-bottom:2px solid #000099; line-height: 1;"><span class="fn org">\xc4\xb0stanbul district Municipalities<br /><span style="font-size:85%;"><a href="/wiki/Turkish_local_elections,_2014" title="Turkish local elections, 2014">Turkish local elections, 2014</a></span><br /><a href="/wiki/File:%C4%B0stanbul_2014.png" class="image"><img alt="\xc4\xb0stanbul 2014.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/%C4%B0stanbul_2014.png/220px-%C4%B0stanbul_2014.png" width="220" height="116" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/%C4%B0stanbul_2014.png/330px-%C4%B0stanbul_2014.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/%C4%B0stanbul_2014.png/440px-%C4%B0stanbul_2014.png 2x" data-file-width="789" data-file-height="417" /></a></span></div></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="line-height:1.3em;"><a href="/wiki/Justice_and_Development_Party_(Turkey)" title="Justice and Development Party (Turkey)">AK Party</a></th><td style="line-height:1.3em;">\n<div style="width: 100px;"><span class="nowrap">25 / 39</span><div role="img" style="box-sizing: border-box; border: 1px solid #aaa; height: 1.15em; position: relative;"><div style="background-color: #fdc400; width: 64%; height: 100%;"></div></div></div>\n</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="line-height:1.3em;"><a href="/wiki/Republican_People%27s_Party_(Turkey)" title="Republican People&#39;s Party (Turkey)">CHP</a></th><td style="line-height:1.3em;">\n<div style="width: 100px;"><span class="nowrap">14 / 39</span><div role="img" style="box-sizing: border-box; border: 1px solid #aaa; height: 1.15em; position: relative;"><div style="background-color: #cc0000; width: 36%; height: 100%;"></div></div></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<table class="infobox vcard" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;padding-top:0; padding-bottom:0;"><div style="padding-top:0.3em; padding-bottom:0.3em; border-top:2px solid #000099; border-bottom:2px solid #000099; line-height: 1;"><span class="fn org">Members of Parliament for \xc4\xb0stanbul<br /><span style="font-size:85%;"><a href="/wiki/Turkish_general_election,_November_2015" title="Turkish general election, November 2015">Turkish general election, November 2015</a></span><br /><a href="/wiki/File:%C4%B0stanbul2015Kas%C4%B1m.png" class="image"><img alt="\xc4\xb0stanbul2015Kas\xc4\xb1m.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/%C4%B0stanbul2015Kas%C4%B1m.png/220px-%C4%B0stanbul2015Kas%C4%B1m.png" width="220" height="116" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/%C4%B0stanbul2015Kas%C4%B1m.png/330px-%C4%B0stanbul2015Kas%C4%B1m.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/%C4%B0stanbul2015Kas%C4%B1m.png/440px-%C4%B0stanbul2015Kas%C4%B1m.png 2x" data-file-width="789" data-file-height="417" /></a></span></div></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="line-height:1.3em;"><a href="/wiki/Justice_and_Development_Party_(Turkey)" title="Justice and Development Party (Turkey)">AK Party</a></th><td style="line-height:1.3em;">\n<div style="width: 100px;"><span class="nowrap">46 / 88</span><div role="img" style="box-sizing: border-box; border: 1px solid #aaa; height: 1.15em; position: relative;"><div style="background-color: #fdc400; width: 52%; height: 100%;"></div></div></div>\n</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="line-height:1.3em;"><a href="/wiki/Republican_People%27s_Party_(Turkey)" title="Republican People&#39;s Party (Turkey)">CHP</a></th><td style="line-height:1.3em;">\n<div style="width: 100px;"><span class="nowrap">28 / 88</span><div role="img" style="box-sizing: border-box; border: 1px solid #aaa; height: 1.15em; position: relative;"><div style="background-color: #cc0000; width: 32%; height: 100%;"></div></div></div>\n</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="line-height:1.3em;"><a href="/wiki/Peoples%27_Democratic_Party_(Turkey)" title="Peoples&#39; Democratic Party (Turkey)">HDP</a></th><td style="line-height:1.3em;">\n<div style="width: 100px;"><span class="nowrap">7 / 88</span><div role="img" style="box-sizing: border-box; border: 1px solid #aaa; height: 1.15em; position: relative;"><div style="background-color: #91007B; width: 8%; height: 100%;"></div></div></div>\n</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="line-height:1.3em;"><a href="/wiki/Nationalist_Movement_Party" title="Nationalist Movement Party">MHP</a></th><td style="line-height:1.3em;">\n<div style="width: 100px;"><span class="nowrap">7 / 88</span><div role="img" style="box-sizing: border-box; border: 1px solid #aaa; height: 1.15em; position: relative;"><div style="background-color: #870000; width: 8%; height: 100%;"></div></div></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Istanbul has voted for the winning party in general elections since 1995. Since 2002, the right-wing <a href="/wiki/Justice_and_Development_Party_(Turkey)" title="Justice and Development Party (Turkey)">Justice and Development Party</a> (AKP) has won pluralities in every general and local election. The city\'s electorate has also voted for the AKP government\'s constitutional reforms proposed during the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_constitutional_referendum,_2007" title="Turkish constitutional referendum, 2007">2007</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turkish_constitutional_referendum,_2010" title="Turkish constitutional referendum, 2010">2010</a> constitutional referenda. Turkish President and former AKP Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Recep_Tayyip_Erdo%C4%9Fan" title="Recep Tayyip Erdo\xc4\x9fan">Recep Tayyip Erdo\xc4\x9fan</a> was elected <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_%C4%B0stanbul" class="mw-redirect" title="List of mayors of \xc4\xb0stanbul">Mayor of \xc4\xb0stanbul</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_local_elections,_1994" title="Turkish local elections, 1994">1994 local elections</a> as the Islamist <a href="/wiki/Welfare_Party" title="Welfare Party">Welfare Party</a> candidate with 25.1% of the vote, winning due to a vote split between the mainstream centrist parties. Conservative parties traditionally find support in older districts with high population densities such as <a href="/wiki/Ba%C4%9Fc%C4%B1lar" title="Ba\xc4\x9fc\xc4\xb1lar">Ba\xc4\x9fc\xc4\xb1lar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fatih" title="Fatih">Fatih</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sultanbeyli" title="Sultanbeyli">Sultanbeyli</a> and <a href="/wiki/Esenler" title="Esenler">Esenler</a>. The opposition <a href="/wiki/Kemalism" title="Kemalism">Kemalist</a> center-left <a href="/wiki/Republican_People%27s_Party_(Turkey)" title="Republican People&#39;s Party (Turkey)">Republican People\'s Party</a> (CHP), currently the second major political force in both \xc4\xb0stanbul and the country, gets most of its support from more rural districts such as <a href="/wiki/Silivri" title="Silivri">Silivri</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C3%87atalca" title="\xc3\x87atalca">\xc3\x87atalca</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sar%C4%B1yer" title="Sar\xc4\xb1yer">Sar\xc4\xb1yer</a>. Urban districts such as <a href="/wiki/Be%C5%9Fikta%C5%9F" title="Be\xc5\x9fikta\xc5\x9f">Be\xc5\x9fikta\xc5\x9f</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bak%C4%B1rk%C3%B6y" title="Bak\xc4\xb1rk\xc3\xb6y">Bak\xc4\xb1rk\xc3\xb6y</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C5%9Ei%C5%9Fli" title="\xc5\x9ei\xc5\x9fli">\xc5\x9ei\xc5\x9fli</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kad%C4%B1k%C3%B6y" title="Kad\xc4\xb1k\xc3\xb6y">Kad\xc4\xb1k\xc3\xb6y</a> have returned strong support for the CHP in past elections. The CHP are generally strongest in the west, where newer residential developments are taking place. \xc4\xb0stanbul has 39 districts, more than any other <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Turkey" title="Provinces of Turkey">province in Turkey</a>. Since \xc4\xb0stanbul is Turkey\'s largest city and has usually voted in the same way as the country as a whole, it is largely perceived in Turkish politics that the winning party of an election is essentially decided by \xc4\xb0stanbul\'s electorate. Political parties thus allocate substantial amounts of electoral campaign funds and to winning control of the \xc4\xb0stanbul Metropolitan Municipality. Due to its electoral importance, \xc4\xb0stanbul has reported the largest and most serious cases of electoral fraud in recent elections, including the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_local_elections,_2014" title="Turkish local elections, 2014">2014 local elections</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Istanbul_Municipality_City_Hall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Istanbul_Municipality_City_Hall.jpg/220px-Istanbul_Municipality_City_Hall.jpg" width="220" height="79" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Istanbul_Municipality_City_Hall.jpg/330px-Istanbul_Municipality_City_Hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Istanbul_Municipality_City_Hall.jpg/440px-Istanbul_Municipality_City_Hall.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2433" data-file-height="874" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Istanbul_Municipality_City_Hall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Istanbul Metropolitan Municipality building in the <a href="/wiki/Fatih" title="Fatih">Fatih</a> district</div></div></div>\n<p>The incumbent mayor of the city is <a href="/wiki/Mevl%C3%BCt_Uysal" title="Mevl\xc3\xbct Uysal">Mevl\xc3\xbct Uysal</a> of the AKP, who was elected after the resignation of the previous mayor, <a href="/wiki/Kadir_Topba%C5%9F" title="Kadir Topba\xc5\x9f">Kadir Topba\xc5\x9f</a>. The leader of the CHP and parliamentary opposition, <a href="/wiki/Kemal_K%C4%B1l%C4%B1%C3%A7daro%C4%9Flu" title="Kemal K\xc4\xb1l\xc4\xb1\xc3\xa7daro\xc4\x9flu">Kemal K\xc4\xb1l\xc4\xb1\xc3\xa7daro\xc4\x9flu</a>, ran against Topba\xc5\x9f in the 2009 local elections. He is currently a <a href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Member of Parliament">Member of Parliament</a> for \xc4\xb0stanbul. Between 2007 and 2014, Prime Minister Recep Tayyip Erdo\xc4\x9fan was also an MP for \xc4\xb0stanbul. For general elections, the city is divided into 3 electoral districts and returns 85 MPs to the <a href="/wiki/Grand_National_Assembly" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand National Assembly">Turkish parliament</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_presidential_election,_2014" title="Turkish presidential election, 2014">2014 presidential election</a>, 49.83% of the city\'s electorate voted for AKP candidate Recep Tayyip Erdo\xc4\x9fan. Although Erdo\xc4\x9fan won the most votes in \xc4\xb0stanbul, his failure to win above 50% was seen as significant. Opposition candidate <a href="/wiki/Ekmeleddin_%C4%B0hsano%C4%9Flu" title="Ekmeleddin \xc4\xb0hsano\xc4\x9flu">Ekmeleddin \xc4\xb0hsano\xc4\x9flu</a> came second with 41.08% and the <a href="/wiki/Peoples%27_Democratic_Party_(Turkey)" title="Peoples&#39; Democratic Party (Turkey)">HDP</a> pro-Kurdish and left-wing candidate <a href="/wiki/Selahattin_Demirta%C5%9F" title="Selahattin Demirta\xc5\x9f">Selahattin Demirta\xc5\x9f</a> won a substantial 9.09%.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> In 2013 and 2014, <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_protests_in_Turkey" class="mw-redirect" title="2013\xe2\x80\x9314 protests in Turkey">large-scale anti-AKP government protests</a> began in \xc4\xb0stanbul and spread throughout the nation.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Istanbul&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Istanbul" title="Economy of Istanbul">Economy of Istanbul</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:758px;">\n<div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Maslak_bussines_center.jpg" class="image" title="A panorama of Maslak business district, situated on the European side of the city, near Levent."><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Maslak_bussines_center.jpg/750px-Maslak_bussines_center.jpg" width="750" height="178" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Maslak_bussines_center.jpg/1125px-Maslak_bussines_center.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/ba/Maslak_bussines_center.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1279" data-file-height="303" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Maslak_bussines_center.jpg" title="File:Maslak bussines center.jpg"> </a></div> <center>A panorama of <a href="/wiki/Maslak" title="Maslak">Maslak</a> business district, situated on the European side of the city, near <a href="/wiki/Levent" title="Levent">Levent</a>.</center></div>\n</div></div>\n<p>With a <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">PPP-adjusted</a> <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> of <span class="nowrap">US$301.1 billion</span>, Istanbul <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_by_GDP" title="List of cities by GDP">ranked 29th</a> among the world\'s urban areas in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> Since the mid-1990s, Istanbul\'s economy has been one of the fastest-growing among <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a> metro-regions.<sup id="cite_ref-oecd_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oecd-20">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Istanbul is responsible for <span class="nowrap">27 percent</span> of Turkey\'s GDP, with <span class="nowrap">20 percent</span> of the country\'s industrial labor force residing in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-oecd_20-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oecd-20">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-urge_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-urge-216">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> Its GDP per capita and <a href="/wiki/Productivity" title="Productivity">productivity</a> are greater than their national averages by <span class="nowrap">70 percent</span> and <span class="nowrap">50 percent</span>, respectively, owing in part to the focus on high-<a href="/wiki/Value_added" title="Value added">value-added</a> activities.
