With its high population and significant contribution to the Turkish economy, Istanbul is responsible for two-fifths of the nation\'s tax revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-oecd_20-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oecd-20">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> That includes the taxes of 37 <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US-dollar</a> billionaires based in Istanbul, the fifth-highest number among cities around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%C4%B0stanbul_view_from_%C4%B0stanbul_Sapphire_observation_deck_Aug_2014,_p9.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Skyline of a portion of the city, including several skyscrapers interspersed among low- and mid-rises, several historic buildings, parks and hilly terrain, and the waterway known as Bosphorus" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/%C4%B0stanbul_view_from_%C4%B0stanbul_Sapphire_observation_deck_Aug_2014%2C_p9.JPG/220px-%C4%B0stanbul_view_from_%C4%B0stanbul_Sapphire_observation_deck_Aug_2014%2C_p9.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/%C4%B0stanbul_view_from_%C4%B0stanbul_Sapphire_observation_deck_Aug_2014%2C_p9.JPG/330px-%C4%B0stanbul_view_from_%C4%B0stanbul_Sapphire_observation_deck_Aug_2014%2C_p9.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/%C4%B0stanbul_view_from_%C4%B0stanbul_Sapphire_observation_deck_Aug_2014%2C_p9.JPG/440px-%C4%B0stanbul_view_from_%C4%B0stanbul_Sapphire_observation_deck_Aug_2014%2C_p9.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%C4%B0stanbul_view_from_%C4%B0stanbul_Sapphire_observation_deck_Aug_2014,_p9.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A view of <a href="/wiki/Levent" title="Levent">Levent</a>, one of the main business districts in Istanbul and home to the city\'s tallest buildings.</div></div></div>\n<p>As expected for a city of its size, Istanbul has a diverse industrial economy, producing commodities as varied as olive oil, tobacco, vehicles, and electronics.<sup id="cite_ref-urge_216-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-urge-216">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> Despite having a focus on high-value-added work, its low-value-added manufacturing sector is substantial, representing just <span class="nowrap">26 percent</span> of Istanbul\'s GDP, but four-fifths of the city\'s total exports.<sup id="cite_ref-oecd_20-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oecd-20">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> In 2005, companies based in Istanbul produced exports worth <span class="nowrap">$41.4 billion</span> and received imports totaling <span class="nowrap">$69.9 billion</span>; these figures were equivalent to <span class="nowrap">57 percent</span> and <span class="nowrap">60 percent</span>, respectively, of the national totals.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Istanbul is home to <a href="/wiki/Borsa_Istanbul" title="Borsa Istanbul">Borsa Istanbul</a>, the sole <a href="/wiki/Exchange_(organized_market)" title="Exchange (organized market)">exchange</a> entity of Turkey, which combined the former Istanbul Stock Exchange, the Istanbul Gold Exchange, and the Derivatives Exchange of Turkey.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> The former <a href="/wiki/Istanbul_Stock_Exchange" class="mw-redirect" title="Istanbul Stock Exchange">Istanbul Stock Exchange</a> was originally established as the Ottoman Stock Exchange in 1866.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> During the 19th and early 20th centuries, <a href="/wiki/Bankalar_Caddesi" title="Bankalar Caddesi">Bankalar Caddesi</a> (Banks Street) in Galata was the financial center of the Ottoman Empire, where the Ottoman Stock Exchange was located.<sup id="cite_ref-OBM_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OBM-221">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> Bankalar Caddesi continued to be Istanbul\'s main financial district until the 1990s, when most Turkish banks began moving their headquarters to the modern central business districts of <a href="/wiki/Levent" title="Levent">Levent</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maslak" title="Maslak">Maslak</a>. In 1995, the Istanbul Stock Exchange (now Borsa Istanbul) moved to its current building in the <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0stinye" title="\xc4\xb0stinye">\xc4\xb0stinye</a> quarter of the <a href="/wiki/Sar%C4%B1yer" title="Sar\xc4\xb1yer">Sar\xc4\xb1yer</a> district.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> A new <a href="/wiki/Central_business_district" title="Central business district">central business district</a> is also under construction in <a href="/wiki/Ata%C5%9Fehir" title="Ata\xc5\x9fehir">Ata\xc5\x9fehir</a> and will host the headquarters of various Turkish banks and financial institutions upon completion.<sup id="cite_ref-Bloomberg2013_223-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg2013-223">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ships_under_Second_Bosphorus_Bridge_(September_2011).jpg" class="image"><img alt="A pair of large ships sailing on a waterway, with a suspension bridge and hilly terrain in the background." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Ships_under_Second_Bosphorus_Bridge_%28September_2011%29.jpg/220px-Ships_under_Second_Bosphorus_Bridge_%28September_2011%29.jpg" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Ships_under_Second_Bosphorus_Bridge_%28September_2011%29.jpg/330px-Ships_under_Second_Bosphorus_Bridge_%28September_2011%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Ships_under_Second_Bosphorus_Bridge_%28September_2011%29.jpg/440px-Ships_under_Second_Bosphorus_Bridge_%28September_2011%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2157" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ships_under_Second_Bosphorus_Bridge_(September_2011).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>As the only route to the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bosphorus" class="mw-redirect" title="Bosphorus">Bosphorus</a> is one of the busiest waterways in the world.</div></div></div>\n<p>As the only sea route between the oil-rich Black Sea and the Mediterranean, the Bosphorus is one of the busiest waterways in the world; more than <span class="nowrap">200 million</span> tonnes of oil pass through the strait each year, and the traffic on the Bosphorus is three times that on the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> As a result, there have been proposals to build a canal, known as <a href="/wiki/Canal_Istanbul" class="mw-redirect" title="Canal Istanbul">Canal Istanbul</a>, parallel to the strait, on the European side of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> Istanbul has three major shipping ports\xe2\x80\x94the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Haydarpa%C5%9Fa" title="Port of Haydarpa\xc5\x9fa">Port of Haydarpa\xc5\x9fa</a>, the Port of Ambarl\xc4\xb1, and the Port of Zeytinburnu\xe2\x80\x94as well as several smaller ports and oil terminals along the Bosphorus and the Sea of Marmara.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> Haydarpa\xc5\x9fa, situated at the southeastern end of the Bosphorus, was Istanbul\'s largest port until the early 2000s. Shifts in operations to Ambarl\xc4\xb1 since then have left Haydarpa\xc5\x9fa running under capacity and with plans to decommission the port.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> In 2007, Ambarl\xc4\xb1, on the western edge of the urban center, had an annual capacity of <span class="nowrap">1.5 million</span> <a href="/wiki/Twenty-foot_equivalent_unit" title="Twenty-foot equivalent unit">TEUs</a> (compared to 354,000 TEUs at Haydarpa\xc5\x9fa), making it the fourth-largest cargo terminal in the Mediterranean basin.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> The Port of Zeytinburnu is advantaged by its proximity to motorways and <a href="/wiki/Atat%C3%BCrk_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Atat\xc3\xbcrk International Airport">Atat\xc3\xbcrk International Airport</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> and long-term plans for the city call for greater connectivity between all terminals and the road and rail networks.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Istanbul is an increasingly popular tourist destination; whereas just <span class="nowrap">2.4 million</span> foreigners visited the city in 2000, it welcomed <span class="nowrap">12.56 million</span> foreign tourists in 2015, making it the world\'s fifth most-visited city.<sup id="cite_ref-Mastercard_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mastercard-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> Istanbul is Turkey\'s second-largest international gateway, after <a href="/wiki/Antalya" title="Antalya">Antalya</a>, receiving a quarter of the nation\'s foreign tourists. Istanbul\'s tourist industry is concentrated in the European side, with <span class="nowrap">90 percent</span> of the city\'s hotels located there. Low- and mid-range hotels tend to be located on the <a href="/wiki/Sarayburnu" title="Sarayburnu">Sarayburnu</a>; higher-end hotels are primarily located in the entertainment and financial centers north of the Golden Horn. Istanbul\'s seventy museums, the most visited of which are the Topkap\xc4\xb1 Palace Museum and the Hagia Sophia, bring in <span class="nowrap">$30 million</span> in revenue each year. The city\'s environmental master plan also notes that there are <span class="nowrap">17 palaces</span>, <span class="nowrap">64 mosques</span>, and <span class="nowrap">49 churches</span> of historical significance in Istanbul.<sup id="cite_ref-iv&amp;c_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iv&amp;c-234">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Istanbul&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Istanbul" title="Culture of Istanbul">Culture of Istanbul</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%C4%B0stanbul_Arkeoloji_M%C3%BCzeleri_(ana_bina,_Arkeoloji_M%C3%BCzesi)_-_Mart_2013.JPG" class="image"><img alt="The fa\xc3\xa7ade of a masonry building, with four Greek adorning its entrance, under a clear blue sky" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/%C4%B0stanbul_Arkeoloji_M%C3%BCzeleri_%28ana_bina%2C_Arkeoloji_M%C3%BCzesi%29_-_Mart_2013.JPG/220px-%C4%B0stanbul_Arkeoloji_M%C3%BCzeleri_%28ana_bina%2C_Arkeoloji_M%C3%BCzesi%29_-_Mart_2013.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/%C4%B0stanbul_Arkeoloji_M%C3%BCzeleri_%28ana_bina%2C_Arkeoloji_M%C3%BCzesi%29_-_Mart_2013.JPG/330px-%C4%B0stanbul_Arkeoloji_M%C3%BCzeleri_%28ana_bina%2C_Arkeoloji_M%C3%BCzesi%29_-_Mart_2013.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/%C4%B0stanbul_Arkeoloji_M%C3%BCzeleri_%28ana_bina%2C_Arkeoloji_M%C3%BCzesi%29_-_Mart_2013.JPG/440px-%C4%B0stanbul_Arkeoloji_M%C3%BCzeleri_%28ana_bina%2C_Arkeoloji_M%C3%BCzesi%29_-_Mart_2013.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%C4%B0stanbul_Arkeoloji_M%C3%BCzeleri_(ana_bina,_Arkeoloji_M%C3%BCzesi)_-_Mart_2013.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Istanbul_Archaeology_Museums" class="mw-redirect" title="Istanbul Archaeology Museums">Istanbul Archaeology Museums</a>, founded by <a href="/wiki/Osman_Hamdi_Bey" title="Osman Hamdi Bey">Osman Hamdi Bey</a> in 1891, form Turkey\'s oldest modern museum.<sup id="cite_ref-kultur_235-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kultur-235">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>Istanbul was historically known as a cultural hub, but its cultural scene stagnated after the Turkish Republic shifted its focus toward <a href="/wiki/Ankara" title="Ankara">Ankara</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup> The new national government established programs that served to orient Turks toward musical traditions, especially those originating in Europe, but musical institutions and visits by foreign classical artists were primarily centered in the new capital.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> Much of Turkey\'s cultural scene had its roots in Istanbul, and by the 1980s and 1990s Istanbul reemerged globally as a city whose cultural significance is not solely based on its past glory.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Peramuzesi_nighttime.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Peramuzesi_nighttime.jpg/220px-Peramuzesi_nighttime.jpg" width="220" height="231" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Peramuzesi_nighttime.jpg/330px-Peramuzesi_nighttime.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Peramuzesi_nighttime.jpg/440px-Peramuzesi_nighttime.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="2104" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Peramuzesi_nighttime.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Pera_Museum" title="Pera Museum">Pera Museum</a> in <a href="/wiki/Beyo%C4%9Flu" title="Beyo\xc4\x9flu">Beyo\xc4\x9flu</a></div></div></div>\n<p>By the end of the 19th century, Istanbul had established itself as a regional artistic center, with Turkish, European, and Middle Eastern artists flocking to the city. Despite efforts to make Ankara Turkey\'s cultural heart, Istanbul had the country\'s primary institution of art until the 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-gosotu2213_239-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gosotu2213-239">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> When additional universities and art journals were founded in Istanbul during the 1980s, artists formerly based in Ankara moved in.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Beyo%C4%9Flu" title="Beyo\xc4\x9flu">Beyo\xc4\x9flu</a> has been transformed into the artistic center of the city, with young artists and older Turkish artists formerly residing abroad finding footing there. Modern art museums, including <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0stanbul_Modern" title="\xc4\xb0stanbul Modern">\xc4\xb0stanbul Modern</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pera_Museum" title="Pera Museum">Pera Museum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sak%C4%B1p_Sabanc%C4%B1_Museum" title="Sak\xc4\xb1p Sabanc\xc4\xb1 Museum">Sak\xc4\xb1p Sabanc\xc4\xb1 Museum</a> and <a href="/wiki/SantralIstanbul" title="SantralIstanbul">SantralIstanbul</a>, opened in the 2000s to complement the exhibition spaces and auction houses that have already contributed to the cosmopolitan nature of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup> These museums have yet to attain the popularity of older museums on the historic peninsula, including the <a href="/wiki/Istanbul_Archaeology_Museums" class="mw-redirect" title="Istanbul Archaeology Museums">Istanbul Archaeology Museums</a>, which ushered in the era of modern museums in Turkey, and the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_and_Islamic_Arts_Museum" title="Turkish and Islamic Arts Museum">Turkish and Islamic Arts Museum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-iv&amp;c_234-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iv&amp;c-234">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kultur_235-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kultur-235">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%C4%B0stanbul_Modern_February_2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/%C4%B0stanbul_Modern_February_2013.jpg/220px-%C4%B0stanbul_Modern_February_2013.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/%C4%B0stanbul_Modern_February_2013.jpg/330px-%C4%B0stanbul_Modern_February_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/%C4%B0stanbul_Modern_February_2013.jpg/440px-%C4%B0stanbul_Modern_February_2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4338" data-file-height="2440" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%C4%B0stanbul_Modern_February_2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The former building of <a href="/wiki/Istanbul_Modern" class="mw-redirect" title="Istanbul Modern">Istanbul Modern</a>, a museum of contemporary art on the <a href="/wiki/Bosphorus" class="mw-redirect" title="Bosphorus">Bosphorus</a>, is currently being replaced by a new one designed by Italian architect <a href="/wiki/Renzo_Piano" title="Renzo Piano">Renzo Piano</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> The new building is a component of the <i>Galataport</i> project for the renovation of the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Istanbul" title="Port of Istanbul">port of Istanbul</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>The first film screening in Turkey was at <a href="/wiki/Y%C4%B1ld%C4%B1z_Palace" title="Y\xc4\xb1ld\xc4\xb1z Palace">Y\xc4\xb1ld\xc4\xb1z Palace</a> in 1896, a year after the technology publicly debuted in Paris.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup> Movie theaters rapidly cropped up in Beyo\xc4\x9flu, with the greatest concentration of theaters being along the street now known as <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0stiklal_Avenue" title="\xc4\xb0stiklal Avenue">\xc4\xb0stiklal Avenue</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> Istanbul also became the heart of <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Turkey" title="Cinema of Turkey">Turkey\'s nascent film industry</a>, although Turkish films were not consistently developed until the 1950s.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup> Since then, Istanbul has been the most popular location to film Turkish dramas and comedies.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup> The Turkish film industry ramped up in the second half of the century, and with <i><a href="/wiki/Uzak" title="Uzak">Uzak</a></i> (2002) and <i><a href="/wiki/My_Father_and_My_Son" title="My Father and My Son">My Father and My Son</a></i> (2005), both filmed in Istanbul, the nation\'s movies began to see substantial international success.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup> Istanbul and its picturesque skyline have also served as a backdrop for several foreign films, including <i><a href="/wiki/From_Russia_with_Love_(film)" title="From Russia with Love (film)">From Russia with Love</a></i> (1963), <i><a href="/wiki/Topkapi_(film)" title="Topkapi (film)">Topkapi</a></i> (1964), <i><a href="/wiki/The_World_Is_Not_Enough" title="The World Is Not Enough">The World Is Not Enough</a></i> (1999), and <i><a href="/wiki/Mission_Istaanbul" title="Mission Istaanbul">Mission Istaanbul</a></i> (2008).<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Coinciding with this cultural reemergence was the establishment of the Istanbul Festival, which began showcasing a variety of art from Turkey and around the world in 1973. From this flagship festival came the <a href="/wiki/International_Istanbul_Film_Festival" title="International Istanbul Film Festival">International Istanbul Film Festival</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Istanbul_International_Jazz_Festival" title="Istanbul International Jazz Festival">Istanbul International Jazz Festival</a> in the early 1980s. With its focus now solely on music and dance, the Istanbul Festival has been known as the <a href="/wiki/Istanbul_International_Music_Festival" title="Istanbul International Music Festival">Istanbul International Music Festival</a> since 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup> The most prominent of the festivals that evolved from the original Istanbul Festival is the <a href="/wiki/Istanbul_Biennial" title="Istanbul Biennial">Istanbul Biennial</a>, held every two years since 1987. Its early incarnations were aimed at showcasing Turkish visual art, and it has since opened to international artists and risen in prestige to join the elite <a href="/wiki/Biennale" title="Biennale">biennales</a>, alongside the <a href="/wiki/Venice_Biennale" title="Venice Biennale">Venice Biennale</a> and the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Art_Biennial" title="S\xc3\xa3o Paulo Art Biennial">S\xc3\xa3o Paulo Art Biennial</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Leisure_and_entertainment">Leisure and entertainment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Istanbul&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Leisure and entertainment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Grand-Bazaar_Shop.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Goods overflow out of storefronts, leaving a narrow passageway where shoppers move about." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Grand-Bazaar_Shop.jpg/220px-Grand-Bazaar_Shop.jpg" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Grand-Bazaar_Shop.jpg/330px-Grand-Bazaar_Shop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Grand-Bazaar_Shop.jpg/440px-Grand-Bazaar_Shop.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="688" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Grand-Bazaar_Shop.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Grand_Bazaar,_Istanbul" title="Grand Bazaar, Istanbul">Grand Bazaar</a> is one of the largest covered markets in the world.</div></div></div>\n<p>Istanbul has <a href="/wiki/List_of_shopping_malls_in_Istanbul" title="List of shopping malls in Istanbul">numerous shopping centers</a>, from the historic to the modern. The <a href="/wiki/Grand_Bazaar,_Istanbul" title="Grand Bazaar, Istanbul">Grand Bazaar</a>, in operation since 1461, is among the world\'s oldest and largest covered markets.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kos9192_255-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kos9192-255">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mahmutpasha_Bazaar,_Istanbul" title="Mahmutpasha Bazaar, Istanbul">Mahmutpasha Bazaar</a> is an open-air market extending between the Grand Bazaar and the <a href="/wiki/Spice_Bazaar,_Istanbul" class="mw-redirect" title="Spice Bazaar, Istanbul">Egyptian Bazaar</a>, which has been Istanbul\'s major spice market since 1660. <a href="/wiki/Galleria_Atak%C3%B6y" title="Galleria Atak\xc3\xb6y">Galleria Atak\xc3\xb6y</a> ushered in the age of modern shopping malls in Turkey when it opened in 1987.<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> Since then, malls have become major shopping centers outside the historic peninsula. <a href="/wiki/Akmerkez" title="Akmerkez">Akmerkez</a> was awarded the titles of "Europe\'s best" and "World\'s best" shopping mall by the <a href="/wiki/International_Council_of_Shopping_Centers" title="International Council of Shopping Centers">International Council of Shopping Centers</a> in 1995 and 1996; <a href="/wiki/Istanbul_Cevahir" title="Istanbul Cevahir">Istanbul Cevahir</a> has been one of the continent\'s largest since opening in 2005; <a href="/wiki/Kanyon_Shopping_Mall,_Istanbul" class="mw-redirect" title="Kanyon Shopping Mall, Istanbul">Kanyon</a> won the Cityscape Architectural Review Award in the Commercial Built category in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-kos9192_255-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kos9192-255">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0stinye_Park" title="\xc4\xb0stinye Park">\xc4\xb0stinye Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0stinye" title="\xc4\xb0stinye">\xc4\xb0stinye</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zorlu_Center" title="Zorlu Center">Zorlu Center</a> near <a href="/wiki/Levent" title="Levent">Levent</a> are among the newest malls which include the stores of the world\'s top fashion brands. <a href="/wiki/Abdi_%C4%B0pek%C3%A7i_Street" title="Abdi \xc4\xb0pek\xc3\xa7i Street">Abdi \xc4\xb0pek\xc3\xa7i Street</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ni%C5%9Fanta%C5%9F%C4%B1" title="Ni\xc5\x9fanta\xc5\x9f\xc4\xb1">Ni\xc5\x9fanta\xc5\x9f\xc4\xb1</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ba%C4%9Fdat_Avenue" title="Ba\xc4\x9fdat Avenue">Ba\xc4\x9fdat Avenue</a> on the Anatolian side of the city have evolved into high-end shopping districts.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ni%C5%9Fanta%C5%9F%C4%B1_2010-11_Y%C4%B1lba%C5%9F%C4%B1_S%C3%BCslemeleri.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A large tree decorated under the night sky in red and green and surrounded by spotlights, city lights, and mid-rise buildings" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Ni%C5%9Fanta%C5%9F%C4%B1_2010-11_Y%C4%B1lba%C5%9F%C4%B1_S%C3%BCslemeleri.jpg/220px-Ni%C5%9Fanta%C5%9F%C4%B1_2010-11_Y%C4%B1lba%C5%9F%C4%B1_S%C3%BCslemeleri.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Ni%C5%9Fanta%C5%9F%C4%B1_2010-11_Y%C4%B1lba%C5%9F%C4%B1_S%C3%BCslemeleri.jpg/330px-Ni%C5%9Fanta%C5%9F%C4%B1_2010-11_Y%C4%B1lba%C5%9F%C4%B1_S%C3%BCslemeleri.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Ni%C5%9Fanta%C5%9F%C4%B1_2010-11_Y%C4%B1lba%C5%9F%C4%B1_S%C3%BCslemeleri.jpg/440px-Ni%C5%9Fanta%C5%9F%C4%B1_2010-11_Y%C4%B1lba%C5%9F%C4%B1_S%C3%BCslemeleri.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ni%C5%9Fanta%C5%9F%C4%B1_2010-11_Y%C4%B1lba%C5%9F%C4%B1_S%C3%BCslemeleri.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_Eve" title="New Year&#39;s Eve">New Year\'s Eve</a> decorations in <a href="/wiki/Ni%C5%9Fanta%C5%9F%C4%B1" title="Ni\xc5\x9fanta\xc5\x9f\xc4\xb1">Ni\xc5\x9fanta\xc5\x9f\xc4\xb1</a> shopping district</div></div></div>\n<p>Istanbul is famous for its historic <a href="/wiki/Seafood" title="Seafood">seafood</a> restaurants. Many of the city\'s most popular and upscale seafood restaurants line the shores of the <a href="/wiki/Bosphorus" class="mw-redirect" title="Bosphorus">Bosphorus</a> (particularly in neighborhoods like <a href="/wiki/Ortak%C3%B6y" title="Ortak\xc3\xb6y">Ortak\xc3\xb6y</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bebek,_Istanbul" class="mw-redirect" title="Bebek, Istanbul">Bebek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arnavutk%C3%B6y" title="Arnavutk\xc3\xb6y">Arnavutk\xc3\xb6y</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yenik%C3%B6y,_Istanbul" class="mw-redirect" title="Yenik\xc3\xb6y, Istanbul">Yenik\xc3\xb6y</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beylerbeyi" title="Beylerbeyi">Beylerbeyi</a> and <a href="/wiki/%C3%87engelk%C3%B6y" title="\xc3\x87engelk\xc3\xb6y">\xc3\x87engelk\xc3\xb6y</a>). <a href="/wiki/Kumkap%C4%B1" title="Kumkap\xc4\xb1">Kumkap\xc4\xb1</a> along the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Marmara" title="Sea of Marmara">Sea of Marmara</a> has a pedestrian zone that hosts around fifty fish restaurants.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Prince_Islands" title="Prince Islands">Prince Islands</a>, 15 kilometers (9&#160;mi) from the city center, are also popular for their seafood restaurants. Because of their restaurants, historic summer mansions, and tranquil, car-free streets, the Prince Islands are a popular vacation destination among Istanbulites and foreign tourists.<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup> Istanbul is also famous for its sophisticated and elaborately-cooked dishes of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_cuisine" title="Ottoman cuisine">Ottoman cuisine</a>. However, following the influx of immigrants from southeastern and eastern Turkey, which began in the 1960s, the foodscape of the city has drastically changed by the end of the century; with influences of Middle Eastern cuisine such as <a href="/wiki/Kebab" title="Kebab">kebab</a> taking an important place in the food scene. Restaurants featuring foreign cuisines are mainly concentrated in the <a href="/wiki/Beyo%C4%9Flu" title="Beyo\xc4\x9flu">Beyo\xc4\x9flu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Be%C5%9Fikta%C5%9F" title="Be\xc5\x9fikta\xc5\x9f">Be\xc5\x9fikta\xc5\x9f</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C5%9Ei%C5%9Fli" title="\xc5\x9ei\xc5\x9fli">\xc5\x9ei\xc5\x9fli</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kad%C4%B1k%C3%B6y" title="Kad\xc4\xb1k\xc3\xb6y">Kad\xc4\xb1k\xc3\xb6y</a> districts.\n</p><p>Istanbul is famous for its <a href="/wiki/Nightlife" title="Nightlife">nightlife</a>, as well as its historic <a href="/wiki/Tavern" title="Tavern">taverns</a>, a signature characteristic of the city for centuries if not millennia. Along <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0stiklal_Avenue" title="\xc4\xb0stiklal Avenue">\xc4\xb0stiklal Avenue</a> is the <a href="/wiki/%C3%87i%C3%A7ek_Pasaj%C4%B1" title="\xc3\x87i\xc3\xa7ek Pasaj\xc4\xb1">\xc3\x87i\xc3\xa7ek Pasaj\xc4\xb1</a>, now home to winehouses (known as <i>meyhanes</i>), pubs, and restaurants.<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup> \xc4\xb0stiklal Avenue, originally famous for its taverns, has shifted toward shopping, but the nearby Nevizade Street is still lined with winehouses and pubs.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> Some other neighborhoods around \xc4\xb0stiklal Avenue have recently been revamped to cater to Beyo\xc4\x9flu\'s nightlife, with formerly commercial streets now lined with pubs, cafes, and restaurants playing live music.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup> Other focal points for Istanbul\'s nightlife include <a href="/wiki/Ni%C5%9Fanta%C5%9F%C4%B1" title="Ni\xc5\x9fanta\xc5\x9f\xc4\xb1">Ni\xc5\x9fanta\xc5\x9f\xc4\xb1</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ortak%C3%B6y" title="Ortak\xc3\xb6y">Ortak\xc3\xb6y</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bebek,_Istanbul" class="mw-redirect" title="Bebek, Istanbul">Bebek</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kad%C4%B1k%C3%B6y" title="Kad\xc4\xb1k\xc3\xb6y">Kad\xc4\xb1k\xc3\xb6y</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Istanbul&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_sport_facilities_in_Istanbul" title="List of sport facilities in Istanbul">List of sport facilities in Istanbul</a></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px"><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Atat%C3%BCrk_Olimpiyat.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Atat%C3%BCrk_Olimpiyat.jpg/200px-Atat%C3%BCrk_Olimpiyat.jpg" width="200" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Atat%C3%BCrk_Olimpiyat.jpg/300px-Atat%C3%BCrk_Olimpiyat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Atat%C3%BCrk_Olimpiyat.jpg/400px-Atat%C3%BCrk_Olimpiyat.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Ali_Sami_Yen_Spor_Kompleksi_T%C3%BCrk_Telekom_Arena2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Ali_Sami_Yen_Spor_Kompleksi_T%C3%BCrk_Telekom_Arena2.jpg/200px-Ali_Sami_Yen_Spor_Kompleksi_T%C3%BCrk_Telekom_Arena2.jpg" width="200" height="61" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Ali_Sami_Yen_Spor_Kompleksi_T%C3%BCrk_Telekom_Arena2.jpg/300px-Ali_Sami_Yen_Spor_Kompleksi_T%C3%BCrk_Telekom_Arena2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Ali_Sami_Yen_Spor_Kompleksi_T%C3%BCrk_Telekom_Arena2.jpg/400px-Ali_Sami_Yen_Spor_Kompleksi_T%C3%BCrk_Telekom_Arena2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1400" data-file-height="430" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Atat%C3%BCrk_Olympic_Stadium" title="Atat\xc3\xbcrk Olympic Stadium">Atat\xc3\xbcrk Olympic Stadium</a> (top)<br /><a href="/wiki/T%C3%BCrk_Telekom_Stadium" title="T\xc3\xbcrk Telekom Stadium">T\xc3\xbcrk Telekom Stadium</a> (bottom)</div></div></div></div>\n<p>Istanbul is home to some of Turkey\'s oldest <a href="/wiki/Sports_club" title="Sports club">sports clubs</a>. <a href="/wiki/Be%C5%9Fikta%C5%9F_J.K." class="mw-redirect" title="Be\xc5\x9fikta\xc5\x9f J.K.">Be\xc5\x9fikta\xc5\x9f JK</a>, established in 1903, is considered the oldest of these sports clubs. Due to its initial status as Turkey\'s only club, Be\xc5\x9fikta\xc5\x9f occasionally represented the Ottoman Empire and Turkish Republic in international sports competitions, earning the right to place the Turkish flag inside its team logo.<sup id="cite_ref-fifa-bes_266-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fifa-bes-266">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Galatasaray_S.K." title="Galatasaray S.K.">Galatasaray SK</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fenerbah%C3%A7e_S.K." title="Fenerbah\xc3\xa7e S.K.">Fenerbah\xc3\xa7e SK</a> have fared better in international competitions and have won more <a href="/wiki/S%C3%BCper_Lig" title="S\xc3\xbcper Lig">S\xc3\xbcper Lig</a> titles, at 21 and 19 times, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fifa-gal_268-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fifa-gal-268">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup> Galatasaray and Fenerbah\xc3\xa7e have a long-standing rivalry, with Galatasaray based in the European part and Fenerbah\xc3\xa7e based in the Anatolian part of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-fifa-gal_268-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fifa-gal-268">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup> Istanbul has seven basketball teams\xe2\x80\x94<a href="/wiki/Anadolu_Efes_S.K." title="Anadolu Efes S.K.">Anadolu Efes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Be%C5%9Fikta%C5%9F_J.K._(men%27s_basketball)" title="Be\xc5\x9fikta\xc5\x9f J.K. (men&#39;s basketball)">Be\xc5\x9fikta\xc5\x9f</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dar%C3%BC%C5%9F%C5%9Fafaka_S.K." title="Dar\xc3\xbc\xc5\x9f\xc5\x9fafaka S.K.">Dar\xc3\xbc\xc5\x9f\xc5\x9fafaka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fenerbah%C3%A7e_Men%27s_Basketball" class="mw-redirect" title="Fenerbah\xc3\xa7e Men&#39;s Basketball">Fenerbah\xc3\xa7e</a>, <a href="/wiki/Galatasaray_S.K._(men%27s_basketball)" title="Galatasaray S.K. (men&#39;s basketball)">Galatasaray</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0stanbul_B%C3%BCy%C3%BCk%C5%9Fehir_Belediyespor_(basketball)" title="\xc4\xb0stanbul B\xc3\xbcy\xc3\xbck\xc5\x9fehir Belediyespor (basketball)">\xc4\xb0stanbul B\xc3\xbcy\xc3\xbck\xc5\x9fehir Belediyespor</a> and <a href="/wiki/B%C3%BCy%C3%BCk%C3%A7ekmece_Basketbol" title="B\xc3\xbcy\xc3\xbck\xc3\xa7ekmece Basketbol">B\xc3\xbcy\xc3\xbck\xc3\xa7ekmece</a>\xe2\x80\x94that play in the premier-level <a href="/wiki/Basketbol_S%C3%BCper_Ligi" title="Basketbol S\xc3\xbcper Ligi">Turkish Basketball Super League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Many of Istanbul\'s sports facilities have been built or upgraded since 2000 to bolster the city\'s bids for the <a href="/wiki/Summer_Olympic_Games" title="Summer Olympic Games">Summer Olympic Games</a>. <a href="/wiki/Atat%C3%BCrk_Olympic_Stadium" title="Atat\xc3\xbcrk Olympic Stadium">Atat\xc3\xbcrk Olympic Stadium</a>, the largest multi-purpose stadium in Turkey, was completed in 2002 as an <a href="/wiki/International_Association_of_Athletics_Federations" title="International Association of Athletics Federations">IAAF</a> first-class venue for <a href="/wiki/Track_and_field" title="Track and field">track and field</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup> The stadium hosted the <a href="/wiki/2005_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2005 UEFA Champions League Final">2005 UEFA Champions League Final</a> and will host the <a href="/wiki/2020_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2020 UEFA Champions League Final">2020 UEFA Champions League Final</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/%C5%9E%C3%BCkr%C3%BC_Saraco%C4%9Flu_Stadium" title="\xc5\x9e\xc3\xbckr\xc3\xbc Saraco\xc4\x9flu Stadium">\xc5\x9e\xc3\xbckr\xc3\xbc Saraco\xc4\x9flu Stadium</a>, Fenerbah\xc3\xa7e\'s home field, hosted the <a href="/wiki/2009_UEFA_Cup_Final" title="2009 UEFA Cup Final">2009 UEFA Cup Final</a> three years after its completion. <a href="/wiki/T%C3%BCrk_Telekom_Arena" class="mw-redirect" title="T\xc3\xbcrk Telekom Arena">T\xc3\xbcrk Telekom Arena</a> opened in 2011 to replace <a href="/wiki/Ali_Sami_Yen_Stadium" title="Ali Sami Yen Stadium">Ali Sami Yen Stadium</a> as Galatasaray\'s home turf,<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Vodafone_Arena" class="mw-redirect" title="Vodafone Arena">Vodafone Arena</a> opened in 2016 to replace <a href="/wiki/BJK_%C4%B0n%C3%B6n%C3%BC_Stadium" title="BJK \xc4\xb0n\xc3\xb6n\xc3\xbc Stadium">BJK \xc4\xb0n\xc3\xb6n\xc3\xbc Stadium</a> as the home turf of Be\xc5\x9fikta\xc5\x9f, which won the S\xc3\xbcper Lig in the same season. All four stadiums are elite <a href="/wiki/UEFA_stadium_categories" title="UEFA stadium categories">Category 4</a> (formerly five-star) UEFA stadiums.<sup id="cite_ref-uefa-category_278-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uefa-category-278">&#91;f&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px"><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Sinan_Erdem_Dome_Panaroma.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Sinan_Erdem_Dome_Panaroma.jpg/200px-Sinan_Erdem_Dome_Panaroma.jpg" width="200" height="70" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Sinan_Erdem_Dome_Panaroma.jpg/300px-Sinan_Erdem_Dome_Panaroma.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Sinan_Erdem_Dome_Panaroma.jpg/400px-Sinan_Erdem_Dome_Panaroma.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1330" data-file-height="464" /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:%C3%9Clker_Sports_Arena-_Fenerbah%C3%A7e_vs._Armani_Milano.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/%C3%9Clker_Sports_Arena-_Fenerbah%C3%A7e_vs._Armani_Milano.jpg/200px-%C3%9Clker_Sports_Arena-_Fenerbah%C3%A7e_vs._Armani_Milano.jpg" width="200" height="113" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/%C3%9Clker_Sports_Arena-_Fenerbah%C3%A7e_vs._Armani_Milano.jpg/300px-%C3%9Clker_Sports_Arena-_Fenerbah%C3%A7e_vs._Armani_Milano.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/%C3%9Clker_Sports_Arena-_Fenerbah%C3%A7e_vs._Armani_Milano.jpg/400px-%C3%9Clker_Sports_Arena-_Fenerbah%C3%A7e_vs._Armani_Milano.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="2432" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Sinan_Erdem_Dome" title="Sinan Erdem Dome">Sinan Erdem Dome</a> (top)<br /><a href="/wiki/%C3%9Clker_Sports_Arena" class="mw-redirect" title="\xc3\x9clker Sports Arena">\xc3\x9clker Sports Arena</a> (bottom)</div></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Sinan_Erdem_Dome" title="Sinan Erdem Dome">Sinan Erdem Dome</a>, among the largest indoor arenas in Europe, hosted the final of the <a href="/wiki/2010_FIBA_World_Championship" title="2010 FIBA World Championship">2010 FIBA World Championship</a>, the <a href="/wiki/2012_IAAF_World_Indoor_Championships" title="2012 IAAF World Indoor Championships">2012 IAAF World Indoor Championships</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Euroleague" title="2011\xe2\x80\x9312 Euroleague">2011\xe2\x80\x9312 Euroleague</a> and <a href="/wiki/2016-17_EuroLeague" class="mw-redirect" title="2016-17 EuroLeague">2016-17 EuroLeague</a> Final Fours.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup> Prior to the completion of the Sinan Erdem Dome in 2010, <a href="/wiki/Abdi_%C4%B0pek%C3%A7i_Arena" title="Abdi \xc4\xb0pek\xc3\xa7i Arena">Abdi \xc4\xb0pek\xc3\xa7i Arena</a> was Istanbul\'s primary indoor arena, having hosted the finals of <a href="/wiki/EuroBasket_2001" title="EuroBasket 2001">EuroBasket 2001</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup> Several other indoor arenas, including the <a href="/wiki/BJK_Akatlar_Arena" title="BJK Akatlar Arena">Be\xc5\x9fikta\xc5\x9f Akatlar Arena</a>, have also been inaugurated since 2000, serving as the home courts of Istanbul\'s sports clubs. The most recent of these is the 13,800-seat <a href="/wiki/%C3%9Clker_Sports_Arena" class="mw-redirect" title="\xc3\x9clker Sports Arena">\xc3\x9clker Sports Arena</a>, which opened in 2012 as the home court of Fenerbah\xc3\xa7e\'s basketball teams.<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup> Despite the construction boom, five bids for the Summer Olympics\xe2\x80\x94in <a href="/wiki/2000_Summer_Olympics" title="2000 Summer Olympics">2000</a>, <a href="/wiki/2004_Summer_Olympics" title="2004 Summer Olympics">2004</a>, <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics" title="2008 Summer Olympics">2008</a>, <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">2012</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2020_Summer_Olympics" title="2020 Summer Olympics">2020</a>\xe2\x80\x94and national bids for <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012" title="UEFA Euro 2012">UEFA Euro 2012</a> and <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016" title="UEFA Euro 2016">UEFA Euro 2016</a> have ended unsuccessfully.<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/TVF_Burhan_Felek_Sport_Hall" title="TVF Burhan Felek Sport Hall">TVF Burhan Felek Sport Hall</a> is one of the major volleyball arenas in the city and hosts clubs such as <a href="/wiki/Eczac%C4%B1ba%C5%9F%C4%B1_VitrA" title="Eczac\xc4\xb1ba\xc5\x9f\xc4\xb1 VitrA">Eczac\xc4\xb1ba\xc5\x9f\xc4\xb1 VitrA</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vak%C4%B1fbank_S.K." title="Vak\xc4\xb1fbank S.K.">Vak\xc4\xb1fbank SK</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fenerbah%C3%A7e_Women%27s_Volleyball" title="Fenerbah\xc3\xa7e Women&#39;s Volleyball">Fenerbah\xc3\xa7e</a> who have won numerous <a href="/wiki/CEV_Women%27s_Champions_League" title="CEV Women&#39;s Champions League">European</a> and <a href="/wiki/FIVB_Volleyball_Women%27s_Club_World_Championship" title="FIVB Volleyball Women&#39;s Club World Championship">World Championship</a> titles. \n</p><p>Between 2005 and 2011, <a href="/wiki/Intercity_Istanbul_Park" title="Intercity Istanbul Park">Istanbul Park</a> racing circuit hosted the annual <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a> <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Grand_Prix" title="Turkish Grand Prix">Turkish Grand Prix</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup> Istanbul Park was also a venue of the <a href="/wiki/World_Touring_Car_Championship" title="World Touring Car Championship">World Touring Car Championship</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Le_Mans_Series" title="European Le Mans Series">European Le Mans Series</a> in 2005 and 2006, but the track has not seen either of these competitions since then.<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup> It also hosted the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Motorcycle_Grand_Prix" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish Motorcycle Grand Prix">Turkish Motorcycle Grand Prix</a> between 2005 and 2007. Istanbul was occasionally a venue of the <a href="/wiki/F1_Powerboat_World_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="F1 Powerboat World Championship">F1 Powerboat World Championship</a>, with the last race on the Bosphorus strait on 12\xe2\x80\x9313 August 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup> The last race of the <a href="/wiki/Offshore_powerboat_racing#UIM_Powerboat_GPS_World_Championship" title="Offshore powerboat racing">Powerboat P1 World Championship</a> on the Bosphorus took place on 19\xe2\x80\x9321 June 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup> Istanbul Sailing Club, established in 1952, hosts races and other sailing events on the waterways in and around Istanbul each year.<sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup> Turkish Offshore Racing Club also hosts major yacht races, such as the annual Naval Forces Trophy.<sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Istanbul&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Istanbul_-H%C3%BCrriyet-_2000_by_RaBoe_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Entrance to an office building with an overhead sign saying &#39;H\xc3\xbcrriyet&#39;" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Istanbul_-H%C3%BCrriyet-_2000_by_RaBoe_02.jpg/220px-Istanbul_-H%C3%BCrriyet-_2000_by_RaBoe_02.jpg" width="220" height="182" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Istanbul_-H%C3%BCrriyet-_2000_by_RaBoe_02.jpg/330px-Istanbul_-H%C3%BCrriyet-_2000_by_RaBoe_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Istanbul_-H%C3%BCrriyet-_2000_by_RaBoe_02.jpg/440px-Istanbul_-H%C3%BCrriyet-_2000_by_RaBoe_02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="661" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Istanbul_-H%C3%BCrriyet-_2000_by_RaBoe_02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Established in 1948, <i><a href="/wiki/H%C3%BCrriyet" title="H\xc3\xbcrriyet">H\xc3\xbcrriyet</a></i> is one of Turkey\'s most circulated newspapers.</div></div></div>\n<p>Most state-run radio and television stations are based in Ankara, but Istanbul is the primary hub of Turkish media. The industry has its roots in the former Ottoman capital, where the first Turkish newspaper, <i>Takvim-i Vekayi</i> (Calendar of Affairs), was published in 1831. The <a href="/wiki/Ca%C4%9Falo%C4%9Flu" title="Ca\xc4\x9falo\xc4\x9flu">Ca\xc4\x9falo\xc4\x9flu</a> street on which the newspaper was printed, B\xc3\xa2b-\xc4\xb1 \xc3\x82li Street, rapidly became the center of Turkish print media, alongside Beyo\xc4\x9flu across the Golden Horn.<sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Today, Istanbul hosts a wide variety of periodicals. Most nationwide newspapers are based in Istanbul, with simultaneous Ankara and \xc4\xb0zmir editions.<sup id="cite_ref-loc-pro_292-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-pro-292">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/H%C3%BCrriyet" title="H\xc3\xbcrriyet">H\xc3\xbcrriyet</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Sabah_(newspaper)" title="Sabah (newspaper)">Sabah</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Posta_(newspaper)" title="Posta (newspaper)">Posta</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/S%C3%B6zc%C3%BC" title="S\xc3\xb6zc\xc3\xbc">S\xc3\xb6zc\xc3\xbc</a></i>, the country\'s top four papers, are all headquartered in Istanbul, boasting more than 275,000 weekly sales each.<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup> <i>H\xc3\xbcrriyet\'</i>s English-language edition, <i><a href="/wiki/H%C3%BCrriyet_Daily_News" title="H\xc3\xbcrriyet Daily News">H\xc3\xbcrriyet Daily News</a></i>, has been printed since 1961, but the English-language <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Sabah" title="Daily Sabah">Daily Sabah</a></i>, first published by <i>Sabah</i> in 2014, has overtaken it in circulation. Several smaller newspapers, including popular publications like <i><a href="/wiki/Cumhuriyet" title="Cumhuriyet">Cumhuriyet</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Milliyet" title="Milliyet">Milliyet</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Habert%C3%BCrk" title="Habert\xc3\xbcrk">Habert\xc3\xbcrk</a></i> are also based in Istanbul.<sup id="cite_ref-loc-pro_292-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-pro-292">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup> Istanbul also has long-running <a href="/wiki/Armenian_language" title="Armenian language">Armenian language</a> newspapers, notably the dailies <i><a href="/wiki/Marmara_(newspaper)" title="Marmara (newspaper)">Marmara</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Jamanak" title="Jamanak">Jamanak</a></i> and the bilingual weekly <i><a href="/wiki/Agos" title="Agos">Agos</a></i> in Armenian and Turkish. \n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%C4%B0stanbul_radio1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="A four-story, white flat-roofed building with two Turkish flags and a portrait on the exterior" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/%C4%B0stanbul_radio1.JPG/220px-%C4%B0stanbul_radio1.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/%C4%B0stanbul_radio1.JPG/330px-%C4%B0stanbul_radio1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/%C4%B0stanbul_radio1.JPG/440px-%C4%B0stanbul_radio1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%C4%B0stanbul_radio1.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Headquarters of the state-run TRT\'s Istanbul radio operations</div></div></div>\n<p>Radio broadcasts in Istanbul date back to 1927, when Turkey\'s first radio transmission came from atop the Central Post Office in Emin\xc3\xb6n\xc3\xbc. Control of this transmission, and other radio stations established in the following decades, ultimately came under the state-run <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Radio_and_Television_Corporation" title="Turkish Radio and Television Corporation">Turkish Radio and Television Corporation</a> (TRT), which held a monopoly on radio and television broadcasts between its founding in 1964 and 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-trt-radio_294-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trt-radio-294">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup> Today, TRT runs four national radio stations; these stations have transmitters across the country so each can reach over <span class="nowrap">90 percent</span> of the country\'s population, but only <span class="nowrap">Radio 2</span> is based in Istanbul. Offering a range of content from educational programming to coverage of sporting events, <span class="nowrap">Radio 2</span> is the most popular radio station in Turkey.<sup id="cite_ref-trt-radio_294-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trt-radio-294">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup> Istanbul\'s airwaves are the busiest in Turkey, primarily featuring either Turkish-language or English-language content. One of the exceptions, offering both, is <a href="/wiki/A%C3%A7%C4%B1k_Radyo" title="A\xc3\xa7\xc4\xb1k Radyo">A\xc3\xa7\xc4\xb1k Radyo</a> (94.9 FM). Among Turkey\'s first private stations, and the first featuring foreign popular music, was Istanbul\'s <a href="/wiki/Metro_FM_(Turkey)" title="Metro FM (Turkey)">Metro FM</a> (97.2 FM). The state-run <span class="nowrap">Radio 3</span>, although based in Ankara, also features English-language popular music, and English-language news programming is provided on NTV Radyo (102.8 FM).<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>TRT-Children is the only TRT television station based in Istanbul.<sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup> Istanbul is home to the headquarters of several Turkish stations and regional headquarters of international media outlets. Istanbul-based <a href="/wiki/Star_TV_(Turkey)" title="Star TV (Turkey)">Star TV</a> was the first private television network to be established following the end of the TRT monopoly; Star TV and <a href="/wiki/Show_TV" title="Show TV">Show TV</a> (also based in Istanbul) remain highly popular throughout the country, airing Turkish and American series.<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kanal_D" title="Kanal D">Kanal D</a> and <a href="/wiki/Atv_(Turkey)" class="mw-redirect" title="Atv (Turkey)">ATV</a> are other stations in Istanbul that offer a mix of news and series; <a href="/wiki/NTV_(Turkey)" title="NTV (Turkey)">NTV</a> (partnered with U.S. media outlet <a href="/wiki/MSNBC" title="MSNBC">MSNBC</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Sky_Turk_360" class="mw-redirect" title="Sky Turk 360">Sky Turk</a>\xe2\x80\x94both based in the city\xe2\x80\x94are mainly just known for their news coverage in Turkish. The <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> has a regional office in Istanbul, assisting its Turkish-language news operations, and the American news channel <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a> established the Turkish-language <a href="/wiki/CNN_T%C3%BCrk" title="CNN T\xc3\xbcrk">CNN T\xc3\xbcrk</a> there in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup> The Istanbul-based business and entertainment channel <a href="/wiki/CNBC-e" title="CNBC-e">CNBC-e</a> began broadcasting in 2000.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Istanbul&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Turkey" title="Education in Turkey">Education in Turkey</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Istanbul_University_cropped.JPG" class="image"><img alt="A triumphal arch adjacent to a Turkish flag and in front of an open plaza" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Istanbul_University_cropped.JPG/170px-Istanbul_University_cropped.JPG" width="170" height="216" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Istanbul_University_cropped.JPG/255px-Istanbul_University_cropped.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Istanbul_University_cropped.JPG/340px-Istanbul_University_cropped.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1491" data-file-height="1897" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Istanbul_University_cropped.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Main entrance gate of <a href="/wiki/Istanbul_University" title="Istanbul University">Istanbul University</a>, the city\'s oldest Turkish institution, established in 1453.</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Istanbul_University" title="Istanbul University">Istanbul University</a>, founded in 1453, is the oldest Turkish educational institution in the city. Although originally an <a href="/wiki/Madrasah" class="mw-redirect" title="Madrasah">Islamic school</a>, the university established law, medicine, and science departments in the 19th century and was secularized after the founding of the Turkish Republic.<sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">&#91;293&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Istanbul_Technical_University" title="Istanbul Technical University">Istanbul Technical University</a>, founded in 1773, is the world\'s third-oldest university dedicated entirely to engineering sciences.<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">&#91;295&#93;</a></sup> These public universities are two of just eight across the city;<sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup> other prominent state universities in Istanbul include the <a href="/wiki/Mimar_Sinan_Fine_Arts_University" title="Mimar Sinan Fine Arts University">Mimar Sinan Fine Arts University</a>, which served as Turkey\'s primary institution of art until the 1970s,<sup id="cite_ref-gosotu2213_239-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gosotu2213-239">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Marmara_University" title="Marmara University">Marmara University</a>, the country\'s third-largest institution of higher learning.<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">&#91;297&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RobertCollegeGouldHall1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="An ivy-covered neoclassical building atop a hill, with a greenery-adorned walkway leading to its entrance" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/RobertCollegeGouldHall1.jpg/220px-RobertCollegeGouldHall1.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/RobertCollegeGouldHall1.jpg/330px-RobertCollegeGouldHall1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/RobertCollegeGouldHall1.jpg/440px-RobertCollegeGouldHall1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RobertCollegeGouldHall1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Established in 1863, <a href="/wiki/Robert_College" title="Robert College">Robert College</a> has been an American boarding school since its higher education section became <a href="/wiki/Bo%C4%9Fazi%C3%A7i_University" title="Bo\xc4\x9fazi\xc3\xa7i University">Bo\xc4\x9fazi\xc3\xa7i University</a> in 1971.</div></div></div>\n<p>Most established universities in Istanbul are backed by the government; the city also has several prominent private institutions. The first modern private university in Istanbul, also the oldest American school in existence in its original location outside the United States, was <a href="/wiki/Robert_College" title="Robert College">Robert College</a>, founded by <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Robert" title="Christopher Robert">Christopher Robert</a>, an American philanthropist, and <a href="/wiki/Cyrus_Hamlin" title="Cyrus Hamlin">Cyrus Hamlin</a>, a missionary devoted to education, in 1863. The tertiary element of its education program became the public <a href="/wiki/Bo%C4%9Fazi%C3%A7i_University" title="Bo\xc4\x9fazi\xc3\xa7i University">Bo\xc4\x9fazi\xc3\xa7i University</a> in 1971; the remaining portion in Arnavutk\xc3\xb6y continues as a boarding high-school under the name Robert College.<sup id="cite_ref-dog_304-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dog-304">&#91;298&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305">&#91;299&#93;</a></sup> Private universities were officially outlawed in Turkey before the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Turkey" title="Constitution of Turkey">Constitution of 1982</a>, but there were already fifteen private "higher schools", which were effectively universities, in Istanbul by 1970. The first private university established in Istanbul since 1982 was <a href="/wiki/Ko%C3%A7_University" title="Ko\xc3\xa7 University">Ko\xc3\xa7 University</a> (founded in 1992), and another dozen had opened within the following decade.<sup id="cite_ref-dog_304-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dog-304">&#91;298&#93;</a></sup> Today, there are at least 30 private universities in the city, including <a href="/wiki/Istanbul_Commerce_University" title="Istanbul Commerce University">Istanbul Commerce University</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kadir_Has_University" title="Kadir Has University">Kadir Has University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306">&#91;300&#93;</a></sup> A new <a href="/wiki/Medical_research" title="Medical research">biomedical research</a> and development hub, called Bio Istanbul, is under construction in <a href="/wiki/Ba%C5%9Fak%C5%9Fehir" title="Ba\xc5\x9fak\xc5\x9fehir">Ba\xc5\x9fak\xc5\x9fehir</a>, and will host 15,000 residents, 20,000 working commuters, and a university upon completion.<sup id="cite_ref-Hurriyet2013_307-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hurriyet2013-307">&#91;301&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AECOM_308-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AECOM-308">&#91;302&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kuleli_Military_High_School.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Kuleli_Military_High_School.jpg/220px-Kuleli_Military_High_School.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Kuleli_Military_High_School.jpg/330px-Kuleli_Military_High_School.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Kuleli_Military_High_School.jpg/440px-Kuleli_Military_High_School.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="680" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kuleli_Military_High_School.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View of <a href="/wiki/Kuleli_Military_High_School" title="Kuleli Military High School">Kuleli Military High School</a> (1845-2016)</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2007, there were about <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_Istanbul" class="mw-redirect" title="List of schools in Istanbul">4,350 schools</a>, about half of which were <a href="/wiki/Primary_school" title="Primary school">primary schools</a>; on average, each school had 688 students. In recent years, Istanbul\'s educational system has expanded substantially; from 2000 to 2007, the number of classrooms and teachers nearly doubled and the number of students increased by more than <span class="nowrap">60 percent</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-309" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-309">&#91;303&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Galatasaray_High_School" title="Galatasaray High School">Galatasaray High School</a>, established in 1481 as the Galata Palace Imperial School, is the oldest high school in Istanbul and the second-oldest educational institution in the city. It was built at the behest of Sultan <a href="/wiki/Bayezid_II" title="Bayezid II">Bayezid II</a>, who sought to bring students with diverse backgrounds together as a means of strengthening his growing empire.<sup id="cite_ref-310" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-310">&#91;304&#93;</a></sup> It is one of Turkey\'s <a href="/wiki/Anatolian_High_School" title="Anatolian High School">Anatolian High Schools</a>, elite public high schools that place a stronger emphasis on instruction in foreign languages. Galatasaray, for example, offers instruction in French; other Anatolian High Schools primarily teach in English or German alongside Turkish.<sup id="cite_ref-311" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-311">&#91;305&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-312" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-312">&#91;306&#93;</a></sup> The city also has foreign high schools, such as <a href="/wiki/Liceo_Italiano" class="mw-redirect" title="Liceo Italiano">Liceo Italiano</a>, that were established in the 19th century to educate foreigners.<sup id="cite_ref-313" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-313">&#91;307&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Kuleli_Military_High_School" title="Kuleli Military High School">Kuleli Military High School</a>, along the shores of the Bosphorus in <a href="/wiki/%C3%87engelk%C3%B6y" title="\xc3\x87engelk\xc3\xb6y">\xc3\x87engelk\xc3\xb6y</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Naval_High_School" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish Naval High School">Turkish Naval High School</a>, located on one of the <a href="/wiki/Princes%27_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Princes&#39; Islands">Princes\' Islands</a>, were military high schools, complemented by three <a href="/wiki/Military_academy" title="Military academy">military academies</a>\xe2\x80\x94the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Air_Force_Academy" title="Turkish Air Force Academy">Turkish Air Force</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Military_Academy" title="Turkish Military Academy">Turkish Military</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Naval_Academy" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish Naval Academy">Turkish Naval</a> Academies. Both schools were shut <a href="/wiki/Dar%C3%BC%C5%9F%C5%9Fafaka_High_School" title="Dar\xc3\xbc\xc5\x9f\xc5\x9fafaka High School">Dar\xc3\xbc\xc5\x9f\xc5\x9fafaka High School</a> provides free education to children across the country missing at least one parent. Dar\xc3\xbc\xc5\x9f\xc5\x9fafaka begins instruction with the fourth grade, providing instruction in English and, starting in sixth grade, a second foreign language\xe2\x80\x94German or French.<sup id="cite_ref-314" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-314">&#91;308&#93;</a></sup> Other prominent high schools in the city include <a href="/wiki/Istanbul_Lisesi" class="mw-redirect" title="Istanbul Lisesi">Istanbul Lisesi</a> (founded in 1884), <a href="/wiki/Kabata%C5%9F_Erkek_Lisesi" title="Kabata\xc5\x9f Erkek Lisesi">Kabata\xc5\x9f Erkek Lisesi</a> (founded in 1908)<sup id="cite_ref-315" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-315">&#91;309&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Kad%C4%B1k%C3%B6y_Anadolu_Lisesi" title="Kad\xc4\xb1k\xc3\xb6y Anadolu Lisesi">Kad\xc4\xb1k\xc3\xb6y Anadolu Lisesi</a> (founded in 1955).<sup id="cite_ref-316" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-316">&#91;310&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_services">Public services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Istanbul&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Public services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Utilities_in_Istanbul" title="Utilities in Istanbul">Utilities in Istanbul</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Turkey" title="Telecommunications in Turkey">Telecommunications in Turkey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Health_care_in_Turkey" title="Health care in Turkey">Health care in Turkey</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sunset_at_Santral_Istanbul.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A brick factory stands in front of a park, with open green space, a reflecting pool, and benches" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Sunset_at_Santral_Istanbul.jpg/220px-Sunset_at_Santral_Istanbul.jpg" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Sunset_at_Santral_Istanbul.jpg/330px-Sunset_at_Santral_Istanbul.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Sunset_at_Santral_Istanbul.jpg/440px-Sunset_at_Santral_Istanbul.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3336" data-file-height="2088" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sunset_at_Santral_Istanbul.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Silahtara%C4%9Fa_Power_Station" title="Silahtara\xc4\x9fa Power Station">Silahtara\xc4\x9fa Power Station</a>, now the art museum <a href="/wiki/SantralIstanbul" title="SantralIstanbul">SantralIstanbul</a>, was Istanbul\'s sole source of power between 1914 and 1952.</div></div></div>\n<p>Istanbul\'s first <a href="/wiki/Water_supply" title="Water supply">water supply</a> systems date back to the city\'s early history, when <a href="/wiki/Aqueduct_(watercourse)" class="mw-redirect" title="Aqueduct (watercourse)">aqueducts</a> (such as the <a href="/wiki/Valens_Aqueduct" title="Valens Aqueduct">Valens Aqueduct</a>) deposited the water in the city\'s numerous <a href="/wiki/Cistern" title="Cistern">cisterns</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-iskitarihce_317-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iskitarihce-317">&#91;311&#93;</a></sup> At the behest of <a href="/wiki/Suleiman_the_Magnificent" title="Suleiman the Magnificent">Suleiman the Magnificent</a>, the K\xc4\xb1rk\xc3\xa7e\xc5\x9fme water supply network was constructed; by 1563, the network provided 4,200 cubic meters (150,000&#160;cu&#160;ft) of water to <span class="nowrap">158 sites</span> each day.<sup id="cite_ref-iskitarihce_317-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iskitarihce-317">&#91;311&#93;</a></sup> In later years, in response to increasing public demand, water from various springs was channeled to public fountains, like the <a href="/wiki/Fountain_of_Ahmed_III" title="Fountain of Ahmed III">Fountain of Ahmed III</a>, by means of supply lines.<sup id="cite_ref-318" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-318">&#91;312&#93;</a></sup> Today, Istanbul has a chlorinated and filtered water supply and a <a href="/wiki/Sewage_treatment" title="Sewage treatment">sewage treatment</a> system managed by the Istanbul Water and Sewerage Administration (\xc4\xb0stanbul Su ve Kanalizasyon \xc4\xb0daresi, \xc4\xb0SK\xc4\xb0).<sup id="cite_ref-319" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-319">&#91;313&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Silahtara%C4%9Fa_Power_Station" title="Silahtara\xc4\x9fa Power Station">Silahtara\xc4\x9fa Power Station</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Fossil-fuel_power_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Fossil-fuel power station">coal-fired power plant</a> along the Golden Horn, was the sole source of Istanbul\'s electricity between 1914, when its first engine room was completed, and 1952.<sup id="cite_ref-silah_320-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-silah-320">&#91;314&#93;</a></sup> Following the founding of the Turkish Republic, the plant underwent renovations to accommodate the city\'s increasing demand; its capacity grew from <span class="nowrap">23 megawatts</span> in 1923 to a peak of <span class="nowrap">120 megawatts</span> in 1956.<sup id="cite_ref-silah_320-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-silah-320">&#91;314&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-teias_321-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-teias-321">&#91;315&#93;</a></sup> Capacity declined until the power station reached the end of its economic life and shut down in 1983.<sup id="cite_ref-silah_320-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-silah-320">&#91;314&#93;</a></sup> The state-run Turkish Electrical Authority (TEK) briefly\xe2\x80\x94between its founding in 1970 and 1984\xe2\x80\x94held a monopoly on the generation and distribution of electricity, but now the authority\xe2\x80\x94since split between the Turkish Electricity Generation Transmission Company (TEA\xc5\x9e) and the Turkish Electricity Distribution Company (TEDA\xc5\x9e)\xe2\x80\x94competes with private <a href="/wiki/Electric_utility" title="Electric utility">electric utilities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-teias_321-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-teias-321">&#91;315&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%C4%B0stanbul_Sirkeci_B%C3%BCy%C3%BCk_Postane_1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="An arched neoclassical building with hanging banners, with a yellow vehicle parked in front" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/%C4%B0stanbul_Sirkeci_B%C3%BCy%C3%BCk_Postane_1.JPG/220px-%C4%B0stanbul_Sirkeci_B%C3%BCy%C3%BCk_Postane_1.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/%C4%B0stanbul_Sirkeci_B%C3%BCy%C3%BCk_Postane_1.JPG/330px-%C4%B0stanbul_Sirkeci_B%C3%BCy%C3%BCk_Postane_1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/%C4%B0stanbul_Sirkeci_B%C3%BCy%C3%BCk_Postane_1.JPG/440px-%C4%B0stanbul_Sirkeci_B%C3%BCy%C3%BCk_Postane_1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%C4%B0stanbul_Sirkeci_B%C3%BCy%C3%BCk_Postane_1.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Istanbul\'s current central post office dates back to 1909.<sup id="cite_ref-322" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-322">&#91;316&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>The Ottoman Ministry of Post and Telegraph was established in 1840 and the first post office, the Imperial Post Office, opened near the courtyard of <a href="/wiki/New_Mosque_(Istanbul)" title="New Mosque (Istanbul)">Yeni Mosque</a>. By 1876, the first international mailing network between Istanbul and the lands beyond the Ottoman Empire had been established.<sup id="cite_ref-PTT_323-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PTT-323">&#91;317&#93;</a></sup> Sultan <a href="/wiki/Abd%C3%BClmecid_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Abd\xc3\xbclmecid I">Abd\xc3\xbclmecid I</a> issued <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Morse" title="Samuel Morse">Samuel Morse</a> his first official honor for the <a href="/wiki/Electrical_telegraph" title="Electrical telegraph">telegraph</a> in 1847, and construction of the first telegraph line\xe2\x80\x94between Istanbul and <a href="/wiki/Edirne" title="Edirne">Edirne</a>\xe2\x80\x94finished in time to announce the end of the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_War" title="Crimean War">Crimean War</a> in 1856.<sup id="cite_ref-324" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-324">&#91;318&#93;</a></sup> A nascent telephone system began to emerge in Istanbul in 1881 and after the first manual <a href="/wiki/Telephone_exchange" title="Telephone exchange">telephone exchange</a> became operational in Istanbul in 1909, the Ministry of Post and Telegraph became the Ministry of Post, Telegraph, and Telephone.<sup id="cite_ref-PTT_323-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PTT-323">&#91;317&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-325" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-325">&#91;319&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/GSM" title="GSM">GSM</a> cellular networks arrived in Turkey in 1994, with Istanbul among the first cities to receive the service.<sup id="cite_ref-turkt_326-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-turkt-326">&#91;320&#93;</a></sup> Today, <a href="/wiki/Mobile_phone" title="Mobile phone">mobile</a> and <a href="/wiki/Landline" title="Landline">landline</a> service is provided by private companies, after <a href="/wiki/T%C3%BCrk_Telekom" title="T\xc3\xbcrk Telekom">T\xc3\xbcrk Telekom</a>, which split from the Ministry of Post, Telegraph, and Telephone in 1995, was privatized in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-PTT_323-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PTT-323">&#91;317&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-turkt_326-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-turkt-326">&#91;320&#93;</a></sup> Postal services remain under the purview of what is now the Post and Telegraph Organization (retaining the acronym PTT).<sup id="cite_ref-PTT_323-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PTT-323">&#91;317&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2000, Istanbul had <span class="nowrap">137 hospitals</span>, of which 100 were private.<sup id="cite_ref-327" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-327">&#91;321&#93;</a></sup> Turkish citizens are entitled to subsidized healthcare in the nation\'s state-run hospitals.<sup id="cite_ref-loc-pro_292-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-pro-292">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup> As public hospitals tend to be overcrowded or otherwise slow, private hospitals are preferable for those who can afford them. Their prevalence has increased significantly over the last decade, as the percentage of outpatients using private hospitals increased from <span class="nowrap">6 percent</span> to <span class="nowrap">23 percent</span> between 2005 and 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-loc-pro_292-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-pro-292">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-328" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-328">&#91;322&#93;</a></sup> Many of these private hospitals, as well as some of the public hospitals, are equipped with high-tech equipment, including <a href="/wiki/Magnetic_resonance_imaging" title="Magnetic resonance imaging">MRI</a> machines, or associated with medical research centers.<sup id="cite_ref-329" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-329">&#91;323&#93;</a></sup> Turkey has more hospitals accredited by the U.S.-based <a href="/wiki/Joint_Commission" title="Joint Commission">Joint Commission</a> than any other country in the world, with most concentrated in its big cities. The high quality of healthcare, especially in private hospitals, has contributed to a recent upsurge in <a href="/wiki/Medical_tourism" title="Medical tourism">medical tourism</a> to Turkey (with a <span class="nowrap">40 percent</span> increase between 2007 and 2008).<sup id="cite_ref-330" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-330">&#91;324&#93;</a></sup> Laser <a href="/wiki/Eye_surgery"
