title="Eye surgery">eye surgery</a> is particularly common among medical tourists, as Turkey is known for specializing in the procedure.<sup id="cite_ref-331" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-331">&#91;325&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Istanbul&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Public_transport_in_Istanbul" title="Public transport in Istanbul">Public transport in Istanbul</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fatih_Sultan_Mehmet_Bridge_panorama.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A docked sailboat floats in front of a suspension bridge, at twilight." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Fatih_Sultan_Mehmet_Bridge_panorama.jpg/220px-Fatih_Sultan_Mehmet_Bridge_panorama.jpg" width="220" height="119" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Fatih_Sultan_Mehmet_Bridge_panorama.jpg/330px-Fatih_Sultan_Mehmet_Bridge_panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Fatih_Sultan_Mehmet_Bridge_panorama.jpg/440px-Fatih_Sultan_Mehmet_Bridge_panorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4782" data-file-height="2576" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fatih_Sultan_Mehmet_Bridge_panorama.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Fatih_Sultan_Mehmet_Bridge" title="Fatih Sultan Mehmet Bridge">Fatih Sultan Mehmet Bridge</a> is one of three <a href="/wiki/Suspension_bridge" title="Suspension bridge">suspension bridges</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Bosphorus" class="mw-redirect" title="Bosphorus">Bosphorus</a> strait.</div></div></div>\n<p>Istanbul\'s primary motorways are the <a href="/wiki/Otoyol_1" title="Otoyol 1">O-1</a>, <a href="/wiki/Otoyol_2" title="Otoyol 2">O-2</a>, <a href="/wiki/Otoyol_3" title="Otoyol 3">O-3</a> and <a href="/wiki/Otoyol_4" title="Otoyol 4">O-4</a>. The O-1 forms the city\'s inner <a href="/wiki/Ring_road" title="Ring road">ring road</a>, traversing the <a href="/wiki/Bosphorus_Bridge" title="Bosphorus Bridge">15 Temmuz \xc5\x9eehitler (First Bosphorus) Bridge</a>, and the O-2 is the city\'s outer ring road, crossing the <a href="/wiki/Fatih_Sultan_Mehmet_Bridge" title="Fatih Sultan Mehmet Bridge">Fatih Sultan Mehmet (Second Bosphorus) Bridge</a>. The O-2 continues west to <a href="/wiki/Edirne" title="Edirne">Edirne</a> and the O-4 continues east to Ankara; the O-2, O-3, and O-4 are part of <a href="/wiki/European_route_E80" title="European route E80">European route E80</a> (the Trans-European Motorway) between Portugal and the Turkish\xe2\x80\x93Iranian border.<sup id="cite_ref-googma_332-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-googma-332">&#91;326&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, the first and second bridges on the Bosphorus carried <span class="nowrap">400,000 vehicles</span> each day.<sup id="cite_ref-333" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-333">&#91;327&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Yavuz_Sultan_Selim_Bridge" title="Yavuz Sultan Selim Bridge">Yavuz Sultan Selim (Third Bosphorus) Bridge</a> entered service on 26 August 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-334" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-334">&#91;328&#93;</a></sup> Environmentalist groups worry that the third bridge will endanger the remaining green areas to the north of Istanbul.<sup id="cite_ref-eib_335-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eib-335">&#91;329&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-let_336-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-let-336">&#91;330&#93;</a></sup> Apart from the three Bosphorus Bridges, the dual-deck, 14.6-kilometer (9.1&#160;mi) <a href="/wiki/Eurasia_Tunnel" title="Eurasia Tunnel">Eurasia Tunnel</a> (which entered service on 20 December 2016) under the Bosphorus strait also provides road crossings for motor vehicles between the Asian and European sides of Turkey.<sup id="cite_ref-337" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-337">&#91;331&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px"><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:T%C3%BCrkiye_%C4%B0stanbul_nostalji_iki_tramvay_kar%C5%9F%C4%B1la%C5%9Fmas%C4%B1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/T%C3%BCrkiye_%C4%B0stanbul_nostalji_iki_tramvay_kar%C5%9F%C4%B1la%C5%9Fmas%C4%B1.jpg/200px-T%C3%BCrkiye_%C4%B0stanbul_nostalji_iki_tramvay_kar%C5%9F%C4%B1la%C5%9Fmas%C4%B1.jpg" width="200" height="155" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/T%C3%BCrkiye_%C4%B0stanbul_nostalji_iki_tramvay_kar%C5%9F%C4%B1la%C5%9Fmas%C4%B1.jpg/300px-T%C3%BCrkiye_%C4%B0stanbul_nostalji_iki_tramvay_kar%C5%9F%C4%B1la%C5%9Fmas%C4%B1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/T%C3%BCrkiye_%C4%B0stanbul_nostalji_iki_tramvay_kar%C5%9F%C4%B1la%C5%9Fmas%C4%B1.jpg/400px-T%C3%BCrkiye_%C4%B0stanbul_nostalji_iki_tramvay_kar%C5%9F%C4%B1la%C5%9Fmas%C4%B1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="772" data-file-height="600" /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Istanbul_T1_line_Alstom_Citadis_tram.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Istanbul_T1_line_Alstom_Citadis_tram.jpg/200px-Istanbul_T1_line_Alstom_Citadis_tram.jpg" width="200" height="133" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Istanbul_T1_line_Alstom_Citadis_tram.jpg/300px-Istanbul_T1_line_Alstom_Citadis_tram.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Istanbul_T1_line_Alstom_Citadis_tram.jpg/400px-Istanbul_T1_line_Alstom_Citadis_tram.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3340" data-file-height="2224" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Istanbul\'s <a href="/wiki/Istanbul_nostalgic_tram" class="mw-redirect" title="Istanbul nostalgic tram">nostalgic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Istanbul_modern_tram" class="mw-redirect" title="Istanbul modern tram">modern tram</a> systems</div></div></div></div>\n<p>Istanbul\'s local public transportation system is a network of <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">trams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Funicular" title="Funicular">funiculars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Metro_(rapid_transit)" class="mw-redirect" title="Metro (rapid transit)">metro</a> lines, buses, <a href="/wiki/Bus_rapid_transit" title="Bus rapid transit">bus rapid transit</a>, and ferries. Fares across modes are integrated, using the <a href="/wiki/Contactless_smart_card" title="Contactless smart card">contactless</a> <a href="/wiki/Istanbulkart" title="Istanbulkart">Istanbulkart</a>, introduced in 2009, or the older <a href="/wiki/Akbil_(smart_ticket)" title="Akbil (smart ticket)">Akbil</a> electronic ticket device.<sup id="cite_ref-338" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-338">&#91;332&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Trams_in_Istanbul" title="Trams in Istanbul">Trams in Istanbul</a> date back to 1872, when they were horse-drawn, but even the first electrified trams were decommissioned in the 1960s.<sup id="cite_ref-iett-history_339-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iett-history-339">&#91;333&#93;</a></sup> Operated by Istanbul Electricity, Tramway, and Tunnel General Management (\xc4\xb0ETT), trams slowly returned to the city in the 1990s with the introduction of <a href="/wiki/Istanbul_nostalgic_tram" class="mw-redirect" title="Istanbul nostalgic tram">a nostalgic route</a> and a faster <a href="/wiki/Istanbul_modern_tram" class="mw-redirect" title="Istanbul modern tram">modern tram line</a>, which now carries <span class="nowrap">265,000 passengers</span> each day.<sup id="cite_ref-iett-history_339-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iett-history-339">&#91;333&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-340" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-340">&#91;334&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/T%C3%BCnel" title="T\xc3\xbcnel">T\xc3\xbcnel</a> opened in 1875 as the world\'s second-oldest subterranean rail line (after London\'s <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Railway" title="Metropolitan Railway">Metropolitan Railway</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-iett-history_339-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iett-history-339">&#91;333&#93;</a></sup> It still carries passengers between <a href="/wiki/Karak%C3%B6y" title="Karak\xc3\xb6y">Karak\xc3\xb6y</a> and \xc4\xb0stiklal Avenue along a steep 573-meter (1,880&#160;ft) track; a more modern funicular between Taksim Square and <a href="/wiki/Kabata%C5%9F,_Istanbul" class="mw-redirect" title="Kabata\xc5\x9f, Istanbul">Kabata\xc5\x9f</a> began running in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-341" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-341">&#91;335&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-342" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-342">&#91;336&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:M2_at_Levent_station.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/M2_at_Levent_station.JPG/220px-M2_at_Levent_station.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/M2_at_Levent_station.JPG/330px-M2_at_Levent_station.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/M2_at_Levent_station.JPG/440px-M2_at_Levent_station.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:M2_at_Levent_station.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Levent" title="Levent">Levent</a> station of the <a href="/wiki/Istanbul_Metro" title="Istanbul Metro">Istanbul Metro</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Istanbul_Metro" title="Istanbul Metro">Istanbul Metro</a> comprises five lines (the <a href="/wiki/M1_(Istanbul)" class="mw-redirect" title="M1 (Istanbul)">M1</a>, <a href="/wiki/M2_(Istanbul_Metro)" title="M2 (Istanbul Metro)">M2</a>, <a href="/wiki/M3_(Istanbul_Metro)" title="M3 (Istanbul Metro)">M3</a> and <a href="/wiki/M6_(Istanbul_Metro)" title="M6 (Istanbul Metro)">M6</a> on the European side, and the <a href="/wiki/M4_(Istanbul_Metro)" title="M4 (Istanbul Metro)">M4</a> on the Asian side) with several other lines (such as the <a href="/wiki/M5_(Istanbul_Metro)" title="M5 (Istanbul Metro)">M5</a>, <a href="/wiki/M7_(Istanbul_Metro)" title="M7 (Istanbul Metro)">M7</a>, and <a href="/wiki/M8_(Istanbul_Metro)" title="M8 (Istanbul Metro)">M8</a>) and extensions under construction.<sup id="cite_ref-343" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-343">&#91;337&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-344" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-344">&#91;338&#93;</a></sup> The two sides of Istanbul\'s metro are connected under the Bosphorus by the <a href="/wiki/Marmaray" title="Marmaray">Marmaray</a> tunnel, inaugurated in 2013 as the first rail connection between Thrace and Anatolia.<sup id="cite_ref-345" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-345">&#91;339&#93;</a></sup> With the Marmaray\'s completion, rail use in the city is expected to increase to <span class="nowrap">28 percent</span> (from <span class="nowrap">4 percent</span>), behind only <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-346" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-346">&#91;340&#93;</a></sup> Until then, buses provide transportation within and between the two halves of the city, accommodating <span class="nowrap">2.2 million</span> passenger trips each day.<sup id="cite_ref-347" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-347">&#91;341&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Metrobus_(Istanbul)" title="Metrobus (Istanbul)">Metrobus</a>, a form of bus rapid transit, crosses the Bosphorus Bridge, with dedicated lanes leading to its termini.<sup id="cite_ref-348" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-348">&#91;342&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0DO" title="\xc4\xb0DO">\xc4\xb0DO</a> (Istanbul Seabuses) runs a combination of all-passenger ferries and car-and-passenger ferries to ports on both sides of the Bosphorus, as far north as the Black Sea.<sup id="cite_ref-349" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-349">&#91;343&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-350" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-350">&#91;344&#93;</a></sup> With additional destinations around the Sea of Marmara, \xc4\xb0DO runs the largest municipal ferry operation in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-351" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-351">&#91;345&#93;</a></sup> The city\'s main cruise ship terminal is the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Istanbul" title="Port of Istanbul">Port of Istanbul</a> in Karak\xc3\xb6y, with a capacity of 10,000 passengers per hour.<sup id="cite_ref-352" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-352">&#91;346&#93;</a></sup> Most visitors enter Istanbul by air, but about half a million foreign tourists enter the city by sea each year.<sup id="cite_ref-iv&amp;c_234-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iv&amp;c-234">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bahnhofsfront-Istanbul-Sirkeci_retouched_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Bahnhofsfront-Istanbul-Sirkeci_retouched_2.jpg/220px-Bahnhofsfront-Istanbul-Sirkeci_retouched_2.jpg" width="220" height="89" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Bahnhofsfront-Istanbul-Sirkeci_retouched_2.jpg/330px-Bahnhofsfront-Istanbul-Sirkeci_retouched_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Bahnhofsfront-Istanbul-Sirkeci_retouched_2.jpg/440px-Bahnhofsfront-Istanbul-Sirkeci_retouched_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2398" data-file-height="971" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bahnhofsfront-Istanbul-Sirkeci_retouched_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Originally opened in 1873 with a smaller terminal building as the main terminus of the <a href="/wiki/Chemins_de_fer_Orientaux" title="Chemins de fer Orientaux">Rumelia (Balkan) Railway</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, which connected Istanbul with <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>; the current <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0stanbul_Sirkeci_Terminal" class="mw-redirect" title="\xc4\xb0stanbul Sirkeci Terminal">Sirkeci Terminal</a> building was constructed between 1888 and 1890, and became the eastern terminus of the <a href="/wiki/Orient_Express" title="Orient Express">Orient Express</a> from <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>International rail service from Istanbul launched in 1889, with a line between <a href="/wiki/Bucharest" title="Bucharest">Bucharest</a> and Istanbul\'s <a href="/wiki/Istanbul_Sirkeci_Terminal" class="mw-redirect" title="Istanbul Sirkeci Terminal">Sirkeci Terminal</a>, which ultimately became famous as the eastern terminus of the <a href="/wiki/Orient_Express" title="Orient Express">Orient Express</a> from <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ha251_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ha251-86">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> Regular service to Bucharest and <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">Thessaloniki</a> continued until the early 2010s, when the former was interrupted for Marmaray construction and the latter was halted due to <a href="/wiki/Greek_government-debt_crisis" title="Greek government-debt crisis">economic problems in Greece</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-353" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-353">&#91;347&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-354" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-354">&#91;348&#93;</a></sup> After Istanbul\'s <a href="/wiki/Haydarpa%C5%9Fa_Terminal" class="mw-redirect" title="Haydarpa\xc5\x9fa Terminal">Haydarpa\xc5\x9fa Terminal</a> opened in 1908, it served as the western terminus of the <a href="/wiki/Baghdad_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Baghdad Railway">Baghdad Railway</a> and an extension of the <a href="/wiki/Hejaz_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Hejaz Railway">Hejaz Railway</a>; today, neither service is offered directly from Istanbul.<sup id="cite_ref-355" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-355">&#91;349&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-356" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-356">&#91;350&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-357" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-357">&#91;351&#93;</a></sup> Service to Ankara and other points across Turkey is normally offered by <a href="/wiki/Turkish_State_Railways" title="Turkish State Railways">Turkish State Railways</a>, but the construction of Marmaray and the <a href="/wiki/Ankara-Istanbul_high-speed_railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Ankara-Istanbul high-speed railway">Ankara-Istanbul high-speed line</a> forced the station to close in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-akay_358-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-akay-358">&#91;352&#93;</a></sup> New stations to replace both the Haydarpa\xc5\x9fa and Sirkeci terminals, and connect the city\'s disjointed railway networks, are expected to open upon completion of the Marmaray project; until then, Istanbul is without intercity rail service.<sup id="cite_ref-akay_358-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-akay-358">&#91;352&#93;</a></sup> Private bus companies operate instead. Istanbul\'s main bus station is the largest in Europe, with a daily capacity of <span class="nowrap">15,000 buses</span> and <span class="nowrap">600,000 passengers</span>, serving destinations as distant as <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-359" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-359">&#91;353&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-360" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-360">&#91;354&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ataturk_Airport_Karakas-1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="An aerial view of an airport with three runways and several taxiways arranged around a terminal" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Ataturk_Airport_Karakas-1.jpg/220px-Ataturk_Airport_Karakas-1.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Ataturk_Airport_Karakas-1.jpg/330px-Ataturk_Airport_Karakas-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Ataturk_Airport_Karakas-1.jpg/440px-Ataturk_Airport_Karakas-1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ataturk_Airport_Karakas-1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Istanbul_Atat%C3%BCrk_Airport" title="Istanbul Atat\xc3\xbcrk Airport">Istanbul Atat\xc3\xbcrk Airport</a>, which handled <a href="/wiki/List_of_busiest_airports_by_passenger_traffic" title="List of busiest airports by passenger traffic">63.7 million passengers</a> in 2017,<sup id="cite_ref-361" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-361">&#91;355&#93;</a></sup> is the city\'s primary airport.</div></div></div>\n<p>Istanbul has two international airports. The larger is <a href="/wiki/Istanbul_Atat%C3%BCrk_Airport" title="Istanbul Atat\xc3\xbcrk Airport">Istanbul Atat\xc3\xbcrk</a>, 24 kilometers (15&#160;mi) west of the city center. It handled <span class="nowrap">61.3 million</span> passengers in 2015, making it the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_Europe" title="List of the busiest airports in Europe">third-busiest airport in Europe</a> and the <a href="/wiki/World%27s_busiest_airports_by_passenger_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="World&#39;s busiest airports by passenger traffic">eighteenth-busiest in the world</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-aci_362-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aci-362">&#91;356&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sabiha_G%C3%B6k%C3%A7en_International_Airport" title="Sabiha G\xc3\xb6k\xc3\xa7en International Airport">Sabiha G\xc3\xb6k\xc3\xa7en International</a>, 45 kilometers (28&#160;mi) southeast of the city center, opened in 2001 to relieve Atat\xc3\xbcrk. Dominated by <a href="/wiki/Low-cost_carrier" title="Low-cost carrier">low-cost carriers</a>, Istanbul\'s second airport has rapidly become popular, especially since the opening of a new international terminal in 2009;<sup id="cite_ref-363" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-363">&#91;357&#93;</a></sup> the airport handled <span class="nowrap">14.7 million</span> passengers in 2012, a year after <a href="/wiki/Airports_Council_International" title="Airports Council International">Airports Council International</a> named it the world\'s fastest-growing airport.<sup id="cite_ref-364" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-364">&#91;358&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-365" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-365">&#91;359&#93;</a></sup> Atat\xc3\xbcrk has also experienced rapid growth, as its <span class="nowrap">20.6 percent</span> rise in passenger traffic between 2011 and 2012 was the highest among the world\'s top 30 airports.<sup id="cite_ref-aci_362-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aci-362">&#91;356&#93;</a></sup> Because of the traffic at Istanbul\'s current airports,<sup id="cite_ref-zaman2012_366-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zaman2012-366">&#91;360&#93;</a></sup> a third international airport is planned for the Black Sea coast.<sup id="cite_ref-367" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-367">&#91;361&#93;</a></sup> Building a new runway at Atat\xc3\xbcrk Airport was rejected due to the cost involved;<sup id="cite_ref-zaman2012_366-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zaman2012-366">&#91;360&#93;</a></sup> environmental concerns have also been raised with respect to the new airport.<sup id="cite_ref-368" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-368">&#91;362&#93;</a></sup> Currently under construction, the <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0stanbul_New_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="\xc4\xb0stanbul New Airport">new international airport</a> will become the largest airport in the world upon the completion of all four stages of the project, with a capacity to serve 150 million passengers per year.<sup id="cite_ref-dhmi_369-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dhmi-369">&#91;363&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-370" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-370">&#91;364&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-371" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-371">&#91;365&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sister_and_twin_cities">Sister and twin cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Istanbul&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Sister and twin cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_Turkey#Istanbul" title="List of twin towns and sister cities in Turkey">List of twin and sister cities of Istanbul</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Istanbul&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Historic_Areas_of_Istanbul" title="Historic Areas of Istanbul">Historic Areas of Istanbul</a>, a World Heritage Site</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Istanbul&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Where governor\'s office is located.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-city-area-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-city-area_4-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-city-area_4-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-city-area_4-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Sources have provided conflicting figures on the area of Istanbul. The most authoritative source on this figure ought to be the Istanbul Metropolitan Municipality (MMI), but the English version of its website suggests a few figures for this area. One page states that "Each MM is sub-divided into District Municipalities ("DM") <i>of which there are 27 in Istanbul</i>" [emphasis added] with a total area of 1,538.9 square kilometers (594.2&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-mmi-districts_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mmi-districts-97">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> The Municipal History page appears to be the most explicit and most updated, saying that in 2004, "Istanbul Metropolitan Municipality\'s jurisdiction was enlarged to cover all the area within the provincial limits". It also states a 2008 law merged the <a href="/wiki/Emin%C3%B6n%C3%BC" title="Emin\xc3\xb6n\xc3\xbc">Emin\xc3\xb6n\xc3\xbc</a> district into the <a href="/wiki/Fatih" title="Fatih">Fatih</a> district (a point that is not reflected in the previous source) and increased the number of districts in Istanbul to 39.<sup id="cite_ref-mmi-history_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mmi-history-98">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> That total area, as corroborated on the Turkish version of the MMI website,<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> and a Jurisdiction page on the English site<sup id="cite_ref-mmi-jurisdiction_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mmi-jurisdiction-100">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> is 5,343 square kilometers (2,063&#160;sq&#160;mi).</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-byz-date-50"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-byz-date_50-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The foundation of Byzantion (<a href="/wiki/Byzantium" title="Byzantium">Byzantium</a>) is sometimes, especially in encyclopedic or other tertiary sources, placed firmly in 667 BCE. Historians have disputed the precise year the city was founded. Commonly cited is the work of 5th-century-BC historian <a href="/wiki/Herodotus" title="Herodotus">Herodotus</a>, which says the city was founded seventeen years after <a href="/wiki/Chalcedon" title="Chalcedon">Chalcedon</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> which came into existence around 685 BCE. <a href="/wiki/Eusebius" title="Eusebius">Eusebius</a> concurs with 685 BCE as the year Chalcedon was founded, but places Byzantion\'s establishment in 659 BCE.<sup id="cite_ref-isa199_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-isa199-46">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Among more modern historians, Carl Roebuck proposed the 640s BCE<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> and others have suggested even later. The foundation date of Chalcedon is itself subject to some debate; while many sources place it in 685 BC,<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> others put it in 675 BC<sup id="cite_ref-fre10_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fre10-49">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> or even 639 BCE (with Byzantion\'s establishment placed in 619 BCE).<sup id="cite_ref-isa199_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-isa199-46">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Some sources refer to Byzantium\'s foundation as the 7th century BCE.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-pop-figures-70"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-pop-figures_70-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-pop-figures_70-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Historians disagree\xe2\x80\x94sometimes substantially\xe2\x80\x94on population figures of Istanbul (Constantinople), and other world cities, prior to the 20th century. A follow-up to Chandler &amp; Fox 1974,<a href="#CITEREFChandler1987">Chandler 1987</a>, pp.&#160;463\xe2\x80\x93505<sup id="cite_ref-chfo_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chfo-83">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> examines different sources\' estimates and chooses the most likely based on historical conditions; it is the source of most population figures between 100 and 1914. The ranges of values between 500 and 1000 are due to <a href="#CITEREFMorris2010">Morris 2010</a>, which also does a comprehensive analysis of sources, including Chandler (1987); Morris notes that many of Chandler\'s estimates during that time seem too large for the city\'s size, and presents smaller estimates. Chandler disagrees with <a href="#CITEREFTuran2010">Turan 2010</a> on the population of the city in the mid-1920s (with the former suggesting 817,000 in 1925), but Turan, p. 224, is used as the source of population figures between 1924 and 2005. Turan\'s figures, as well as the 2010 figure,<sup id="cite_ref-turkstat-curr_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-turkstat-curr-175">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> come from the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.turkstat.gov.tr/">Turkish Statistical Institute</a>. The drastic increase in population between 1980 and 1985 is largely due to an enlargement of the city\'s limits (see the <a href="#Administration">Administration section</a>). Explanations for population changes in pre-Republic times can be inferred from the <a href="#History">History section</a>.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-un-agg-183"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-un-agg_183-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The United Nations defines an urban agglomeration as "the population contained within the contours of a contiguous territory inhabited at urban density levels without regard to administrative boundaries". The agglomeration "usually incorporates the population in a city or town plus that in the suburban areas lying outside of, but being adjacent to, the city boundaries".<sup id="cite_ref-wup-faq_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wup-faq-181">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wup-pop_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wup-pop-182">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-uefa-category-278"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-uefa-category_278-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">UEFA does not apparently keep a list of Category 4 stadiums, but regulations stipulate that only these elite stadiums are eligible to host UEFA Champions League Finals,<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup> which Atat\xc3\xbcrk Olympic Stadium did in 2005, and UEFA Europa League (formerly UEFA Cup) Finals,<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup> which \xc5\x9e\xc3\xbckr\xc3\xbc Saraco\xc4\x9flu Stadium did in 2009. <a href="/wiki/T%C3%BCrk_Telekom_Arena" class="mw-redirect" title="T\xc3\xbcrk Telekom Arena">T\xc3\xbcrk Telekom Arena</a> is noted as an elite UEFA stadium by its architects.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Istanbul&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 27em;
